DECLARATION OF INVESTIGATOR  
I have read and understood all sections of the protocol entitled “A Phase 3, Randomized, 
Observer-Blind, Placebo-Controlled Study to Evaluate the Efficacy, Safety, and Immunogenicity 
of [AMENDMENT_A101] Cytomegalovirus (CMV) Vaccine in Healthy Participants 16 to 40 Years of 
Age” and the most recent version of the Investigator’s Brochure. 
I agree to supervise all aspects of the protocol and to conduct the clinical investigation in 
accordance with the current protocol, the International Council for Harmonisation (ICH) of 
Technical Requirements for Registration of Pharmaceuticals for Human Use, E6(R2) Good 
Clinical Practice (GCP) Guidance, and all applicable government regulations. I will not make 
changes to the protocol before consulting with [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. or implement protocol changes 
without IRB/IEC approval except to eliminate an immediate risk to participants. 
I agree to administer study treatment only to participants under my personal supervision or the 
supervision of a Subinvestigator. I will not supply study treatment to any person not authorized 
to receive it. I also agree that persons debarred from conducting or working on clinical studies by 
any court or regulatory agency will not be allowed to conduct or work on studies for the Sponsor 
or a partnership in which the Sponsor is involved. I will immediately disclose it in writing to the 
Sponsor if any person who is involved in the study is debarred, or if any proceeding for 
debarment is pending, or, to the best of my knowledge, threatened. 
I will not disclose confidential information contained in this document including participant 
information, to anyone other than the recipient study staffs and members of the IRB/IEC. I agree 
to ensure that this information will not be used for any purpose other than the evaluation or 
conduct of the clinical investigation without the prior written consent from [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
I will not disclose information regarding this clinical investigation or publish results of the 
investigation without authorization from [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
The signature below provides the necessary assurance that this study will be conducted 
according to all stipulations of the protocol, including statements regarding confidentiality, and 
according to local legal and regulatory requirements, US federal regulations, and ICH E6(R2) 
GCP guidelines. 
 
Signature of Principal Investigator 
 
 
Date 
 
 
 
 
 
Printed Name of Principal Investigator

Original Protocol

Amendment 7, 23 Jun 2025: Current Amendment 
Main Rationale for the Amendment: 
This amendment is substantial. The following are the main rationales for the amendment: 
• 
A new secondary efficacy objective and endpoint were added as follows:  
− Secondary Efficacy Objective: To demonstrate the efficacy of [AMENDMENT_A101] to 
prevent systemic viral dissemination in participants who meet the endpoint of 
CMV seroconversion. 
− Secondary Efficacy Endpoint: Systemic viral dissemination defined as 
seroconversion as described in the primary efficacy endpoint AND meeting one 
of the following PCR criteria during the post-seroconversion period: 
a. Positive CMV PCR results in both blood and urine (concurrently or at 
different timepoints)  
OR  
b. Positive CMV PCR results in urine at ≥2 timepoints 
This change was implemented to provide an additional assessment of vaccine 
efficacy as measured by the prevention of systemic viral dissemination in the setting 
of CMV seroconversion as evidence of vaccine-associated enhanced virologic 
control, permitting a more comprehensive understanding of vaccine efficacy. 
• 
A component of the exploratory objective, to assess the effect of [AMENDMENT_A101] on the 
frequency of urinary CMV shedding after seroconversion, has been elevated to a 
secondary efficacy objective. Evaluating the vaccine’s impact on CMV urinary 
shedding over time may yield important insights into the vaccine’s efficacy. Elevating 
this endpoint underscores the significance of these data in determining the vaccine’s 
clinical benefit. 


--- Page 5 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 5 
• 
The [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301-EXT substudy was amended to expand eligibility to include 
participants who met the endpoint of CMV seroconversion during the main study and 
to include the following additional objectives and endpoints in the Extension 
Substudy: 
− Primary Objective: To assess for systemic viral dissemination in participants who 
meet the endpoint of CMV seroconversion during the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 EXT 
substudy. 
− Primary Endpoint: Systemic viral dissemination, defined as seroconversion from a 
negative to a positive result for serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] AND meeting one of the following 
PCR criteria during the post-seroconversion period: 
a. Positive CMV PCR results in both blood and urine (concurrently or at 
different timepoints) 
OR  
b. Positive CMV PCR results in urine at ≥2 timepoints 
− Secondary Objective: To evaluate the efficacy of [AMENDMENT_A101] to reduce the 
frequency of urinary CMV shedding in CMV-seronegative participants meeting 
the endpoint of seroconversion due to primary CMV infection. 
− Secondary Endpoint: CMV PCR results in urine at each post-seroconversion 
timepoint and during the entire post-seroconversion period. 
The addition of these endpoints to the Extension Substudy will allow for the longer-
term follow up of the new secondary efficacy objective of systemic viral 
dissemination in the setting of CMV seroconversion from the main study as well as 
allow for the longer-term follow up of CMV shedding in the urine of participants 
who seroconverted due to primary CMV infection. 
The summary of changes table outlines the revisions made in Amendment 7 relative to 
Amendment 6, including the modified sections and the corresponding rationales for each 
description. Minor editorial or formatting changes are not included in the summary of changes 
table.

Confidential 
Page 22 
1. 
PROTOCOL SUMMARY  
1.1. 
Synopsis  
Name of Sponsor/Company: [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
Name of Investigational Product: [AMENDMENT_A101] 
Protocol Title: A Phase 3, Randomized, Observer-Blind, Placebo-Controlled Study to Evaluate 
the Efficacy, Safety, and Immunogenicity of [AMENDMENT_A101] Cytomegalovirus (CMV) Vaccine in 
Healthy Participants 16 to 40 Years of Age 
Protocol Number: [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 
Study Period (Years): Approximately 4.5 Years 
Phase of Development: Phase 3 
Total Number of Sites: Approximately 300 
Objectives and Endpoints 
Primary Objectives 
Primary Endpoints 
Primary Efficacy Objective 
Primary Efficacy Endpoint 
• 
To demonstrate the efficacy of [AMENDMENT_A101] 
vaccine to prevent primary CMV infection 
in CMV-seronegative female participants. 
• 
Primary CMV infection, defined as 
seroconversion from a negative to a positive 
result for serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] as measured by a 
platform-based automated immunoassay 
based on at least 1 of the 4 recombinant CMV 
antigens not encoded by [AMENDMENT_A101] (pp150, 
pp28, pp52, pp38) assessed starting 28 days 
after the third injection. 
Primary Safety Objective 
Primary Safety Endpoint 
• 
To evaluate the safety and reactogenicity of 
[AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine when administered on 
a 3-dose injection schedule in all 
participants. 
• 
Solicited ARs through 7 days after each 
injection, unsolicited AEs through 28 days 
after each injection, MAAEs from Day 1 
through 6 months after the last injection, 
AESIs from Day 1 through EoS, and SAEs 
from time of consent through EoS. 
Secondary Immunogenicity and Efficacy 
Objectives 
Secondary Immunogenicity and Efficacy 
Endpoints 
• 
To evaluate the immunogenicity to mRNA-
1647 when administered on a 3-dose 
injection schedule in all participants. 
• 
Antigen-specific nAb and binding antibody 
GMTs or GMCs on Day 1, Month 3, 
Month 7, and Month 12. 


--- Page 23 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 23 
• 
To evaluate persistence of immunogenicity 
to [AMENDMENT_A101] through 24 months after the 
third injection in all participants. 
• 
Antigen-specific nAb and binding antibody 
GMTs or GMCs on Month 18, Month 24, and 
Month 30. 
• 
To demonstrate the efficacy of [AMENDMENT_A101] 
to prevent systemic viral dissemination in 
participants who meet the endpoint of CMV 
seroconversion. 
• 
Systemic viral dissemination defined as 
seroconversion as described in the primary 
efficacy endpoint AND meeting one of the 
following PCR criteria during the 
post-seroconversion period:  
a) Positive CMV PCR results in both blood 
and urine (concurrently or at different 
timepoints) OR 
b) Positive CMV PCR results in urine at 
≥2 timepoints 
• 
To evaluate the efficacy of [AMENDMENT_A101] to 
reduce the frequency of urinary CMV 
shedding in CMV-seronegative participants 
meeting the endpoint of seroconversion due 
to primary CMV infection. 
• 
CMV PCR results in urine at each 
post-seroconversion timepoint and during the 
entire post-seroconversion period. 
Exploratory 
• 
To evaluate the effect of [AMENDMENT_A101] on CMV infection kinetics in CMV-seronegative 
participants meeting the endpoint of seroconversion due to primary CMV infection as measured 
by CMV PCR of blood, urine, and saliva. 
• 
To evaluate the effect of [AMENDMENT_A101] on the frequency and level of urinary CMV shedding in 
CMV-seropositive participants. 
• 
In CMV-seronegative participants receiving [AMENDMENT_A101], to evaluate levels of antigen-specific 
nAb and binding antibodies in participants meeting the endpoint of seroconversion due to 
primary CMV infection and participants not meeting the endpoint of seroconversion due to 
primary CMV infection. 
• 
To evaluate the effect of [AMENDMENT_A101] on incidence of symptomatic primary CMV infection in 
CMV-seronegative participants. 
• 
To evaluate immune markers after receipt of [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine as correlates of risk for 
primary CMV infection in CMV-seronegative participants. 
• 
To describe the effect of [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine to prevent primary CMV infection in 
CMV-seronegative participants who received 2 doses of a 3-dose regimen. 
• 
To evaluate the impact of symptomatic primary CMV infection on participant-reported health 
state and health-related productivity in CMV-seronegative participants. 
Abbreviations: AE = adverse event; AESI = adverse event of special interest; AR = adverse reaction; 
CMV = cytomegalovirus; EoS = end-of-study; GMC = geometric mean concentration; GMT = geometric 
mean titer; [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] = Immunoglobulin G; MAAE = medically attended adverse event; mRNA = messenger 
ribonucleic acid; nAb = neutralizing antibody; PCR = polymerase chain reaction; SAE = serious adverse 
event. 
Overall Study Design 
This is a Phase 3, randomized, observer-blinded, placebo-controlled study in healthy 
participants 16 to 40 years of age. 


--- Page 24 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 24 
The primary efficacy objective is to demonstrate vaccine effect of [AMENDMENT_A101] against primary 
CMV infection in female participants who are CMV-seronegative at enrollment. Primary CMV 
infection is defined as seroconversion from a negative result (baseline/Day 1) to a positive 
result for serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] against CMV as measured by a platform-based automated immunoassay 
based on at least 1 of the 4 recombinant CMV antigens not encoded by [AMENDMENT_A101] (pp150, 
pp28, pp52, pp38) assessed starting 28 days after the third injection and confirmed by a repeat 
[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion.  
Participants who are CMV-seropositive at baseline will not be included in the primary efficacy 
analysis. 
Approximately 6,900 total participants will be enrolled in the study: 
• 
CMV-seronegative cohort: 5,500 female participants 
• 
CMV-seropositive cohort: 1,400 female participants 
Participants will be randomly assigned in a 1:1 ratio to receive either 100 µg [AMENDMENT_A101] or 
placebo. Randomization will be in a blinded manner using a centralized IRT at the Day 1 visit, 
in accordance with pregenerated randomization schedules. For each serostatus cohort 
(CMV-seronegative, CMV-seropositive), randomization will be stratified by age (≥16 to 
<18 years, ≥18 to <20 years, and ≥20 to ≤40 years) to balance treatment assignments. At least 
400 enrolled CMV-seronegative female participants will be in the ≥16 to <18 age group. At 
least 400 female participants will be enrolled in Japan (including approximately 
320 CMV-seronegative and 80 CMV-seropositive female participants, respectively). Each 
participant will participate in 2 phases: Vaccination Period (Screening to Month 7 [Day 197; 
28 days following the third injection]) and a Follow-up Period (post Month 7 [Day 198]) 
through Month 30 (Day 887; approximately 24 months after the third injection). Upon 
completing the Vaccination Period, participants will have scheduled study visits approximately 
every 3 months during the Follow-up Period for safety and study assessments. 
All participants will receive the first injection on Day 1 and will receive the same treatment for 
the second injection at Month 2 (Day 57) and the third injection at Month 6 (Day 169). 
Participants will have approximately 14 study visits and approximately 21 safety telephone 
calls/eDiary safety and surveillance prompts over the course of the study. During the 
Vaccination Period, local and systemic solicited ARs will be collected through 7 days following 
each injection using an eDiary. Any solicited AR that is ongoing beyond Day 7 will be recorded 
until no longer reported, not exceeding 28 days. Unsolicited AEs will be collected starting the 
day of each injection and through 28 days following each injection. MAAEs will be collected 
starting on Day 1 and through 6 months after the last injection. SAEs will be collected from 
time of consent through EoS. Deaths, AESIs, and AEs leading to withdrawal from further 
injections or from study participation will be collected through EoS. Pregnancy and pregnancy 
outcome data will be collected in all participants who become pregnant during the study from 
Day 1 to EoS, including spontaneous and voluntary terminations and congenital abnormalities. 
Pregnancy and pregnancy outcome data may be collected beyond EoS (ie, for pregnancies 
continuing beyond EoS Visit). 
Participants will have scheduled blood samplings over the course of the study to assess 
eligibility, seroconversion due to primary CMV infection (CMV-seronegative cohort), 
vaccine-induced antibody responses, and antibody persistence. 


--- Page 25 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 25 
The study is observer-blind where only delegated unblinded study personnel responsible for 
study injection preparation, administration, and/or accountability will have access to study 
treatment assignments. Neither the participant nor participant’s parent(s)/LAR(s) nor the 
Investigator nor study site staff responsible for study assessments/safety will have access to the 
treatment assignment during the conduct of the study. The Investigator may unblind in the event 
of an emergency. 
Participants may experience AEs that necessitate an unscheduled visit or may be identified 
during scheduled study visits; these AEs will be recorded as MAAEs. There may also be 
situations in which the Investigator asks a participant to return for a visit following the report of 
an AE. Additional examinations may be conducted at these visits as necessary to ensure the 
safety and well-being of participants during the study. Electronic case report forms should be 
completed for each visit. 
All participants will be followed for safety for a minimum of 30 months (24 months after the 
third injection), for seroconversion due to primary CMV infection (CMV-seronegative cohort), 
CMV shedding (CMV-seropositive participants and CMV-seronegative participants meeting the 
endpoint of seroconversion), pregnancy outcomes, and SAEs through to EoS and MAAEs for 
6 months after the last injection. 
Participants who discontinue from further vaccinations after either the first or second 
vaccination but do not withdraw consent will be followed for safety as noted above and will 
provide blood samples for immunogenicity and seroconversion due to primary CMV infection 
(CMV-seronegative cohort) and urine samples for CMV shedding (CMV-seropositive 
participants and CMV-seronegative participants meeting the endpoint of seroconversion). 
Cytomegalovirus-Seronegative Cohort: 
Cytomegalovirus-seronegative cohort participants will provide blood samples for assessment of 
seroconversion due to primary CMV infection and, for female participants of childbearing 
potential, urine samples for pregnancy testing at the following study visits: Day 1, Month 2 
(Day 57), Month 3 (Day 85), Month 6 (Day 169), Month 7 (Day 197), Month 10 (Day 287), 
Month 12 (Day 347), Month 15 (Day 437), Month 18 (Day 527), Month 21 (Day 617), 
Month 24 (Day 707), Month 27 (Day 797), and Month 30 (Day 887, EoS). 
Participants meeting the endpoint of seroconversion due to primary CMV infection from 
Month 3 through EoS will be contacted to be seen for an unscheduled study visit 
(Seroconversion Visit) for clinical assessment including blood, urine, and saliva sampling for 
CMV PCR, after which they will return to the planned visit schedule. At each scheduled visit 
after the Seroconversion Visit through the EoS, urine will be collected for CMV PCR and 
serum will no longer be collected for CMV serology, with the exception of Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] 
testing. Participants who seroconvert prior to Month 3 will not require a Seroconversion Visit 
and will no longer be required to have serum collected for CMV serology at subsequent planned 
visits, with the exception of Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing, and will have urine collected for CMV 
PCR. Participants who seroconvert at the EoS Visit (Visit 31) will be asked to return to the 
clinic as soon as possible for a Seroconversion Visit (unscheduled visit) and will be asked to 
return ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion (unscheduled visit) for Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] 
testing and urine collection. 


--- Page 26 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 26 
In the CMV-seronegative cohort, it is anticipated that the majority of seroconversions due to 
primary CMV infection will be asymptomatic and will be detected by planned serological 
surveillance testing at scheduled study visits. Participants will be assessed for symptoms 
meeting criteria for possible symptomatic primary CMV infection by protocol-defined criteria 
at scheduled study visits starting at Month 3, safety telephone calls, and via eDiary safety 
surveillance prompts (beginning at Month 8). Participants meeting protocol-defined criteria for 
possible symptomatic primary CMV infection between scheduled study visits, during safety 
telephone calls, or via eDiary during the Follow-up Period will be instructed to return to the 
study site for a CMV Illness Assessment Visit (unscheduled visit). The CMV Illness 
Assessment Visit will include physical examination (including vital signs); collection of blood 
samples for hematology, chemistry, seroconversion due to primary CMV infection, and EBV 
panel; and a urine sample for CMV PCR. At the discretion of the Investigator, testing for HIV 
antibodies, HIV viral load, and SARS-CoV-2 may be performed. In addition, participants 
reporting symptoms for possible symptomatic primary CMV infection by protocol-defined 
criteria may also receive electronic-patient-reported outcomes (ePRO) questionnaires to collect 
health status and health-related productivity information as reported by the participant. The 
questionnaires include the EuroQol-5 Dimension 5 Level (EQ-5D-5L) and the Health-Related 
Productivity Questionnaire (HRPQ), which is tr[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]ered based on potential symptomatic primary 
CMV illness symptoms. 
Cytomegalovirus-Seropositive Cohort: 
Cytomegalovirus-seropositive cohort participants will have urine sampling for CMV shedding 
and, for female participants of childbearing potential, urine pregnancy testing at the following 
study visits: Day 1, Month 2 (Day 57), Month 3 (Day 85), Month 6 (Day 169), Month 7 
(Day 197), Month 10 (Day 287), Month 12 (Day 347), Month 15 (Day 437), Month 18 
(Day 527), Month 21 (Day 617), Month 24 (Day 707), Month 27 (Day 797), and Month 30 
(Day 887, EoS). 
Safety Oversight: 
Internal Safety Team 
A blinded IST composed of the CRO medical monitor, Sponsor clinical development lead, and 
Sponsor safety physician, will provide primary safety oversight at defined intervals throughout 
the study. Details regarding composition, responsibilities, and procedures of the IST will be 
presented in the IST charter. 
Data Safety Monitoring Board: 
Scheduled meetings of the independent DSMB will occur at the following timepoints in the 
study as detailed in the DSMB Charter: 
• 
After the first 600 participants have been enrolled and have completed Day 29 
(28 days after first injection) follow-up to review unblinded study safety data and 
make recommendations to the Sponsor regarding ongoing enrollment. 
• 
At specified enrollment milestones to review unblinded study safety data including 
pregnancy and pregnancy outcomes and make recommendations to the Sponsor 
regarding study conduct. 


--- Page 27 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 27 
• 
At the release of the Primary Analysis and to make recommendations to the Sponsor 
regarding study conduct based on the prespecified criteria for early efficacy. 
The DSMB may make the following recommendations to the Sponsor (as appropriate): 
• 
Continue enrollment as planned after the initial 600 participants have been enrolled. 
• 
Continue enrollment and/or study conduct as planned. 
• 
Pause enrollment and/or dosing due to a safety concern. 
• 
Stop further enrollment due to overwhelming VE. 
The Sponsor may also request that the DSMB convene on an ad hoc basis to review any safety 
concerns brought to the DSMB by the safety review team, to review any safety data from this 
study, or review other data including new nonclinical or clinical information related to 
[AMENDMENT_A101] external to this study. The DSMB composition, its remit, and frequency of data 
review will be further defined in the DSMB Charter. 
Adjudication Committee: 
An independent AC blinded to treatment assignments will be assembled to confirm that criteria 
for symptomatic seroconversion due to primary CMV infection have been met in cases that 
have been identified as symptomatic primary CMV infection. 
The AC composition, its remit, and frequency of data review will be further defined in the AC 
charter. 
Independent Cardiac Event Adjudication Committee: 
An independent CEAC comprising medically qualified personnel, including cardiologists, will 
review all suspected cases of myocarditis, pericarditis, and myopericarditis to determine if they 
meet CDC criteria for “probable” or “confirmed” events, which are reported in ongoing clinical 
studies per the CEAC charter (Gargano et al 2021). Any cases that the CEAC assesses as 
representing probable or confirmed cases of myocarditis or pericarditis will be referred to the 
Sponsor, who will then determine if additional action is needed. The CEAC will operate under 
the rules of an approved charter that will be written and reviewed at the organizational meeting 
of the CEAC. Details regarding the CEAC composition, responsibilities, procedures, and 
frequency of data review will be defined in the charter. 
Study Duration: Approximately 30 months for each participant in the main study (up to 
54 months total for participants continuing in the Extension Substudy). 
Number of Participants: Approximately 6,900 total participants will be enrolled in the study: 
• 
CMV-seronegative cohort: 5,500 female participants will be enrolled with 
approximately 2,750 participants each exposed to [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine or placebo. 
• 
CMV-seropositive cohort: 1,400 female participants will be enrolled with 
approximately 700 participants each exposed to [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine or placebo.

Study Eligibility Criteria: 
Inclusion Criteria: 
Participants are eligible to be included in the study only if all the following criteria apply (no 
protocol exemptions will be allowed in this study): 
1. Is a female and 16 to 40 years of age, at the time of consent. 
2. According to the assessment of the Investigator, is capable of complying with study 
procedures. 
3. For female participants aged ≥20 years, has or anticipates having direct exposure 
within 7 months after the planned first dose (in the home, socially, or 
occupationally) to at least 1 child ≤5 years of age. Direct exposure is defined as 
either a) participant is the parent, or b) participant has close contact (feeding, diaper 
changes, childcare/supervision) for at least 8 hours per week. 
4. For the CMV-seronegative Cohorts: at the Screening Visit, is CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-negative 
and CMV IgM-negative. 
For CMV-seropositive Cohorts: at the Screening Visit, is CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-positive and 
CMV IgM-negative, or CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-positive and CMV IgM-positive. Participants 
with an isolated positive result for CMV IgM (ie, CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-negative and CMV 
IgM-positive) will not be eligible for enrollment but may be rescreened after at least 
6 weeks from the initial CMV Screening. 
A participant with a CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-positive result and an IgM-indeterminate result at 
Screening will not require the IgM sampling to be repeated in order to consider the 
participant CMV-seropositive. 
5. Participant (and parent/LAR, if applicable) provides written informed 
consent/assent. Participants under the age of majority (ie, under legal age) at the 
time of enrollment must provide written informed consent at the next study visit 
once turning the age of majority. 
6. Investigator assessment confirms that the participant (including in the case of an 
emancipated minor), or parent(s)/LAR(s), as applicable, understands and is willing 
and physically able to comply with protocol-mandated follow-up including all study 
visits and procedures anticipated during the 30-month Study Period. 
7. This criterion has been removed in Protocol Amendment 2: Has a body mass index 
of 15 to 35 kg/m2, inclusive. 
8. Female participants of childbearing potential: Urine pregnancy test is negative at 
Screening and negative on the day of the first injection (Day 1). 
Note: urine pregnancy test at Screening or Day 1 is not required for female 
participants of nonchildbearing potential. See Section 11.8 for definition of 
nonchildbearing potential. 
9. Female participants of childbearing potential: If the participant is sexually active 
with men, all of the following criteria must be met:

•

prior to Screening without an alternative medical cause).

assessment of immune response, or adherence to study procedures. Clinically 
unstable is defined as a diagnosis or condition requiring significant changes in 
management or medication within the 2 months prior to Screening and includes

condition. This includes but is not limited to:

intramuscular (IM) injection or phlebotomy. 
• 
Any medical, psychiatric, or occupational condition, including reported history of 
drug or alcohol abuse, that, in the opinion of the Investigator, might pose additional 
risk due to participation in the study or could interfere with the interpretation of 
study results.

Study Treatments: 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
Approximately 3,450 participants (2,750 CMV-seronegative participants and 
700 CMV-seropositive participants) will receive 100 μg of [AMENDMENT_A101] injection on a Day 1, 
Day 57 (Month 2), and Day 169 (Month 6) schedule. 
Placebo 
Approximately 3,450 participants (2,750 CMV-seronegative participants and 
700 CMV-seropositive participants]) receiving 0.5mL of 0.9% sodium chloride injection on a 
Day 1, Day 57 (Month 2), and Day 169 (Month 6) schedule. 
Investigational Product, Dosage, and Mode of Administration: 
The [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine against CMV infection consists of 6 distinct mRNA sequences 
encoding important targets of nAb response to human CMV infection (full length CMV 
glycoprotein B [gB] and pentameric gH/gL/UL128/UL130/UL131A glycoprotein complex 
[pentamer]) in an LNP formulation. 
The LNP formulation includes 4 lipid excipients: SM-102, a proprietary ionizable amino lipid, 
and the commercially available lipids cholesterol, DSPC, and PEG2000-DMG. 


--- Page 31 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 31 
[AMENDMENT_A101] injection is stored at 2ºC to 8ºC until use. Following appropriate dose preparation, 
[AMENDMENT_A101] injection will be administered IM into the deltoid muscle, preferably in the 
nondominant arm, in a volume of 0.5 mL. 
The Phase 3 formulation of [AMENDMENT_A101] will be filled and lyophilized in 2R Type I glass vials 
at a total mRNA content of 151 μg/vial. Prior to use, the lyophilized drug product is 
reconstituted with 0.7 mL of 0.9% sodium chloride injection, a concentration of 0.2 mg/mL for 
administration of the specified dose level of 100 μg in a volume of 0.5 mL. 
A 0.9% sodium chloride injection (normal saline) placebo will be administered IM into the 
deltoid muscle, preferably in the nondominant arm, in a volume of 0.5 mL. 
Assessments and Procedures: 
Efficacy and Exploratory Assessments: 
Cytomegalovirus-Seronegative Cohort: 
Blood sampling for assessment of primary CMV infection will be performed at all study site 
visits throughout the study. On dosing days, blood sampling should be completed prior to study 
injection but after measurement of the pre-dose vital signs. 
An indeterminate result will be repeated ≥2 weeks after the date of the indeterminate result to 
assess for an evolving antibody response to a primary CMV infection. A positive repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] 
result meets criteria for seroconversion due to primary CMV infection once confirmed by a 
positive [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion; a negative Confirmatory 
[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test will be handled on a case-by-case basis. 
Participants in the CMV-seronegative cohort will be informed if antibody testing demonstrates 
seroconversion due to primary CMV infection. Cytomegalovirus PCR results will not be made 
available to participants during the study. Participants will be instructed not to seek CMV 
testing outside of the study and should request any additional CMV testing through the Study 
Investigator. 
Seronegative participants reporting symptoms meeting criteria for possible primary CMV 
infection at or after the Month 3 study visit will be asked to return to the study clinic for an 
unscheduled CMV Illness Assessment Visit. This visit will include a physical examination; 
collection of blood samples for hematology, chemistry, seroconversion due to primary CMV 
infection, and EBV panel; and a urine sample for CMV PCR. At the discretion of the 
Investigator, testing for HIV antibodies, HIV viral load, and/or SARS-CoV-2 may be 
performed. Clinical criteria for possible symptomatic primary CMV infection are an illness 
reported by the participant consisting of at least 2 of the following symptoms: fever 
≥38°C/100.4°F, myalgia, moderate to severe fatigue, sore throat/pharyngitis, or cervical 
lymphadenopathy in the absence of respiratory symptoms (eg, nasal congestion, runny nose, 
cough). A participant meeting clinical criteria for possible symptomatic primary CMV infection 
with a positive test for seroconversion due to primary CMV infection documented within 
6 months after symptom onset meets criteria for symptomatic primary CMV infection. 
If a CMV-seronegative participant has previously seroconverted due to primary CMV infection 
prior to reporting symptoms meeting criteria for possible symptomatic primary CMV infection, 
a CMV Illness Assessment Visit is not required.

Cytomegalovirus-Seronegative Cohort and Cytomegalovirus-Seropositive Cohort: 
Immunogenicity Assessments: 
• 
Serum functional antibody levels against vaccine antigens as measured by nAb titer 
against epithelial cell infection and nAb titer against fibroblast infection. 
• 
Serum binding antibody titers against vaccine antigens as measured by ELISA 
specific to the gB and pentamer proteins. 
Safety Assessments: 
Safety assessments will include monitoring and recording of the following for each participant: 
• 
Solicited local and systemic ARs that occur during the 7 days following each 
injection (ie, the day of injection and 6 subsequent days). Any solicited AR that is 
ongoing beyond Day 7 will be recorded until no longer reported, not exceeding 
28 days. Solicited ARs will be recorded daily using eDiaries. 
− Solicited local ARs include injection site pain, injection site erythema [redness], 
injection site swelling/induration [hardness], and localized axillary swelling or 
tenderness ipsilateral to the vaccination arm. 
− Solicited systemic ARs include headache, fatigue, myalgia (muscle aches all 
over the body), arthralgia (aching in several joints), nausea/vomiting, fever, and 
chills. 
• 
Beginning at Month 8, participants will receive safety eDiary prompts at timepoints 
specified in the SoA. Safety eDiary will prompt the participant to report occurrence 
of relevant safety events. If eDiary prompt results in identification of a relevant 
safety event, trained study site personnel will call the participant within 1 business 
day, or within 2 business days after the window for eDiary completion has closed if 
the participant did not complete the eDiary, to collect information relating to 
MAAEs (up to 6 months after the last injection), AESIs, AEs leading to withdrawal, 
SAEs, and information on concomitant medications associated with those events. 
For the CMV-seronegative cohort only, safety eDiary will also prompt the 
participant to report symptoms that may be consistent with symptomatic CMV. For 
CMV-seronegative participants who have not seroconverted due to primary CMV 
infection, site personnel will review symptoms reported in the safety eDiary and 
determine whether a CMV Illness Assessment Visit is required. 
• 
Unsolicited AEs observed or reported starting on Day 1 and during the 28 days 
following each injection (ie, the first day of each injection and 27 subsequent days). 
• 
AEs leading to discontinuation from dosing and/or study participation from Day 1 
through Month 30 (Day 887) or withdrawal from the study.

AESIs from Day 1 through Month 30 (Day 887) or withdrawal from the study.

Vital sign measurements.

Statistical Methods: 
The overall Type I error rate for this study is strictly controlled at 2.5% (one-sided) with 0.5% 
allocated to the Primary Analysis and 2.0% allocated to the Final Analysis for testing the null 
hypothesis for the primary efficacy endpoint (H0). Statistical significance of the primary 
efficacy endpoint can be achieved either at the Primary Analysis or at the Final Analysis. 
No formal multiple comparison adjustments will be employed for multiple safety endpoints or 
multiple efficacy endpoints.

Immunogenicity Subset 
Immunogenicity tests will be run on a subset of participants in the FAS.

The Solicited Safety Set consists of all randomized participants who

Abbreviations: AR = adverse reaction; CMV = cytomegalovirus; FAS = full analysis set; 
[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] = Immunoglobulin G; mITT = modified intent-to-treat. 
Efficacy Analysis: 
The primary efficacy endpoint is primary CMV infection. A primary efficacy endpoint (ie, 
primary CMV infection) case is defined as seroconversion from a negative to a positive result 
for serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] as measured by a platform-based automated immunoassay based on at least 1 of 
4 recombinant CMV antigens not encoded by [AMENDMENT_A101] (pp150, pp28, pp52, pp38) and 
confirmed by a repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion. The 
primary analysis will be conducted in the PP Set with cases counted starting 28 days after the 
third injection. Seronegative female participants who have received the full 3-dose injection 
schedule with primary CMV infections occurring from Month 7 (Day 197) through the EoS will 
contribute to case accrual. 
VE is defined as the percent reduction in the hazard of the primary endpoint (mRNA‑1647 vs. 
placebo). The VE will be estimated using 1 minus the hazard ratio (HR) ([AMENDMENT_A101] vs. 
placebo) estimand. A stratified Cox proportional hazard model will be used to assess the 
magnitude of the treatment group difference (ie, hazard ratio) between [AMENDMENT_A101] versus 
placebo. The hazard ratio and its alpha-adjusted CI from the stratified Cox model with Efron’s 
method of tie handling and with injection group as covariate will be reported. 
The PP Set will be the primary analysis population for all efficacy endpoints unless otherwise 
specified. Supportive analyses of efficacy using the mITT Set will also be carried out. 
Sensitivity analyses will also be performed to assess VE in participants who have not received 
all 3 dose injections per schedule. 
For the planned analyses, cases will be counted starting at 1 month (28 days) after the third 
injection. Sensitivity analyses will be performed with cases counted starting from the third 


--- Page 35 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 35 
injection, from 1 month (28 days) after the second injection, from the second injection, from the 
first injection, and after randomization, respectively. 
In addition, VE will be estimated based on the incidence rate of primary CMV infection in each 
group, defined as (1 – relative risk), where relative risk is the incidence rate of the primary 
CMV infection in participants in the [AMENDMENT_A101] arm relative to that of the placebo arm 
([AMENDMENT_A101]/placebo). The 2-sided 95% CI of VE will be provided using the exact method 
conditional upon the total number of cases. 
A secondary efficacy endpoint (ie, systemic viral dissemination) case is defined as: 
• seroconversion from a negative to a positive result for serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] as measured by a 
platform-based automated immunoassay based on at least 1 of the 4 recombinant CMV 
antigens not encoded by [AMENDMENT_A101] (pp150, pp28, pp52, pp38) and confirmed by a 
repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion, AND  
• positive CMV PCR results in both blood and urine (on the same date or on different 
dates) or in urine (on ≥2 different dates) on or after the date of seroconversion. 
This secondary efficacy endpoint will be analyzed using methods similar to those for the 
primary efficacy endpoint. VE and the corresponding nominal 2-sided 95% CI will be provided. 
Immunogenicity Analysis: 
Immunogenicity endpoints include nAb against epithelial cell infection, nAb against fibroblast 
infection, pentamer-specific binding antibody, and gB-specific binding antibody. 
Immunogenicity endpoints will be analyzed by serostatus (CMV-seronegative, 
CMV-seropositive) and treatment group using the Immunogenicity PP Subset, unless otherwise 
specified. The SAP will describe the complete set of Immunogenicity analyses, including the 
approach to sample individuals into an Immunogenicity Subset for characterizing [AMENDMENT_A101]–
induced immunogenicity. 
Neutralizing antibody and binding antibody data will be summarized for each cohort and 
treatment group using GMT or GMC with corresponding 95% CI at each timepoint for which 
an assessment is performed, and GMFR with corresponding 95% CI at each postbaseline 
timepoint over preinjection baseline at Day 1 will be provided by study arm. Descriptive 
summary statistics including median, minimum, and maximum will also be provided. 
The number and percentage of participants with fold rise ≥2, ≥3, and ≥4 of vaccine-induced 
antibody titers and CMV-seronegative cohort participants with seroconversion to vaccine 
antigens from baseline will be provided with 2-sided 95% CI using the Clopper-Pearson method 
at each postbaseline timepoint for all assays. At a participant level, seroconversion to vaccine 
antigens from baseline is defined as a change in antigen-specific nAb or binding antibody titer 
from below the LLOQ to equal to or above the LLOQ. 
A restricted maximum likelihood-based MMRM will be used to estimate the treatment effect 
between [AMENDMENT_A101] versus placebo. The model will include all available log-transformed 
antibody titers at each postbaseline visit as the dependent variable, treatment groups, visit (as a 
class variable), and interaction of treatment group and visit as fixed effects, and participant as a 
random effect. An unstructured covariance structure will be used to model the within-
participant errors. If the model fails to converge, a compound symmetry covariance structure 
will be considered. The degrees of freedom of the denominator will be approximated by the 


--- Page 36 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 36 
Kenward-Roger method. The GLSM and corresponding 2-sided 95% CI for the antibody titers 
for each treatment group will be provided for each scheduled visit. The GLSM and 
corresponding 95% CI results in log-transformed scale estimated from the model will be back-
transformed to obtain these estimates in the original scale. 
In addition, GMR, estimated by the ratio of GLSM and the corresponding 2-sided 95% CI, will 
be provided to assess the treatment difference between [AMENDMENT_A101] group versus placebo 
group at each visit. The analysis may adjust for the stratification factor, ie, the stratification 
factor may be included in the MMRM as a fixed effect. 
Safety Analysis: 
Safety analysis will be performed for the overall study population as well as separately for the 
CMV-seronegative and the CMV-seropositive participants. 
Safety endpoints include solicited local and systemic ARs collected through 7 days following 
each injection, unsolicited AEs collected through 28 days following each injection, MAAEs 
collected from Day 1 through 6 months after the last injection, AESIs collected from Day 1 
through EoS, and SAEs collected from time of consent through EoS. Pregnancy and pregnancy 
outcome data in participants becoming pregnant throughout the course of the study will also be 
collected. Solicited ARs and unsolicited AEs, including MAAEs, AESIs, and SAEs, will be 
coded by system organ class and preferred term according to the MedDRA. Severity of solicited 
ARs will be graded according to the grading scales modified from the Toxicity Grading Scale 
for Healthy Adult and Adolescent Volunteers Enrolled in Preventive Vaccine Clinical Trials. 
All safety analyses will be based on the Safety Set, except summaries of solicited ARs which 
will be based on the Solicited Safety Set. Participants will be analyzed according to actual 
treatment received ([AMENDMENT_A101] or placebo). All safety analyses will be provided by treatment 
group, unless otherwise specified, with the number and percentage of participants experiencing 
at least 1 event. 
The number and percentage of participants with any solicited local AR and with any solicited 
systemic AR during the 7-day Follow-up Period after each injection will be provided. A 2-sided 
95% exact CI using the Clopper-Pearson method will be also provided for the percentage of 
participants for all safety endpoints. 
Number and percentage of participants with unsolicited AEs, SAEs, MAAEs, Grade 3 or higher 
ARs and severe AEs, AESIs, AEs leading to discontinuation from study or withdrawal of 
participation in the study, deaths, and pregnancy and outcome data will be summarized. 
Number of events of solicited ARs, unsolicited AEs/SAEs, and MAAEs will be reported in 
summarization tables accordingly. 
For all other safety parameters, descriptive summary statistics will be provided. Further details 
will be described in the SAP. 
Sample Size Justification: 
The study originally planned to enroll approximately 6,900 female participants outside Japan 
(5,500 CMV-seronegative and 1,400 CMV-seropositive). In Protocol Amendment 2, 
approximately 400 female participants (320 CMV-seronegative and 80 CMV-seropositive) 
were added in Japan, resulting in a total sample size of approximately 7,300 female participants 
(5,820 CMV-seronegative and 1,480 CMV-seropositive). As this sample size update occurred 


--- Page 37 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 37 
prior to the first planned analysis without unblinding the study, no adjustment to the alpha 
levels of the planned analyses is needed. 
At the time of preparing Protocol Amendment 2, it was anticipated that, by the time enrollment 
in Japan started, enrollment outside Japan would have been completed. Therefore, 
approximately 400 participants in Japan were added beyond the originally planned total sample 
size to ensure an adequate number of participants would be enrolled in Japan. Since Protocol 
Amendment 2 became effective, enrollment in Japan started earlier than anticipated and overall 
enrollment outside Japan was slower than anticipated. As a result, in Protocol Amendment 3, 
the sample size is reduced back to the originally planned total of approximately 6,900 female 
participants (5,500 CMV-seronegative and 1,400 CMV-seropositive), with at least 400 
participants in Japan now a part of this planned total. Similar as in Protocol Amendment 2, 
given this sample size update occurred prior to the first planned analysis without unblinding the 
study, no adjustment to the alpha levels of the planned analyses is needed. In addition, this is a 
case-driven study in which the statistical power to address the primary efficacy objective in 
CMV-seronegative female participants depends directly on the number of primary infection 
cases observed at the time of the planned inferential analyses; as detailed below, this sample 
size will still provide at least 90% power at either planned inferential analysis. 
Power and Sample Size for the Cytomegalovirus-Seronegative Cohort 
The primary efficacy objective is to demonstrate VE in CMV-seronegative female participants. 
The sample size of the CMV-seronegative female cohort is driven by the total number of cases 
meeting the primary efficacy endpoint of primary CMV infection to demonstrate [AMENDMENT_A101] 
VE versus placebo in participants who are CMV-seronegative at baseline. The study will 
randomly assign approximately 5,500 CMV-seronegative female participants in 1:1 ratio to 
[AMENDMENT_A101] and placebo in the CMV-seronegative female cohort. The sample size calculation 
focuses on having 90% power demonstrating VE of [AMENDMENT_A101] versus placebo by rejecting 
the null hypothesis H0: VE ≤25% at the Primary Analysis and is based on the following 
assumptions: 
1. The underlying VE is 70%, 
2. The 12-months incidence rate on placebo is 1.5%, 
3. An enrollment period of 26 months, 
4. The primary analysis population for efficacy is PP Set, and a yearly loss of evaluable 
participants of 10% (to be excluded from the PP analysis), and 
5. Participants are at risk for primary CMV infection starting 1 month after the third 
injection. 
There are 2 planned inferential analyses of efficacy in this study: the Primary Analysis and the 
Final Analysis. The overall Type I error rate for this study is strictly controlled at 2.5% 
(one-sided) with 0.5% allocated to the Primary Analysis and 2.0% allocated to the Final 
Analysis for testing the null hypothesis for the primary efficacy endpoint (H0). 
The Primary Analysis will be carried out when: 


--- Page 38 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 38 
1. A total of 81 cases of the primary efficacy endpoint (ie, primary CMV infection) have 
been observed across the 2 groups in the PP Set in the CMV-seronegative female 
participants, and 
2. The median follow-up time of CMV-seronegative female participants is at least 
12 months after the third injection. 
A total of 81 primary infection cases at the Primary Analysis will provide 90% power to detect 
a VE of 70% (70% reduction in the hazard rate), rejecting the null hypothesis of H0: VE ≤25%, 
at a (one-sided) Type I error rate of 0.5%. 
If VE is demonstrated at the Primary Analysis (ie, one-sided p-value for testing the null 
hypothesis of H0: VE ≤25% is less than 0.005), there will be no further Type I error-controlled 
inferential analysis of the primary efficacy endpoint. All further/subsequent analyses of the 
primary efficacy endpoint will be considered descriptive or supportive in nature. In the situation 
that VE is demonstrated at the Primary Analysis, a Final Analysis after at least 112 primary 
efficacy endpoint cases have been observed across the 2 groups in the PP Set for Efficacy may 
be performed as a supportive analysis of the primary efficacy endpoint with longer follow-up 
time. 
In the event that VE is not demonstrated at the Primary Analysis (ie, one-sided p-value for 
testing the null hypothesis of H0: VE ≤25% is at or above 0.005), the Final Analysis will be 
carried out as an inferential analysis of efficacy when at least a total of 112 cases of the primary 
efficacy endpoint (ie, primary CMV infection) have been observed across the 2 groups in the PP 
Set for Efficacy. A total of 112 primary infection cases at the Final Analysis will provide >90% 
and approximately 90% power to detect a VE of 70% and 60%, respectively, rejecting the null 
hypothesis of H0: VE ≤25%, at a (one-sided) Type I error rate of 2.0%. 
The calculation is carried out using R package gsDesign. The total number of cases pertains to 
the PP Set with case accrual beginning at Month 7 when serum sample for 
efficacy/immunogenicity assessment is planned 1 month after the third injection. 
Power and Sample Size for the Cytomegalovirus-Seropositive Participants 
Sample size of CMV-seropositive participants is driven by safety. Approximately 
1,400 CMV-seropositive female participants will be randomly assigned in a 1:1 ratio to 
[AMENDMENT_A101] and placebo. With 700 CMV-seropositive participants exposed to mRNA‑1647, 
the study has at least 90% probability to observe at least 1 CMV-seropositive participant with 
an AE at a true 0.35% AE rate. 
Planned Inferential Analyses: 
There are 2 planned inferential analyses of efficacy in this study: the Primary Analysis and the 
Final Analysis. The study will be considered to achieve its primary efficacy objective if VE for 
the primary efficacy endpoint is demonstrated at either planned inferential analysis.

2.
INTRODUCTION
2.1. 
Study Rationale 
The purpose of this Phase 3 study is to evaluate the VE against primary CMV infection in 
healthy CMV-seronegative women 16 to 40 years of age, and to evaluate the safety, 
reactogenicity, and immunogenicity of [AMENDMENT_A101] in CMV-seronegative and 
CMV-seropositive participants.
2.2. 
Background and Overview 
Cytomegalovirus is a double-stranded DNA herpesvirus that is primarily acquired through 
contact with infectious mucosal secretions or in utero and establishes latency in myeloid cells. 
Cytomegalovirus infection is common, with seroprevalence in adult populations ranging from 
18% to 100% worldwide (Zuhair et al 2019). Though initial (primary) CMV infections in 
children and adults are rarely symptomatic, vertically transmitted in utero CMV infection 
(cCMV infection) can result in significant lifelong disability. 
Regional rates of cCMV infection parallel CMV seroprevalence in the population. The annual 
birth prevalence of cCMV ranges from 0.6% to 0.7% in developed countries to as high as 6% in 
the developing world (Kenneson and Cannon 2007; Lanzieri et al 2014). At highest risk are 
infants born to mothers who acquire a primary CMV infection during pregnancy, with cCMV 
occurring in approximately 1/3 of these newborns (Fowler et al 1992; 
Kenneson and Cannon 2007). Congenital CMV infection can occur in the setting of maternal 
primary CMV infection at any time during pregnancy. 
Maternal primary CMV infection occurring in the weeks prior to conception through the first 
trimester carries the highest risk for severe manifestations of cCMV in the newborn, including 
jaundice, hepatosplenomegaly, hematologic abnormalities, microcephaly, sensorineural hearing 
loss, chorioretinitis, or seizures (Daiminger et al 2005; Faure-Bardon et al 2019; Pass et al 2006). 
Overall, 10% to 15% of infants born to women with primary CMV infection during pregnancy 
are symptomatic at birth, and of these symptomatic infants, 4% to 12% die in their first year of 
life and 70% to 80% survive to suffer lifelong disabilities (Boppana et al 1992; 
Dollard et al 2007; Lopez et al 2014; Manicklal et al 2013; Coppola et al 2019). 
Preexisting maternal immunity to CMV from prior infection is moderately protective against 
cCMV, reducing its risk by 70% to 80% (Fowler et al 1992; Adler et al 1995; Fowler et al 2003). 
Current knowledge of maternal immune and viral predictors of cCMV infection is incomplete 
and studies have focused on specific binding and nAb responses as well as specific T-cell 
responses in the setting of maternal primary CMV infection as well as in the setting of latent 
maternal CMV infection (Itell et al 2017). Maternal reinfection with CMV during pregnancy 
may be a risk factor for cCMV in infants born to CMV-seropositive mothers 
(Boppana et al 2001; Kenneson and Cannon 2007), possibly explaining the observation that 
maternal seropositive status confers only partial protection against cCMV infection 
(Fowler et al 1992; Adler et al 1995; Boppana et al 2001; Yamamoto et al 2010). 
Newborns with cCMV infection may appear well at birth but are at risk for development of 
neurocognitive sequelae such as sensorineural hearing loss and developmental delay in infancy 


--- Page 46 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 46 
and childhood (Fowler et al 1999; Fowler and Boppana 2006; Goderis et al 2014). In both 
symptomatic and asymptomatic newborns, the most common long-term complication of cCMV 
infection is sensorineural hearing loss (Faure-Bardon et al 2019). 
There is no approved modality for the prevention of CMV infection, and it is clear that a safe and 
effective vaccine would have a major public health impact, as reflected by its designation as one 
of the most favorable category (Level I) vaccine targets by the Institute of Medicine 
(Institute of Medicine 2000). 
[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. has developed a proprietary mRNA-based vaccine platform for intramuscular 
(IM) delivery of mRNA encoding target antigens in an LNP formulation. The [AMENDMENT_A101] 
vaccine comprises 6 distinct mRNA sequences encoding 2 key antigens: full length CMV gB and 
pentameric gH/gL/UL128/UL130/UL131A glycoprotein complex (pentamer). The mRNAs are 
endogenously translated into conformationally intact antigens that are recognized by the immune 
system in the same manner as that of a natural CMV infection. 
[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. is conducting a number of studies of [AMENDMENT_A101] as part of the clinical 
development plan. See Section 2.2.2 for additional information. 
The purpose of this Phase 3 study is to evaluate the VE against primary CMV infection in 
healthy CMV-seronegative women 16 to 40 years of age, and to evaluate the safety, 
reactogenicity, and immunogenicity of [AMENDMENT_A101] in CMV-seronegative and 
CMV-seropositive participants. 
2.2.1. 
Nonclinical Studies  
Nonclinical studies conducted in mice and nonhuman primates have demonstrated the 
immunogenicity of [AMENDMENT_A101] in the liquid form and the lyophilized form as measured by 
anti-gB and anti-pentamer [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] titers, and titers of nAb against CMV infection in fibroblasts and 
in epithelial cells. 
A study of [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine in liquid form in Bagg Albino/c mice administered 2 IM 
vaccinations 21 days apart demonstrated robust anti-CMV nAb against fibroblast and epithelial 
cell infection. Similar dose-dependent nAb responses were observed in cynomolgus macaques 
administered 2 vaccinations 21 days apart, with nAb responses that remained above baseline 
through the 201-day duration of the study. 
A study in Bagg Albino/c mice administered 2 IM vaccinations 21 days apart of either 
[AMENDMENT_A101] in liquid form or [AMENDMENT_A101] reconstituted from the lyophilized form showed 
similar dose-dependent increases in anti-gB and anti-pentamer [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] titers. A study in rhesus 
macaques administered 3 IM vaccinations 28 days apart of either [AMENDMENT_A101] in liquid form or 
[AMENDMENT_A101] reconstituted from the lyophilized form showed increases in anti-gB and 
anti-pentamer [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] titers after the second dose that were not appreciably enhanced after the third 
dose, with similar immune responses at all doses and all timepoints for the liquid and lyophilized 
forms of [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine. 
Repeat-dose toxicology studies of [AMENDMENT_A101] performed in Sprague-Dawley rats indicated that 
[AMENDMENT_A101] was clinically well-tolerated. Dose-dependent swelling and skin redness localized 
to the injection site was seen with clinical pathology parameters consistent with a systemic 
inflammatory response to the injection site reaction. 


--- Page 47 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 47 
An in vitro study of SM-102, the custom lipid used in [AMENDMENT_A101], showed no genotoxicity or 
increased mutation frequency. An in vivo micronucleus test using mRNA-1706, an mRNA-based 
vaccine encoding the Zika virus premembrane and envelope polypeptide formulated in SM-102 
containing LNPs and administered intravenously, showed nondose-dependent increases in 
events. 
Developmental and reproductive toxicity has been assessed in a non-GLP embryo-fetal dose 
range-finding study and a GLP-compliant embryo-fetal and peri-postnatal developmental 
toxicity study in female Sprague-Dawley rats according to FDA Guidance for Industry 
Considerations for the Developmental Toxicity Studies for Preventive and Therapeutic Vaccines 
for Infectious Disease Indications (DHHS 2006). There were no [AMENDMENT_A101]-related effects on 
mating performance, fertility, pregnancy, embryo-fetal survival, teratogenicity, or any litter 
parameters including effects on postnatal growth and physical/functional development of the F1 
pups in these studies. 
A biodistribution study showed only a relatively small fraction of [AMENDMENT_A101] administered IM 
distributed to distant tissues, and it did not persist past 1 to 3 days in tissues other than at the 
injection site, the spleen, and the lymph nodes. 
A detailed review of nonclinical experience with the study injection is provided in the IB. 
2.2.2. 
Clinical Studies  
Completed and ongoing clinical studies involving the CMV vaccine candidate [AMENDMENT_A101] are 
listed below. Please refer to the most recent version of the IB for detailed descriptions 
([SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. [AMENDMENT_A101] Investigator’s Brochure). 
• 
A completed Phase 1 dose-escalation study ([AMENDMENT_A101]/mRNA-1443-P101) in US 
adults evaluating the safety and immunogenicity of 4 dose levels of [AMENDMENT_A101] in a 
liquid presentation versus placebo.  
• 
A completed Phase 1 study ([AMENDMENT_A101]-P103) in Japanese adults living in the US 
evaluating the safety and immunogenicity of 100 µg [AMENDMENT_A101] in a lyophilized 
presentation versus placebo. 
• 
A completed Phase 2 dose-finding study ([AMENDMENT_A101]-P202) in US adults evaluating 
the safety and immunogenicity of 3 dose levels of [AMENDMENT_A101] in a lyophilized 
presentation versus placebo. 
• 
An ongoing Phase 2 extension study ([AMENDMENT_A101]-P202-EXT) to evaluate immune 
persistence and safety of [AMENDMENT_A101] in participants who completed study 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P202. 
• 
An ongoing Phase 1/2a study ([AMENDMENT_A101]-P104) in adolescents and adults 
evaluating the safety and immunogenicity of 3 dose levels of [AMENDMENT_A101] versus 
placebo. 
• 
An ongoing Phase 2 proof-of-concept study ([AMENDMENT_A101]-P205) in adults who have 
undergone allogenic hematopoietic cell transplantation evaluating the efficacy, safety, 
and immunogenicity of [AMENDMENT_A101] versus placebo.

2.3. 
Benefit/Risk Assessment 
Approximately 2,750 CMV-seronegative and 700 CMV-seropositive participants will be 
exposed to [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine in this study; approximately 2,750 CMV-seronegative and 
700 CMV-seropositive participants will receive placebo. 
A summary of the potential risks and benefits of [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine is provided in the current 
IB. 
2.3.1. 
Known Potential Benefits 
Participants who receive [AMENDMENT_A101] may or may not directly benefit from vaccination as the 
efficacy of [AMENDMENT_A101] is yet to be established. 
Participants will obtain medical advice about their general health status as well as be informed of 
their CMV serostatus through the medical evaluations/assessments associated with this study 
(ie, physical examination). 
Participants will be contributing to the process of developing a new potentially prophylactic 
measure in an area of unmet medical need. 
2.3.2. 
Risks from Study Participation and Their Mitigation 
As with all injectable vaccines, immediate systemic allergic reactions, including serious allergic 
reactions such as anaphylaxis, to vaccination can occur. These immediate systemic allergic 
reactions are very rare and are estimated to occur once per 450,000 vaccinations for vaccines that 
do not contain allergens such as gelatin or egg protein (Zent et al 2002). Serious allergic 
reactions, including anaphylaxis, have been reported in subjects that have received other mRNA 
vaccines. 
As a precautionary measure, all participants will remain under observation at the study site for at 
least 30 minutes after vaccination. Participants with a history of anaphylaxis or other severe 
hypersensitivity reaction to the [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine or any components of the [AMENDMENT_A101] 
vaccine will be excluded. 
Any IM vaccination commonly precipitates a transient and self-limiting local inflammatory 
reaction. This typically includes pain, erythema (redness), or swelling (hardness) at the injection 
site, which usually occur within 24 hours of vaccination. 
Most systemic ARs observed after vaccination with [AMENDMENT_A101] did not exceed 
mild-to-moderate in severity. The most common systemic ARs are anticipated to be headache, 
fatigue, myalgia, or chills in the first days after [AMENDMENT_A101] administration. 
Vasovagal syncope (fainting) can occur before or after any vaccination, is usually tr[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]ered by 
the pain or anxiety caused by the injection and is not related to the substance injected. Therefore, 
it is important that standard precautions and procedures be followed to avoid injury from 
fainting. 
There have been very rare (<1 in 10,000 recipients) reports of myocarditis and pericarditis 
occurring after vaccination with COVID-19 mRNA vaccines. The majority of the cases have 
been reported in young males, within 7 to 14 days after the second dose of the vaccine. These are 
typically mild cases and individuals tend to recover within a short time following standard 


--- Page 49 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 49 
treatment (including rest, NSAIDs, and/or colchicine). Healthcare professionals and study 
participants should be alert to the signs and symptoms of myocarditis and pericarditis 
(Gargano et al 2021). It is not known whether the risk of myocarditis or pericarditis is increased 
following additional doses of other non-COVID mRNA vaccines. 
Further details are provided in the current IB. 
2.3.3. 
Overall Benefit/Risk Conclusion  
[AMENDMENT_A101] is currently under investigation and IA data from Phase 1 and Phase 2 clinical trials 
show that participants receiving [AMENDMENT_A101] show binding and nAbs were observed to be 
induced, although no VE has been demonstrated thus far. Taking into account the measures taken 
to minimize the risk to individuals participating in this study, the potential risks to the 
participants are justified by the potential benefits linked to the development of [AMENDMENT_A101]. 


--- Page 50 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 50
