4. 
STUDY DESIGN  
4.1. 
General Design  
This is a Phase 3, randomized, observer-blinded, placebo-controlled study in healthy participants 
16 to 40 years of age. 
The primary efficacy objective is to demonstrate vaccine effect of [AMENDMENT_A101] against primary 
CMV infection in female participants who are CMV-seronegative at enrollment. Primary CMV 
infection is defined as seroconversion from a negative result (baseline/Day 1) to a positive result 
for serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] against CMV as measured by a platform-based automated immunoassay based on 
at least 1 of the 4 recombinant CMV antigens not encoded by [AMENDMENT_A101] (pp150, pp28, pp52, 
pp38) assessed starting 28 days after the third injection and confirmed by a repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test 
performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion. 
Participants who are CMV-seropositive at baseline will not be included in the primary efficacy 
analysis. 
Approximately 6,900 total participants will be enrolled in the study: 
• 
CMV-seronegative cohort: 5,500 female participants 
• 
CMV-seropositive cohort: 1,400 female participants 
Participants will be randomly assigned in a 1:1 ratio to receive either 100 µg [AMENDMENT_A101] or 
placebo. Randomization will be in a blinded manner using a centralized IRT at the Day 1 visit, in 
accordance with pre-generated randomization schedules. For each serostatus cohort 
(CMV-seronegative, CMV-seropositive), randomization will be stratified by age (≥16 to 
<18 years, ≥18 to <20 years, or ≥20 to ≤40 years) to balance treatment assignments. At least 
400 enrolled CMV-seronegative female participants will be in the ≥16 to <18 age group. At least 
400 female participants will be enrolled in Japan (including approximately 
320 CMV-seronegative and 80 CMV-seropositive female participants, respectively). Each 
participant will participate in 2 phases: Vaccination Period (Screening to Month 7 [Day 197; 
28 days following the third injection]) and a Follow-up Period (post Month 7 [Day 198]) through 
Month 30 (Day 887; approximately 24 months after the third injection) as illustrated in the study 
flow diagram (Figure 1). Upon completing the Vaccination Period, participants will have 
scheduled study visits approximately every 3 months during the Follow-up Period for safety and 
study assessments. 
All participants will receive the first injection on Day 1 and will receive the same treatment for 
the second injection at Month 2 (Day 57) and the third injection at Month 6 (Day 169). 
Participants will have approximately 14 study visits and approximately 21 safety telephone 
calls/eDiary safety and surveillance prompts over the course of the study. During the Vaccination 
Period, local and systemic solicited ARs will be collected through 7 days following each 
injection using an eDiary. Any solicited AR that is ongoing beyond Day 7 will be recorded until 
no longer reported, not exceeding 28 days. Unsolicited AEs will be collected starting the day of 
each injection and through 28 days following each injection. MAAEs will be collected starting 
on Day 1 and through 6 months after the last injection. SAEs will be collected from time of 
consent through EoS. Deaths, AESIs, and AEs leading to withdrawal from further injections or 
from study participation will be collected through EoS. Pregnancy and pregnancy outcome data 


--- Page 53 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 53 
will be collected in all participants who become pregnant during the study from Day 1 to EoS, 
including spontaneous and voluntary terminations and congenital abnormalities, as defined in 
Section 8.14.6. Pregnancy and pregnancy outcome data may be collected beyond EoS (ie, for 
pregnancies continuing beyond EoS Visit). 
Participants will have scheduled blood samplings over the course of the study to assess 
eligibility, seroconversion due to primary CMV infection (CMV-seronegative cohort), 
vaccine-induced antibody responses, and antibody persistence. A more detailed overview of 
procedures and visits can be found in the SoAs (Table 8 and Table 9). 
The study is observer-blind where only delegated unblinded study personnel responsible for 
study injection preparation, administration, and/or accountability will have access to study 
treatment assignments. Neither the participant nor participant’s parent(s)/LAR(s) nor the 
Investigator nor study site staff responsible for study assessments/safety will have access to the 
treatment assignment during the conduct of the study. The Investigator may unblind in the event 
of an emergency (refer to Section 6.3.7). 
Participants may experience AEs that necessitate an unscheduled visit or may be identified 
during scheduled study visits; these AEs will be recorded as MAAEs. There may also be 
situations in which the Investigator asks a participant to return for a visit following the report of 
an AE. Additional examinations may be conducted at these visits as necessary to ensure the 
safety and well-being of participants during the study. eCRFs should be completed for each visit. 
All participants will be followed for safety for a minimum of 30 months (24 months after the 
third injection) for seroconversion due to primary CMV infection (CMV-seronegative cohort), 
CMV shedding (CMV-seropositive participants and CMV-seronegative participants meeting the 
endpoint of seroconversion), pregnancy outcomes, and for SAEs through to EoS and MAAEs for 
6 months after the last injection (refer to Table 9). 
Participants who discontinue from further vaccinations after either the first or second vaccination 
but do not withdraw consent will be followed for safety as noted above and will provide blood 
samples for immunogenicity and seroconversion due to primary CMV infection 
(CMV-seronegative cohort) and urine samples for CMV shedding (CMV-seropositive 
participants, and CMV-seronegative participants meeting the endpoint of seroconversion ) (refer 
to Table 9). 
Cytomegalovirus-Seronegative Cohort: 
Cytomegalovirus-seronegative cohort participants will provide blood samples for assessment of 
seroconversion due to primary CMV infection and, for female participants of childbearing 
potential, urine samples for pregnancy testing at scheduled study visits specified in the SoAs 
(Table 8 and Table 9). 
Participants meeting the endpoint of seroconversion due to primary CMV infection from 
Month 3 through EoS will be contacted to be seen for an unscheduled study visit 
(Seroconversion Visit) for clinical assessment including blood, urine, and saliva sampling for 
CMV PCR, after which they will return to the planned visit schedule. At each scheduled visit 
after the Seroconversion Visit through the EoS, urine will be collected for CMV PCR and serum 
will no longer be collected for CMV serology, with the exception of Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing 
(see Section 8.11). 


--- Page 54 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 54 
Participants who seroconvert prior to Month 3 will not require a Seroconversion Visit, will no 
longer be required to have serum collected for CMV serology at subsequent planned visits, with 
the exception of Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing (Section 8.11), and will have urine collected for CMV 
PCR at subsequent visits. Participants who seroconvert at the EoS Visit (Visit 31) will be asked 
to return to the clinic as soon as possible for a Seroconversion Visit (unscheduled visit) and will 
be asked to return ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion (unscheduled visit) for Confirmatory 
[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing and urine collection. 
Participants who seroconvert will have a repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed to confirm the diagnosis of 
primary CMV infection. The repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test will be performed ≥28 days from the date of 
seroconversion (Section 8.11).  
In the CMV-seronegative cohort, it is anticipated that the majority of seroconversions due to 
primary CMV infection will be asymptomatic and will be detected by planned serological 
surveillance testing at scheduled study visits. Participants will be assessed for symptoms meeting 
criteria for possible symptomatic primary CMV infection by protocol-defined criteria 
(Section 8.9) at scheduled study visits starting at Month 3, safety telephone calls, and via eDiary 
safety surveillance prompts (beginning at Month 8). Participants meeting protocol-defined 
criteria for possible symptomatic primary CMV infection between scheduled study visits, during 
safety telephone calls, or via eDiary during the Follow-up Period will be instructed to return to 
the study site for a CMV Illness Assessment Visit (unscheduled visit) (Section 8.9). The CMV 
Illness Assessment Visit will include physical examination (including vital signs); collection of 
blood samples for hematology, chemistry, seroconversion due to primary CMV infection, and 
EBV panel; and a urine sample for CMV PCR. At the discretion of the Investigator, testing for 
HIV antibodies, HIV viral load, and SARS-CoV-2 may be performed. In addition, participants 
reporting symptoms for possible symptomatic primary CMV infection by protocol-defined 
criteria may also receive electronic patient-reported outcomes (ePRO) questionnaires to collect 
information on health state and health-related productivity as reported by the participant. The 
questionnaires include the EuroQol-5 Dimension 5 Level (EQ-5D-5L) and the HRPQ, which is 
tr[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]ered based on potential symptomatic primary CMV illness symptoms. 
Cytomegalovirus-Seropositive Cohort: 
Cytomegalovirus-seropositive cohort participants will have urine sampling for CMV shedding 
and, for female participants of childbearing potential, urine pregnancy testing at scheduled study 
visits specified in the SoAs (Table 8 and Table 9). 
4.2. 
Scientific Rationale for Study Design  
The design and dose proposed for Study [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 are based on accumulated safety and 
immunogenicity data from Study [AMENDMENT_A101]/mRNA-1443-P101 and Study [AMENDMENT_A101]-P202. 
In the Phase 1 study, a planned IA of safety and immunogenicity through Month 12 (6 months 
after the third vaccination) in the 30 µg, 90 µg, and 180 μg treatment groups and safety through 
Month 7 (1 month after the second vaccination) in the 300 μg treatment group showed that there 
were no vaccine-related SAEs and the safety profile at the 300-µg dose level was comparable to 
that observed at the 180-µg dose level. 
In the CMV-seronegative 30 µg, 90 µg, and 180 µg groups: 


--- Page 55 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 55 
• 
A dose-related immune response was observed. At Month 7 (1 month after the third 
vaccination), GMTs of nAb against epithelial cell infection in the 30 μg, 90 μg, and 
180 μg treatment groups exceeded the natural infection benchmark by 2.8-, 10.8-, and 
10.5-fold, respectively. GMTs of nAb against fibroblast infection exceeded the 
natural infection benchmark by 1.3- and 1.4-fold in the 90 μg and 180 μg treatment 
groups, respectively. 
• 
There was early evidence of immune persistence. At Month 12 (6 months after the 
third vaccination), nAb titers against epithelial cell infection (a measure of immune 
response to intact CMV pentamer antigen) were 3.6- and 3.9-fold higher than the 
natural infection benchmark in the 90 μg and 180 μg treatment groups, respectively, 
and nAb titers against fibroblast infection (a measure of immune response to CMV 
gB antigen) approximated the natural infection benchmark in the 90 μg and 180 μg 
treatment groups. 
In the CMV-seropositive 30 µg, 90 µg, and 180 µg groups: 
• 
At Month 7 (1 month after the third vaccination), GMR of nAbs against epithelial cell 
infection ranged from 22.4 to 40.8 across the 30 µg, 90 µg, and 180 µg groups, 
respectively, and GMRs of nAbs against fibroblast infection ranged from 4.0 to 6.5. 
• 
At Month 12 (6 months after the third vaccination), nAb titers continued to show 
boosting response; GMRs of nAb titers against epithelial cell infection ranged from 
14.6 to 31.4-fold and GMRs of nAbs against fibroblast infection ranged from 6 to 
8-fold across the 30 μg, 90 μg, and 180 μg treatment groups. 
In the Phase 2 study, a planned IA of safety and immunogenicity data through Month 3 (1 month 
after the second vaccination) in the 50 µg, 100 µg, and 150 μg treatment groups showed that 
[AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine was generally well-tolerated across all doses regardless of serostatus. No 
SAEs were reported and there were no unsolicited events leading to study discontinuation. 
In CMV-seronegative participants, nAbs against epithelial cell infection increased in a generally 
dose-related manner after the first vaccination. After the second vaccination, nAb GMTs against 
epithelial cell infection were boosted to at least 12-fold over the baseline GMT of 
CMV-seropositive participants (a measure of previous naturally acquired CMV infection). The 
Month 3 nAb GMTs against epithelial cell infection in the 50 µg, 100 µg, and 150 μg treatment 
groups were generally numerically similar. Neutralizing antibodies against fibroblast infection 
did not show an appreciable increase after the first vaccination. After the second vaccination, 
nAb against fibroblast infection were boosted to GMTs generally equivalent to the baseline 
GMT in CMV-seropositive participants. The Month 3 nAb GMTs in the 50 µg, 100 µg, and 
150 μg treatment groups were generally numerically similar. 
In CMV-seropositive participants, baseline nAb GMTs against epithelial cell infection as well as 
fibroblast infection varied across treatment groups. Within each [AMENDMENT_A101] treatment group, 
nAb GMTs against epithelial cell infection boosted to levels at least 8-fold over the respective 
baseline GMT after the first vaccination, and to GMTs at least 13-fold to greater than 51-fold 
over the respective baseline GMT after the second vaccination. Within each [AMENDMENT_A101] 
treatment group, nAb GMTs against fibroblast infection boosted to levels at least 2-fold over the 
respective baseline GMT after the first and second vaccinations. The increased postbaseline nAb 


--- Page 56 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 56 
GMTs against fibroblast infection in the placebo treatment group resulted in GMRs that were 
similar to the [AMENDMENT_A101] treatment groups. 
Study [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 will evaluate a 100-µg dose of the [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine given in a 
3 vaccination (Day 1, Month 2 [Day 57], and Month 6 [Day 169]) schedule for safety and 
immunogenicity in CMV-seronegative and CMV-seropositive participants 16 to 40 years of age. 
4.3. 
Justification for Choice of Study Population 
The target population for enrollment into this Phase 3 [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 pivotal study are 
participants aged 16 to 40 years. This includes a population of women carrying a relatively 
higher risk for primary CMV infection and an age range that encompasses the childbearing 
years. Inclusion of younger women is particularly important in that primary CMV infection 
occurs at higher rates in younger women at a time when first pregnancy may occur. In 2018, 
most of the births in US women aged <20 years were in those aged 16 to 19 years 
(Martin et al 2019) and annual seroconversion rates in the adolescent population are estimated to 
range from 4 to 13% (Zanghellini et al 1999; Bate et al 2010; Bernstein et al 2016). For all 
women of childbearing age, a safe and effective vaccine against CMV infection administered in 
the years prior to pregnancy would invoke preconceptional immunity and thus prevent cCMV 
infection of the offspring. 
Inclusion criteria specific to female participants also specify that participants ≥20 years of age 
have close contact with young children. The rationale is that CMV infection in young children is 
common and high levels of CMV are shed in their saliva and urine for several months after 
infection (Cannon et al 2014). Cytomegalovirus-seronegative women who care for young 
children are at increased risk for acquiring primary CMV infection through contact with the 
infected secretions of the children they care for (Adler 1991). The risk for primary infection 
during pregnancy and subsequently delivering a congenitally infected infant is significantly 
associated with having had a previous pregnancy (Leruez-Ville et al 2017). A CMV vaccine that 
eliminates child-to-mother transmission could significantly decrease the incidence of cCMV. 
It is important to acknowledge that most children with cCMV infection are born to mothers who 
have acquired CMV in the years prior to pregnancy (Manicklal et al 2013). There is mounting 
evidence indicating that CMV reinfection during pregnancy is also linked to increased risk of 
cCMV infection and disease in the offspring of CMV-seropositive mothers (Ross et al 2010; 
Yamamoto et al 2010; Boppana et al 2001). The ideal vaccination strategy to prevent cCMV 
infection would include not only vaccination against primary CMV infection in 
CMV-seronegative females of childbearing age, but also vaccination of CMV-seropositive
women if boosting preexisting immunity against CMV prevents reinfection.
4.4. 
Justification for Dose and Schedule 
The rationale for a 3-dose schedule at 0, 2 and 6 months is to induce antigen-specific immunity 
with 2 doses spaced 2 months apart followed by a dose at 6 months to optimize the induction of 
immune persistence. The dose level of 100 µg [AMENDMENT_A101] for this Phase 3 ([AMENDMENT_A101]-P301) 
study was determined based on safety and immunogenicity data from the 
[AMENDMENT_A101]/mRNA-1443-P101 study and interim safety and immunogenicity data from Part 1 
of the Phase 2 study ([AMENDMENT_A101]-P202). A predefined approach integrating safety and 
immunogenicity data across all treatment groups (50 µg, 100 µg, or 150 µg [AMENDMENT_A101] or 


--- Page 57 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 57 
placebo) through 1 month after the second vaccination in the Phase 2 study was used to 
determine the dose with the most favorable probability of achieving optimal nAb titers within an 
acceptable safety profile in the majority of participants. 
4.5. 
Justification for Use of Placebo  
There is currently no licensed CMV vaccine available; 0.9% sodium chloride injection (normal 
saline) placebo is used as it allows for blinding of study treatments and allows for a control so 
that the effects of vaccine administration on both efficacy and safety findings can be isolated, 
including adverse effects from the IM injection. 
4.6. 
End-of-Study Definition  
An individual participant is considered to have completed the study if she has completed both 
phases of the study including the last procedure as shown in the SoAs and any required 
Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing, and sample collection for CMV PCR as applicable (Table 8 and 
Table 9). 
The EoS overall is defined as completion of the last visit of the last participant in the study as 
shown in the SoA for the last participant in the study globally.  
There will be an optional Extension Substudy. EoES is the last visit of the last participant in the 
Extension Substudy as shown in the SoA of Extension Substudy (see Section 11.9). 
4.7. 
Safety Oversight  
4.7.1. 
Internal Safety Team  
A blinded IST composed of the CRO medical monitor, Sponsor clinical development lead, and 
Sponsor safety physician, will provide primary safety oversight at defined intervals throughout 
the study. Details regarding composition, responsibilities, and procedures of the IST will be 
presented in the IST charter. 
4.7.2. 
Data Safety Monitoring Board  
Scheduled meetings of the independent DSMB will occur at the following timepoints in the 
study as detailed in the DSMB Charter: 
• 
After the first 600 participants have been enrolled and have completed Day 29 
(28 days after first injection) follow-up to review unblinded study safety data and 
make recommendations to the Sponsor regarding ongoing enrollment. 
• 
At specified enrollment milestones to review unblinded study safety data including 
pregnancy and pregnancy outcomes and make recommendations to the Sponsor 
regarding study conduct. 
• 
At the release of the Primary Analysis and to make recommendations to the Sponsor 
regarding study conduct based on the prespecified criteria for early efficacy as 
described in Section 9.6. 
The DSMB may make the following recommendations to the Sponsor (as appropriate): 


--- Page 58 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 58 
• 
Continue enrollment as planned after the initial 600 participants have been enrolled. 
• 
Continue enrollment and/or study conduct as planned. 
• 
Pause enrollment and/or dosing due to a safety concern. 
• 
Stop further enrollment due to overwhelming VE. 
The Sponsor may also request that the DSMB convene on an ad hoc basis to review any safety 
concerns brought to the DSMB by the safety review team, to review any safety data from this 
study, or review other data including new nonclinical or clinical information related to 
[AMENDMENT_A101] external to this study. The DSMB composition, its remit, and frequency of data 
review will be further defined in the DSMB Charter. 
4.7.3. 
Adjudication Committee  
An independent AC blinded to treatment assignments will be assembled to confirm that criteria 
for symptomatic seroconversion due to primary CMV infection have been met in cases that have 
been identified as symptomatic primary CMV infection. 
The AC composition, its remit, and frequency of data review will be further defined in the AC 
charter. 
4.7.4. 
Independent Cardiac Event Adjudication Committee  
An independent CEAC comprising medically qualified personnel, including cardiologists, will 
review all suspected cases of myocarditis, pericarditis, and myopericarditis to determine if they 
meet CDC criteria for “probable” or “confirmed” events, which are reported in ongoing clinical 
studies per the CEAC charter (Gargano et al 2021). Any cases that the CEAC assesses as 
representing probable or confirmed cases of myocarditis or pericarditis will be referred to the 
Sponsor, who will then determine if additional action is needed. The CEAC will operate under 
the rules of an approved charter that will be written and reviewed at the organizational meeting 
of the CEAC. Details regarding the CEAC composition, responsibilities, procedures, and 
frequency of data review will be defined in the charter.

5. 
STUDY POPULATION  
Approximately 6,900 healthy participants 16 to 40 years of age who are not pregnant at the 
Screening or Day 1 visits will be enrolled into 1 of 2 cohorts: 
• 
CMV-seronegative cohort: approximately 5,500 female participants will be randomly 
assigned to [AMENDMENT_A101] or placebo in a 1:1 ratio. 
• 
CMV-seropositive cohort: approximately 1,400 female participants will be randomly 
assigned to [AMENDMENT_A101] or placebo in a 1:1 ratio. 
For each serostatus cohort (CMV-seronegative, CMV-seropositive), randomization will be 
stratified by age (≥16 to <18 years, ≥18 to <20 years, and ≥20 to ≤40 years) to balance treatment 
assignments. 
Upon completion of all Screening procedures (Section 8.1), the Investigator will review the 
inclusion/exclusion criteria for each participant to determine if the participant is eligible. 
Participants who meet all eligibility criteria will be enrolled in the study. 
Screening information will be recorded on the appropriate page in the eCRF. The Screening Visit 
may be performed across 2 separate study visits. 
Prospective approval of protocol deviations to recruitment and enrollment criteria, also known as 
protocol waivers or exemptions, is not permitted. 
Inclusion and exclusion criteria for the Infant Outcome Substudy are provided in Section 11.6. 
5.1. 
Inclusion Criteria  
Participants are eligible to be included in the study only if all the following criteria apply (no 
protocol exemptions will be allowed in this study): 
1. Is a female and 16 to 40 years of age, at the time of consent. 
2. According to the assessment of the Investigator, is capable of complying with study 
procedures. 
3. For female participants aged ≥20 years, has or anticipates having direct exposure 
within 7 months after the planned first dose (in the home, socially, or occupationally) 
to at least 1 child ≤5 years of age. Direct exposure is defined as either a) participant is 
the parent, or b) participant has close contact (feeding, diaper changes, 
childcare/supervision) for at least 8 hours per week. 
4. For the CMV-seronegative Cohorts: at the Screening Visit, is CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-negative 
and CMV IgM-negative: 
For CMV-seropositive Cohorts: at the Screening Visit, is CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-positive and 
CMV IgM- negative, or CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-positive and CMV IgM-positive. Participants with 
an isolated positive result for CMV IgM (ie, CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-negative and CMV 
IgM-positive) will not be eligible for enrollment but may be rescreened after at least 
6 weeks from the initial CMV Screening.

A participant with a CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-positive result and an IgM-indeterminate result at 
Screening will not require the IgM sampling to be repeated in order to consider the 
participant CMV-seropositive (Section 5.3). 
5. Participant (and parent/LAR, if applicable) provides written informed consent/assent. 
Participants under the age of majority (ie, under legal age) at the time of enrollment 
must provide written informed consent at the next study visit once turning the age of 
majority. 
6. Investigator assessment confirms that the participant (including in the case of an 
emancipated minor), or parent(s)/LAR(s), as applicable, understands and is willing 
and physically able to comply with protocol-mandated follow-up including all study 
visits and procedures anticipated during the 30-month Study Period. 
7. This criterion has been removed in Protocol Amendment 2: Has a body mass index of 
15 to 35 kg/m2, inclusive. 
8. Female participants of childbearing potential: Urine pregnancy test is negative at

participants of nonchildbearing potential. See Section 11.8 for definition of 
nonchildbearing potential. 
9. Female participants of childbearing potential: If the participant is sexually active with 
men, all of the following criteria must be met: 
• 
Has practiced adequate contraception or has abstained from all activities that could

• 
Agrees to continue adequate contraception through 3 months following the third 
study injection (Month 9/Day 257). 
Adequate contraception is defined as consistent and correct use of an approved 
contraceptive method in accordance with the product label, or sterilization of a 
monogamous male partner prior to study enrollment (Section 11.8.2). 
5.2.

1. This criterion has been removed in Protocol Amendment 2: Female participants: Is of 
nonchildbearing potential. Nonchildbearing potential is defined as one of the 
following: 
• 
Surgically sterile (reports history of bilateral tubal ligation, bilateral oophorectomy, 
hysterectomy). 
• 
Postmenopausal state (reports history of amenorrhea for ≥12 consecutive months 
prior to Screening without an alternative medical cause). 
2. History of a diagnosis or condition that, in the judgment of the Investigator, is 
clinically unstable or may affect participant safety, assessment of safety endpoints, 
assessment of immune response, or adherence to study procedures. Clinically

unstable is defined as a diagnosis or condition requiring significant changes in 
management or medication within the 2 months prior to Screening and includes 
ongoing workup of an undiagnosed illness that could lead to a new diagnosis or 
condition. This includes but is not limited to: 
• 
Reported history of congenital or acquired immunodeficiency, immunosuppressive 
condition, or immune-mediated disease. 
• 
Dermatologic conditions that could affect local solicited AR assessments (eg, tattoos; 
psoriasis patches affecting skin over the deltoid areas). 
• 
Reported history of anaphylaxis or severe hypersensitivity reaction after receipt of the 
[AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine or any components of the [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine. 
• 
Reported history of bleeding disorder that is considered a contraindication to IM 
injection or phlebotomy. 
• 
Any medical, psychiatric, or occupational condition, including reported history of 
drug or alcohol abuse, that, in the opinion of the Investigator, might pose additional 
risk due to participation in the study or could interfere with the interpretation of study 
results. 
3. Received or plans to receive any nonstudy vaccine <28 days prior to and after any 
study injection; in addition, the following criteria for COVID-19 and influenza 
vaccines apply: 
• 
Any COVID-19 primary vaccination series must have been completed a minimum 
28 days prior to receiving any dose of the study injection. 
• 
COVID-19 vaccines (including any booster dose, regardless of manufacturer) must be 
administered at least 28 days prior to or after any study injection. 
• 
Influenza vaccines may be administered >14 days prior to or after any study injection. 
4. Received systemic immunosuppressants or immune-modifying drugs for >14 days in 
total within 6 months prior to the day of first injection (Day 1) (for corticosteroids, 
≥5 mg/day of prednisone equivalent) or plans to do so during the course of the study. 
Inhaled, nasal, and topical steroids are allowed. Stable immunomodulator regimens 
used for managing environmental allergies are allowed. 
5. Receipt of an antiviral with activity against CMV (ganciclovir, valganciclovir, 
foscarnet, cidofovir, letermovir, acyclovir, valacyclovir) <2 weeks prior to the day of 
first injection or plans to do so during the course of the study. 
6. Previous receipt of an investigational CMV vaccine. 
7. Receipt of systemic immunoglobulins or blood products <3 months prior to the day of 
first injection. 
8. Has donated ≥450 mL of blood products <28 days prior to Screening. 
9. Participated in an interventional clinical study <28 days prior to the day of first 
injection (Day 1) or plans to do so while enrolled in this study.

5.3. 
Screen Failures  
Screen failures are defined as participants who consent to participate in the clinical study but are 
not subsequently randomized. A minimal set of screen failure information is required to ensure 
transparent reporting of screen failure participants to meet the Consolidated Standards of 
Reporting Trials publishing requirements and to respond to queries from regulatory authorities. 
Minimal information includes date of informed consent, demography, eligibility criteria not met, 
reason not randomized if eligible, and information on any SAE which may have occurred from 
the time informed consent was obtained to the time of withdrawal. 
Individuals who do not meet the eligibility criteria for participation in this study (screen failure) 
may be rescreened. Rescreened participants returning within the initial 28-day Screening window 
will retain the same participant number assigned at the initial Screening. If the rescreen visit 
occurs >28 days from the previous ICF signature date, the participant will be assigned a new 
Screening number, and all Screening procedures will be repeated. Re-screening may not be 
repeated more than once unless there is documented rationale to do so. 
If a participant’s serostatus result is determined to be CMV-seropositive (ie, is either CMV 
[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-positive/IgM-negative or CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-positive/IgM-positive, or CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-positive/IgM 
indeterminate) as reported in the initial study Screening laboratory results, the CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]/IgM 
sampling does not need to be repeated during the Re-screening Visit. The participant may be 
enrolled as a CMV-seropositive participant if all eligibility criteria are met.

6. 
STUDY INTERVENTION  
6.1. 
Study Intervention Administered  
The [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine against CMV infection consists of 6 distinct mRNA sequences 
encoding important targets of nAb response to human CMV infection (full length CMV gB and 
pentameric gH/gL/UL128/UL130/UL131A glycoprotein complex [pentamer]) in an LNP 
formulation. 
The LNP formulation includes 4 lipid components: SM-102, a proprietary ionizable amino lipid, 
and the commercially available lipids cholesterol, DSPC, and PEG2000-DMG (Mui et al 2013). 
[AMENDMENT_A101] injection is stored at 2ºC to 8ºC until use. Following appropriate dose preparation, 
[AMENDMENT_A101] injection will be administered IM into the deltoid muscle, preferably in the 
nondominant arm, in a volume of 0.5 mL. 
The Phase 3 formulation of [AMENDMENT_A101] will be filled and lyophilized in 2R Type I glass vials at 
a total mRNA content of 151 μg/vial. Prior to use, the lyophilized drug product is reconstituted 
with 0.7 mL of 0.9% sodium chloride injection, a concentration of 0.2 mg/mL for administration 
of the specified dose level of 100 μg in a volume of 0.5 mL. 
A 0.9% sodium chloride injection (normal saline) placebo will be administered IM into the 
deltoid muscle, preferably in the nondominant arm, in a volume of 0.5 mL. 
6.2. 
Randomization and Blinding  
6.2.1. 
Randomization  
Randomization within each serostatus cohort (CMV-seronegative, CMV-seropositive) will be 
stratified by age (≥16 to <18 years, ≥18 to <20 years, or ≥20 to ≤40 years) via IRT in a 1:1 ratio 
to receive either 100 µg [AMENDMENT_A101] or placebo administered in a 3-vaccination (Day 1, Day 57 
[Month 2], and Day 169 [Month 6]) schedule. At least 400 enrolled CMV-seronegative female 
participants will be in the ≥16 and <18 age group. 
6.2.2. 
Blinding  
This is an observer-blinded study. The Investigator, study site staff, study participants, site 
monitors, and Sponsor personnel (or its designees) will be blinded to the IP administered, with 
the following exceptions: 
• 
Unblinded personnel (of limited number) will be assigned to vaccine accountability 
procedures and will prepare IP for all participants. These personnel will have no study 
functions other than study injection management, documentation, accountability, 
preparation, and administration. They will not be involved in participant evaluations 
and will not reveal the identity of IP to either the participant or the blinded study site 
personnel involved in the conduct of the study unless this information is necessary in 
the case of an emergency. 
• 
Unblinded medically qualified study site personnel will administer the IP. They will 
not be involved in assessments of any study endpoints. 


--- Page 64 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 64 
• 
Unblinded site monitors, not involved in other aspects of monitoring, will be assigned 
as the IP accountability monitors. They will have responsibilities to ensure that sites 
are following all proper IP accountability, preparation, and administration procedures. 
• 
Laboratory personnel responsible for immunogenicity testing will be blinded to the 
treatment assignment and visit/timepoint of the samples tested throughout the course 
of the study. 
• 
An unblinded statistical and programming team will perform the planned analyses. 
(Section 9.6). 
• 
An independent DSMB will review the interim data to safeguard the interests of 
clinical study participants and to help ensure the integrity of the study. The DSMB 
will review unblinded statistical outputs and interim results, provided by the 
independent unblinded statistician, and make recommendations to the Sponsor 
(Section 4.7.2). 
• 
If the Primary Analysis or Final Analysis is completed based on accrual of 
prespecified seroconversion cases and achieves the primary efficacy objective, 
preidentified Sponsor and CRO team members responsible for the analysis and 
reporting will be unblinded to treatment assignments in order to prepare the CSR. 
In order to maintain an observer-blind design, Investigators, study site staff, participants, 
Sponsor, and the CRO staff with oversight of study conduct will remain blinded to treatment 
allocation for the study duration. All participants will be followed for efficacy and safety 
endpoints through the remainder of planned Study Period and results will be summarized in an 
EoS report (Section 4.1 and Section 9.1). The dosing assignment will be concealed by having the 
unblinded personnel prepare the IP in a secure location that is not accessible or visible to other 
study site staff. An opaque sleeve or label over the syringe used for injection will maintain the 
blind at the time of injection, as the doses containing [AMENDMENT_A101] will look different than 
placebo. Only delegated unblinded study site staff will conduct the injection procedure. Once the 
injection is completed, only the blinded study site staff will perform further assessments and 
interact with the participants. Access to the randomization code will be strictly controlled by the 
unblinded study personnel. 
Except in the case of medical necessity, a participant’s treatment should not be unblinded 
without the approval of the Sponsor. The treatment code should be broken only if the 
Investigator/physician in charge of the participant feels that the case cannot be treated without 
knowing the identity of the study injection. Instructions regarding emergency unblinding will be 
provided to the Investigator and is discussed in Section 6.3.7. 
6.3. 
Preparation/Handling/Storage/Accountability  
6.3.1. 
Clinical Study Material Preparation  
The Sponsor or designee is responsible for the following: 
• 
Supplying the clinical study material. 
• 
Confirming the appropriate labeling of [AMENDMENT_A101] injection, such that it complies 
with the legal requirements of each country where the study is to be performed.

Confidential

The Investigator is responsible for the following: 
• 
Acknowledgment of the receipt of the clinical study material by a unblinded 
designated staff member at the site, including the following: 
− Confirming that the clinical study material was received in good condition. 
− Confirming to the Sponsor that the temperature during shipment from the Sponsor 
to the Investigator’s designated storage location was appropriate. 
− Confirming whether the Sponsor has authorized the clinical study material for 
use. 
− Ensuring the appropriate dose of [AMENDMENT_A101] injection is prepared using aseptic 
technique (lyophilized vaccine reconstituted with 0.9% sodium chloride injection 
for delivery of the specified dose in a volume of 0.5 mL). 
Further description of the clinical study material and instructions for the receipt, storage, 
preparation, administration, accountability, and destruction of the clinical study material are 
described in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Pharmacy Manual. 
6.3.2. 
Clinical Study Material Administration  
The [AMENDMENT_A101] injection is formulated for IM administration preferably in the nondominant 
arm. [AMENDMENT_A101] injection will be prepared for single-dose use. 
Following appropriate dose preparation, [AMENDMENT_A101] injection will be administered IM into the 
deltoid muscle in a volume of 0.5 mL. 
A 0.9% sodium chloride injection (normal saline) placebo will be administered IM into the 
deltoid muscle, preferably in the nondominant arm, in a volume of 0.5 mL. 
Further instructions for the preparation (reconstitution) and administration of [AMENDMENT_A101] 
injections are described in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Pharmacy Manual. 
PRECAUTIONS TO BE OBSERVED IN ADMINISTERING STUDY INJECTION 
Prior to vaccination, participants must be determined to be eligible for study vaccination and it 
must be clinically appropriate in the judgment of the Investigator to vaccinate the participant. 
Eligibility for vaccination prior to first study injection administration is determined by evaluating 
the study entry criteria outlined in Section 5.1 and Section 5.2. 
Study injection should not be administered to participants with known hypersensitivity to the 
[AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine or any components of the [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine. 
Standard vaccination practices are to be observed and care should be taken to administer the IM 
injection. Before administration, the injection site must be disinfected with a skin disinfectant 
(eg, 70% isopropyl alcohol or ethanol) and allowed to dry. The vaccine should NOT be injected 
intravascularly. 
As with all injectable vaccines, trained medical personnel, and appropriate medical treatment 
should be readily available in case of anaphylactic reactions following administration. For 
example, epinephrine 1:1000, diphenhydramine, and/or other medications for treating 
anaphylaxis should be available.

6.3.3. 
Clinical Study Material Packaging and Labeling  
All study treatments will be prepared, packaged, and labeled in accordance with the standard 
operating procedures of [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. or those of its designee, CFR Title 21, GMP 
guidelines, ICH GCP guidelines, guidelines for Quality System Regulations, and applicable 
regulations. 
The study treatments will be labeled in accordance with requirements of the local regulatory 
agencies. 
In addition, the 0.9% sodium chloride injection (normal saline) placebo will be labeled for 
clinical study use. 
6.3.4. 
Clinical Study Material Storage  
[AMENDMENT_A101] injection is stored at 2ºC to 8ºC until use. 
A 0.9% sodium chloride injection (normal saline) is stored according to the label. 
6.3.5. 
Clinical Study Material Accountability  
The Investigator or designee must maintain an accurate record of the shipment receipt, the 
inventory at the site, dispensing of study treatment, and the return to the Sponsor or alternative 
disposition of used/unused study treatment in a drug accountability log. Drug accountability will 
be reviewed by the unblinded CRA during site visits and at the completion of the study. For 
further direction, refer to the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Pharmacy Manual. 
6.3.6. 
Clinical Study Material Handling and Disposal  
The designated unblinded CRA will reconcile the clinical study material in the interim and at the 
end of the study for compliance. Once fully reconciled at the site, the clinical study material can 
be destroyed at the investigational site or Sponsor-selected third party, as appropriate. 
Study products may be destroyed at the study site only if permitted by local regulations and 
authorized by the Sponsor. A Certificate of Destruction or alternative documentation of 
destruction must be obtained and sent to the Sponsor or designee. For further direction refer to 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Pharmacy Manual. 
6.3.7. 
Unblinding  
Except in the case of medical necessity, a participant’s treatment assignment should not be 
unblinded without the approval of the Sponsor. If a participant becomes seriously ill or pregnant 
during the study, the blind will be broken only if knowledge of the treatment assignment will 
affect that participant’s clinical management. In the event of a medical emergency requiring 
identification of individual treatment assignment, the Investigator will make every attempt to 
contact the CRO’s medical monitor to explain the need for unblinding within 24 hours of 
unblinding. The Investigator will be responsible for documenting the time, date, reason for 
unblinding, and the names of the personnel involved. The Investigator (or designee) will have 
access to unblind participants within IRT. All unblinding events will be tracked via an audit trail 
in IRT and documented in the final CSR.

6.4. 
Study Intervention Compliance  
All study treatments will be administered by qualified and trained unblinded study personnel to 
ensure that all treatments administered comply with those planned. Study treatments 
administered will be recorded in the eCRF. Administration data will be reconciled with site 
accountability records to determine compliance. 
6.5. 
Concomitant Therapy  
At each study visit, the study site personnel should question the participant or participant’s 
parent(s)/legal guardian(s)/legally authorized representative regarding any medications taken and 
vaccinations received and record the information as specified in Section 6.5.1. 
Any COVID-19 vaccination series should be completed at least 28 days prior to receiving any 
dose of study injection. COVID-19 vaccines (regardless of manufacturer) must be administered 
at least 28 days prior to or after any study injection. If a participant is eligible to receive a 
COVID-19 vaccine at any point during the study (irrespective of the type of vaccine) and there is 
a conflict with any study-related activities, receiving the COVID-19 vaccination takes priority 
over all other study-related activities. 
In the event a COVID-19 vaccination unavoidably interferes with the scheduling of study 
injection 2 or 3, the study injection visit must be delayed at least 28 days after the COVID-19 
vaccination. In this situation, the study injection will be permitted out of window, but should be 
administered within 14 days after the end of the 28-day post COVID-19 vaccination window. 
If the participant has already received a study injection and is within the 28-day period after 
study injection and a COVID-19 vaccine/booster is recommended, the participant should discuss 
the timing of COVID-19 vaccination with their healthcare provider. 
6.5.1. 
Recording of Concomitant Medications and Concomitant Vaccinations  
The following concomitant medication(s) and vaccine(s) must be recorded in the eCRF: 
• 
Any nonstudy vaccines administered during the period starting 28 days before any 
study injection. 
• 
Any COVID-19 vaccine(s) taken before the first injection and through the last study 
visit. 
• 
All concomitant medications and nonstudy vaccinations taken through 28 days after 
each injection. 
• 
Any concomitant medications and vaccines listed in Section 6.5.2. 
• 
Any concomitant medications and vaccines relevant to an SAE or administered from 
the signing of the ICF through the EoS/the last study visit for the treatment of a SAE. 
• 
Any concomitant medications relevant to or for the treatment of an AESI from Day 1 
through EoS/the last study visit. 
• 
Any antipyretic or analgesic to treat or prevent fever or pain within 7 days after 
vaccination, including the day of vaccination.

• 
Any concomitant medications and/or vaccines relevant to an MAAE administered 
from Day 1 through 6 months after the last study injection (Day 347/Month 12). 
• 
Prophylactic medications (ie, medication administered in the absence of any symptom 
and in anticipation of a reaction to the vaccination) from Day 1 to 28 days after the 
last vaccination. For example, an antipyretic or analgesic is considered to be 
prophylactic when it is given in the absence of fever and any other symptom, to 
prevent fever from occurring. 
6.5.2. 
Concomitant Medications and Vaccines that May Lead to the Elimination of a 
Participant from Per-protocol Analyses  
The use of the following concomitant medications and/or vaccines will not require withdrawal of 
the participant from the study but may determine a participant’s evaluability in the PP analysis. 
Analysis sets are described in Section 9.4. 
• 
Any investigational or nonregistered product (drug or vaccine) other than the study 
vaccine used during the Study Period. 
• 
Immunosuppressants or other immune-modifying drugs administered chronically 
(ie, more than 14 days in total) during the Study Period. For corticosteroids, this 
includes prednisone >5 mg/day or the equivalent. Inhaled, nasal, and topical steroids 
are allowed. Stable immunomodulator regimens used for managing environmental 
allergies are allowed. 
• 
Long-acting immune-modifying drugs administered at any time during the Study 
Period (eg, infliximab). 
• 
Any licensed seasonal influenza vaccine can be administered >14 days prior to or 
after any study injection. 
• 
Other than seasonal influenza vaccine, nonstudy vaccination series including 
COVID-19 vaccination series (regardless of manufacturer), must be completed a 
minimum of 28 days prior to or after receiving any dose of study injection. 
• 
Immunoglobulins and/or any blood products administered during the Study Period. 
• 
Antiviral with activity against CMV (ganciclovir, valganciclovir, foscarnet, cidofovir, 
letermovir, acyclovir, valacyclovir) administered during the course of the study. 
6.6. 
Intervention After the End of the Study  
This section is not applicable.

7. 
DELAY OR DISCONTINUATION OF STUDY INTERVENTION 
AND PARTICIPANT DISCONTINUATION/WITHDRAWAL 
FROM STUDY  
7.1. 
Criteria for Delay of Vaccine or Placebo Administration  
Body temperature should be measured prior to any vaccine/placebo administration. If the 
participant has a fever (defined as a temperature ≥38.0°C/100.4°F) on the day of administration, 
the visit should be rescheduled within the allowed window allowance for that visit (see Table 8). 
The same should be done if the Investigator determines that any other aspect of the participant’s 
health on the day of administration precludes administration such as acute infection. 
Study injection should be rescheduled if the participant received any COVID-19 vaccine 
(regardless of manufacturer) within 28 days prior to planned study injection. 
In the event a COVID-19 vaccination unavoidably interferes with the scheduling of study 
injection 2 or 3, the study injection visit must be delayed at least 28 days after the COVID-19 
vaccination. In this situation, the study injection will be permitted out of window, but should be 
administered within 14 days after the end of the 28-day post COVID-19 vaccination window. 
If the participant has already received a study injection, and is within the 28 day period after 
study injection and a COVID-19 vaccine/booster is recommended, the participant should discuss 
the timing of COVID-19 vaccination with their healthcare provider. 
7.2. 
Discontinuation of Study Treatment  
A discontinuation or missed dose from the study treatment ([AMENDMENT_A101] or placebo) refers to 
any participant who does not receive the 3-dose treatment series. A participant discontinued 
from the study treatment may not necessarily be discontinued from the study as further study 
procedures or follow-up may be performed (safety or immunogenicity), if planned in the study 
protocol. The Investigator should make all efforts to ensure that the participants remain in the 
study to ensure a proper safety follow-up and medical care if needed and document the reason 
for participant discontinuation of study treatment. 
Information relative to premature discontinuation of the study injection will be documented in the 
eCRF. The Investigator will document which of the following reasons was responsible for 
discontinuation of study injections: 
• 
AE (including SAE) 
• 
Solicited Adverse Reaction/Reactogenicity Event 
• 
Probable or confirmed myocarditis, pericarditis, and/or myopericarditis 
• 
Death 
• 
Lost to Follow-up 
• 
Physician Decision 
• 
Pregnancy 
• 
Protocol Deviation 


--- Page 70 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 70 
• 
Study Terminated by Sponsor 
• 
Withdrawal of Consent by Participant 
• 
Other (specify) 
Participants who discontinue from treatment for any reason after the first study injection will be 
followed to Visit 31 (Day 887/Month 30/EoS). 
Participants who are randomized to treatment but do not receive the first study injection on the 
same day will be permitted to return for the first study injection on Day 1 if within the 28-day 
Screening window. Participants who are randomized to treatment but do not receive the first 
study injection will be discontinued from study treatment and the study, with the exception of 
any participant being followed for an SAE. Serious AEs will be followed as per Section 8.14.7. 
7.3. 
Participant Discontinuation/Withdrawal from the Study  
Participants who are withdrawn from the study will not be replaced. 
From an analysis perspective, a “withdrawal” from the study refers to a situation wherein a 
participant does not return for the final visit foreseen in the protocol. 
All data collected until the date of withdrawal or last contact of the participant will be used for 
the analysis. 
A participant is considered a “withdrawal” from the study when no study procedure has 
occurred, no follow-up has been performed, and no further information has been collected for 
that participant from the date of withdrawal or last contact. 
Investigators will attempt (eg, 3 telephone calls) to contact those participants who do not return 
for scheduled visits or follow-up. 
Information relative to the withdrawal will be documented in the eCRF. The Investigator will 
document whether the decision to withdraw a participant from the study was made by the 
participant or by the Investigator as well as which of the following was the primary reason for 
withdrawal: 
• 
AE (including SAE) 
• 
Solicited Adverse Reaction/Reactogenicity Event 
• 
Death 
• 
LTFU (Section 7.4) 
• 
Physician decision (specify) 
• 
Pregnancy (Section 8.14.6) 
• 
Protocol deviation (specify) 
• 
Study terminated by Sponsor 
• 
Withdrawal of consent by participant (specify) 
• 
Other (specify) 


--- Page 71 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 71 
Participants who are withdrawn from the study because of SAEs/AEs must be clearly 
distinguished from participants who are withdrawn for other reasons. Investigators will 
follow-up with participants who are withdrawn from the study as result of an SAE or AE until 
resolution of the event. 
If a participant withdraws from the study, she may request destruction of any samples taken and 
not tested, and the Investigator must document this in the site study records. 
If the participant withdraws consent for disclosure of future information, the Sponsor may retain 
and continue to use any data collected before such a withdrawal of consent. 
The Sponsor will continue to retain and use all research results that have already been collected 
for the study evaluation. All biological samples that have already been collected may be retained 
and analyzed at a later date (or as permitted by local regulations) unless the participant has 
requested for them to be destroyed. 
7.4. 
Lost to Follow-up  
A participant will be considered LTFU if she repeatedly fails to return for scheduled visits 
without stating an intention to withdraw consent and is unable to be contacted by the study site. 
The following actions must be taken if a participant fails to return to the clinic for a required 
study visit: 
• 
The study site must attempt to contact the participant and reschedule the missed visit 
as soon as possible, counsel the participant on the importance of maintaining the 
assigned visit schedule and ascertain whether the participant wishes to and/or should 
continue in the study. 
• 
Before a participant who has been randomized to treatment is deemed LTFU, the 
Investigator or designee must make every effort to regain contact with the participant 
(where possible, 3 telephone calls and, if necessary, a certified letter to the 
participant’s last known mailing address or local equivalent methods). These contact 
attempts (eg, dates of telephone calls and registered letters) should be documented in 
the participant’s study record. 
• 
Should the participant continue to be unreachable, she will be considered to have 
withdrawn from the study for reason of LTFU. 
• 
A participant should not be considered LTFU until due diligence has been completed. 
Date of withdrawal/LTFU should be the date of last contact with the participant 
where safety status of the participant was assessed (eg, study visit, telephone call, 
eDiary entry).

8. 
STUDY ASSESSMENTS AND PROCEDURES  
The study SoAs can be found in Table 8 and Table 9 for the Vaccination Period and Follow-up 
Period, respectively. All information will be recorded on the appropriate page(s) in the eCRF 
unless stated otherwise. 
During the Follow-up Period (after Month 7), participants may have home visits (unless an in-
person visit is required for a symptom-directed physical examination) for study visits as 
indicated by the SoA (Table 9) if permitted per local regulations and IRB/IEC performed by 
appropriately delegated study site staff or a home healthcare service. 
With Sponsor approval, a safety telephone call or telemedicine visit may be conducted with the 
participant in place of the study visit in the event that the participant is not able to comply with a 
study visit. The safety call or telemedicine visit should encompass all scheduled visit 
assessments that can be completed remotely, such as assessment for AEs and concomitant 
medications (eg, as defined in scheduled safety calls). 
8.1. 
Screening  
Screening may be performed across 2 separate study visits starting at Visit Day 0, after the ICF 
has been signed. Where available and approved by the IRB/IEC, the ICF may be signed 
electronically via an eConsent portal. All Screening requirements, including reason for screen 
failure if a participant is not randomized, must be completed. 
8.2. 
Confirm Inclusion and Exclusion Criteria  
All inclusion and exclusion criteria described in Section 5.1 and Section 5.2 must be met before 
enrollment (Visit 1). 
8.3. 
Demographic and Baseline Data  
Demographic information relating to the participant’s sex, age, race, and ethnicity will be 
recorded at Screening. Prior pregnancy information will also be recorded at Screening. 
8.4. 
Medical History  
Medical history, including pregnancy history, for each participant will be collected and recorded 
on the appropriate page in the eCRF. Significant findings that were present prior to the signature 
of the informed consent must be included on the medical history page in the eCRF. 
8.5. 
Randomization  
Screening CMV serostatus must be confirmed prior to randomization to assign the participant to 
the appropriate cohort (CMV-seronegative or CMV-seropositive) and to complete randomization 
within IRT. Treatment assignment allocation will be performed on Day 1 (Visit 1) as described 
in Section 6.2.1. The confirmation of study treatment administration must be recorded in the 
eCRF.

[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 73 
8.6. 
Physical Examination  
A full physical examination including height and weight (body mass index will be calculated) 
will be performed during the Screening Period (Day -28 to Day -1) and throughout the study 
according to standard medical practice. 
Symptom-directed physical examinations will be performed at all study site visits following 
Screening (Table 8 and Table 9), if warranted; on each dosing day before injection, the arm 
receiving the injection must be examined and the associated lymph nodes must be evaluated. 
Any clinically significant findings identified during a study visit should be reported as an 
MAAE, as appropriate. 
8.7. 
Vital Signs  
Vital sign measurements include the assessment of body temperature, systolic and diastolic 
blood pressures, heart rate, and respiratory rate. The information collected will be recorded in the 
eCRF. 
Vital signs will be collected at the timepoints in the SoAs (Table 8 and Table 9). On days of 
study injection (Day 1, Day 57 [Month 2], and Day 169 [Month 6]), vital signs should be 
collected pre and post administration. When applicable, vital sign measurements should be 
performed before blood collection. 
8.8. 
Study Treatment Administration  
A 3-dose (Day 1, Day 57, and Day 169 [0-, 2-, 6-Month, respectively]) schedule will be used for 
all participants. Participants who are randomized to treatment but who do not receive the first 
study injection on the same day will be permitted to return for the first study injection on Day 1 
if within the 28-day Screening window. 
After completing all prerequisite procedures, the first dose of study treatment will be 
administered via IM injection into the deltoid muscle, preferably in the nondominant arm. 
A detailed description of the procedure is provided in Section 6.3.2. 
Participants who are febrile (body temperature ≥38.0°C/100.4°F) before injection must be 
rescheduled within the relevant window period to receive the injection. Afebrile participants with 
minor illnesses can be enrolled at the discretion of the Investigator. 
Participants who have a positive urine pregnancy test any time during the study should receive 
no further dosing with the study injection (Section 8.14.6). 
Participants will be asked if they are currently breastfeeding at each Study Intervention 
administration visit, and then documented in the source record and in eCRF. 
The participants will be observed closely (via clinical assessment including measurement of vital 
signs) for at least 30 minutes following the injection, with appropriate medical treatment readily 
available in case of anaphylaxis or other hypersensitivity reactions. 
Any participant who does not receive all study treatments will continue to be followed for safety, 
immunogenicity, and seroconversion for primary CMV infection (CMV-seronegative cohort) 
until EoS. Any participant who misses the 2-Month vaccination can continue in the study and 
receive the 6-month vaccination on schedule.

8.9. 
CMV Illness Assessment Visit (Unscheduled Visit) in Seronegative 
Cohort  
Seronegative participants reporting symptoms meeting clinical criteria for possible primary 
CMV infection will be evaluated starting at Month 3 at the study visit or at an unscheduled CMV 
Illness Assessment Visit. Possible symptoms meeting clinical criteria for possible primary CMV 
infection is defined as an illness reported by the participant consisting of at least 2 of the 
following symptoms: fever ≥38°C/100.4°F, myalgia, moderate to severe fatigue, sore 
throat/pharyngitis, or cervical lymphadenopathy in the absence of respiratory symptoms, 
(eg, nasal congestion, runny nose, cough). 
The occurrence of symptoms meeting criteria for primary CMV infection (see symptom criteria 
for possible primary CMV infection in Section 8.9) at Month 3 or later timepoint will also be 
reported. Participants reporting symptoms meeting criteria for possible primary CMV infection 
at scheduled study visits starting at Month 3, during safety telephone calls, or via eDiary safety 
surveillance prompts (beginning at Month 8), will have a CMV Illness Assessment Visit 
(unscheduled visit). Participants will be instructed to return to the study site if they experience 
such symptoms between scheduled study visits, during safety telephone call, or via eDiary 
during the Follow-up Period. The CMV Illness Assessment Visit will include physical 
examination (including vital signs); collection of blood samples for hematology, chemistry 
panels, seroconversion due to primary CMV infection (CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]), and EBV panel; and a urine 
sample for CMV PCR. At the discretion of the Investigator, testing for HIV antibodies, HIV viral 
load, and SARS-CoV-2 may be performed. In addition, participants reporting symptoms for 
possible symptomatic primary CMV infection by protocol-defined criteria may also receive 
ePRO questionnaires to collect information on health state and health-related productivity as 
reported by the participant. The questionnaires include the EQ-5D-5L and the HRPQ (see 
Section 8.13.5), which is be tr[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]ered based on potential symptomatic primary CMV illness 
symptoms. 
8.10. 
Seroconversion Visit (Unscheduled Visit) in Seronegative Cohort  
Participants in CMV-seronegative cohort with seroconversion due to primary CMV infection, as 
determined by either a positive [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] result for serum for CMV primary infection collected at 
scheduled study visits starting at Month 3 for CMV-seronegative participants or a positive [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] 
result for serum for CMV primary infection collected at a CMV Illness Assessment Visit, will be 
asked to return to the clinic as soon as possible for a Seroconversion Visit (unscheduled visit). 
This visit will include clinical assessments and blood, urine, and saliva sampling for CMV PCR, 
after which they will return to their usual visit schedule. At each scheduled visit after the 
Seroconversion Visit through the EoS, urine will be collected for CMV PCR and serum will no 
longer be collected for CMV serology, with the exception of Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing (see 
Section 8.11). 
Participants who seroconvert prior to Month 3 will not require a Seroconversion Visit, will no 
longer be required to have serum collected for CMV serology at subsequent planned visits, with 
the exception of Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing (see Section 8.11), and will have urine collected for 
CMV PCR at subsequent visits.  


--- Page 75 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 75 
Participants who seroconvert at the EoS Visit (Visit 31) will be asked to return to the clinic as 
soon as possible for a Seroconversion Visit (unscheduled visit) and will be asked to return 
≥28 days from the date of seroconversion (unscheduled visit) for Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing and 
urine collection. 
8.11. 
Confirmatory CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] Testing  
Participants who seroconvert at any postbaseline visit will have a repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed as 
soon as practicable, but no sooner than 28 days from the date of seroconversion, to confirm the 
diagnosis of primary CMV infection. The Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test may be conducted in one of the 
following ways: 
• 
At an unscheduled visit occurring ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion.  
• 
At the next planned study visit occurring ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion. 
The management of confirmatory testing for participants who seroconverted prior to the 
implementation of Protocol Amendment 5 will be as follows:  
• 
Where feasible, a suitable stored sample that was collected ≥28 days from the date of 
seroconversion will be utilized for the confirmatory test.  
• 
If no suitable stored sample exists, participants may be asked to give a new sample, 
either at an unscheduled visit or during their next scheduled study visit. 
Confirmatory CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test results starting with implementation of Protocol Amendment 5 will 
be managed as follows: 
• 
If the Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test is negative, the participant will revert to seronegative 
status and follow seronegative assessments. Specifically, the participant will 
discontinue urine testing for CMV PCR and resume the standard seronegative 
monitoring procedures, including serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing at scheduled study visits and the 
reporting of potential CMV-related symptoms via their eDiary.  
• 
If the Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test is positive, the participant will follow seropositive 
assessments. 
• 
If the Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test is indeterminate, an [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test will be repeated ≥2 weeks 
after the date of the indeterminate result. If the repeat Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test returns 
positive, the participant will be considered seroconverted and will follow seropositive 
assessments. If the repeat Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test returns negative, the participant will 
revert to seronegative status and follow seronegative assessments. An indeterminate 
repeat Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test will be handled on a case-by-case basis. 
Please refer to Table 8 and Table 9 for seropositive and seronegative assessments. 


--- Page 76 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc.

[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential

8.12. 
Efficacy and Immunogenicity Assessments  
8.12.1. 
Sampling for Assessment of Primary CMV Infection  
8.12.1.1. Cytomegalovirus-Seronegative Cohort  
Blood sampling for assessment of primary CMV infection (ie, CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing) will be 
performed at all study site visits throughout the study. On dosing days, blood sampling should be 
completed prior to study injection but after measurement of the pre-dose vital signs. 
If a blood sample for assessment of primary CMV infection returns a positive CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] result, 
Confirmatory CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing is required (Section 8.11). 
If a blood sample for assessment of primary CMV infection returns an indeterminate CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] 
result, a CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test will be repeated ≥2 weeks after the date of the indeterminate result to 
assess for an evolving antibody response to a primary CMV infection. If the repeat CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] 
test returns positive, Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing is required (Section 8.11). If the repeat CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] 
test returns negative, the participant will revert to seronegative status and follow seronegative 
assessments as outlined in Table 8 and Table 9. An indeterminate repeat CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test will be 
handled on a case-by-case basis. 
CMV-seronegative female cohort participants will be informed if antibody testing demonstrate 
seroconversion due to primary CMV infection. CMV PCR results will not be made available to 
participants during the study. Participants will be instructed not to seek CMV testing outside of 
the study and should request any additional CMV testing through the Study Investigator. 
Participants with seroconversion due to primary CMV infection at or after the Month 3 study 
visit will be asked to return to the clinic for a Seroconversion Visit (unscheduled visit) 
(Section 8.10). As needed, an additional visit may be scheduled to perform the Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] 
test (Section 8.11). If confirmed positive, at each scheduled visit after the Seroconversion Visit 
through the EoS, urine will be collected for CMV PCR. Participants who seroconvert prior to 
Month 3 will not require a Seroconversion Visit, will no longer be required to have serum 
collected for CMV serology at subsequent planned visits, with the exception of Confirmatory 
[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing (see Section 8.11), and will have urine collected for CMV PCR. 
Participants who seroconvert at the EoS Visit (Visit 31) will be asked to return to the clinic as 
soon as possible for a Seroconversion Visit (unscheduled visit) and will be asked to return 
≥28 days from the date of seroconversion (unscheduled visit) for Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing and 
urine collection. 
If a CMV-seronegative participant has previously seroconverted due to primary CMV infection 
prior to reporting symptoms meeting criteria for possible symptomatic primary CMV infection, a 
CMV Illness Assessment Visit is not required. 
8.12.1.2. Cytomegalovirus-Seropositive Cohort  
Cytomegalovirus shedding in CMV-seropositive participants will be assessed by sampling urine 
at the timepoints specified in Table 8 and Table 9. On dosing days, urine sampling should be 
completed prior to study injection.
