8.12.2. 
Sampling for Immunogenicity Assessments  
Immunogenicity assessments for both CMV-seronegative and CMV-seropositive participants 
will include the following: 
• 
Serum functional antibody levels against vaccine antigens as measured by nAb titer 
against epithelial cell infection and nAb titer against fibroblast infection. 
• 
Serum binding antibody levels against vaccine antigens as measured by ELISA 
specific to the gB and pentamer proteins. 
Collection of blood for immunogenicity assessments will occur at the timepoints specified in 
Table 8 and Table 9. 
Testing will be performed in a laboratory designated by the Sponsor. 
8.13. 
Safety Assessments  
Safety assessments will include monitoring and recording of the following for each participant: 
• 
Solicited local and systemic ARs that occur during the 7 days following each 
injection (ie, the day of injection and 6 subsequent days). Any solicited AR that is 
ongoing beyond Day 7 will be recorded until no longer reported, not exceeding 
28 days. Solicited ARs will be recorded daily using eDiaries. 
− Solicited local ARs include injection site pain, injection site erythema (redness), 
injection site swelling/induration (hardness), and localized axillary swelling or 
tenderness ipsilateral to the injection arm. 
− Solicited systemic ARs include headache, fatigue, myalgia (muscle aches all over 
the body), arthralgia (aching in several joints), nausea/vomiting, fever, and chills. 
• 
Beginning at Month 8, participants will receive safety eDiary prompts at timepoints 
specified in the SoA (Table 9). Safety eDiary will prompt the participant to report 
occurrence of relevant safety events. If eDiary prompt results in identification of a 
relevant safety event, trained study site personnel will call the participant within 
1 business day, or within 2 business days after the window for eDiary completion has 
closed if the participant did not complete the eDiary, to collect information relating to 
MAAEs (up to 6 months after the last injection), AESIs, AEs leading to withdrawal, 
SAEs, and information on concomitant medications associated with those events. For 
the CMV-seronegative cohort only, safety eDiary will also prompt the participant to 
report symptoms that may be consistent with symptomatic CMV (see symptom 
criteria for possible primary CMV infection in Section 8.9). For CMV-seronegative 
participants who have not seroconverted due to primary CMV infection, site 
personnel will review symptoms reported in the safety eDiary and determine whether 
a CMV Illness Assessment Visit is required. 
• 
Unsolicited AEs observed or reported starting the day of each injection and during the 
28 days following each injection (ie, the day of injection and 27 subsequent days). 
• 
AEs leading to discontinuation from dosing and/or study participation from Day 1 
through Day 887 (EoS) or withdrawal from the study. 


--- Page 78 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 78 
• 
MAAEs from Day 1 through 6 months after the last injection or withdrawal from the 
study. 
• 
AESIs from Day 1 through Day 887 (EoS) or withdrawal from the study. 
• 
SAEs from time of consent through Day 887 (EoS) or withdrawal from the study. 
• 
Vital sign measurements. 
• 
Physical examination findings. 
• 
For female participants of childbearing potential, urine pregnancy testing at each 
study visit. For participants who become pregnant during the study from Day 1 to 
EoS, pregnancy, and pregnancy outcome data will be collected; data may be collected 
beyond EoS for pregnancies continuing beyond the EoS Visit. 
Planned timepoints for all safety assessments are provided in Table 8 and Table 9. 
8.13.1. 
Sampling for Screening Laboratory Testing  
Screening laboratory testing will include CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] and IgM. Pregnancy testing at Screening and 
at each study visit (or at any time at the discretion of the Investigator) for female participants of 
childbearing potential will be a point-of-care urine test. 
8.13.2. 
Sampling for Safety Laboratory Testing  
Blood samples for safety laboratory testing will be collected if a CMV Illness Assessment Visit 
is performed to assess for seroconversion in CMV-seronegative cohort. Seronegative participants 
reporting symptoms meeting criteria for possible primary CMV infection at or after the Month 3 
study visit will be asked to return to the study clinic for an unscheduled CMV Illness Assessment 
Visit. This visit will include collection of blood samples for hematology and chemistry panels, 
seroconversion due to primary CMV infection (CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]), and EBV panel; and a urine sample 
for CMV PCR. At the discretion of the Investigator, testing for HIV antibodies, HIV viral load, 
and SARS-CoV-2 may be performed. 
The Investigator must review the laboratory report, document this review, and record any 
clinically relevant changes occurring during the study in the AE section of the eCRF. The 
laboratory reports must be filed with the source documents. Clinically significant abnormal 
laboratory findings are those which are not associated with the underlying disease, unless judged 
by the Investigator to be more severe than expected for the participant’s condition. 
8.13.2.1. Pregnancy Screen and Testing  
A urine dipstick pregnancy test will be performed for all female participants of childbearing 
potential at timepoints as specified in Table 8 and Table 9 and at any time during study 
participation if pregnancy is suspected. 
Further details on reporting and follow-up of pregnancy are provided in Section 8.14.6. 
8.13.3. 
Safety Telephone Calls  
Scheduled safety telephone calls will be made to the participant by trained study site personnel at 
the timepoints specified in Table 8 and Table 9. These calls will follow a script, which will 


--- Page 79 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 79 
facilitate the collection of relevant safety information. The participant will be interviewed 
according to the script, and information relating to follow-up for solicited ARs, as applicable (ie, 
for missing entries, medications taken for pain or fever, and/or for solicited ARs continuing 
beyond Day 7), AEs, MAAEs, AESIs, SAEs, and concomitant medications associated with these 
events; receipt of nonstudy vaccinations, and AEs leading to study withdrawal will be collected. 
During the Follow-up Period of the study (starting from Month 8), eDiary prompts resulting in 
identification of a relevant safety event will require site personnel to call the participant within 
1 business day, or within 2 business days after the window for eDiary completion has closed if 
the participant did not complete the eDiary, to collect information relating to MAAEs (up to 
6 months after last injection), AESIs, AEs leading to withdrawal, SAEs, and information on 
concomitant medications associated with those events. For the CMV-seronegative cohort only, 
the safety eDiary will also prompt the participant to report symptoms that may be consistent with 
symptomatic primary CMV infection. Study personnel will call the participant if symptoms 
consistent with possible primary CMV infection (see symptom criteria for possible primary 
CMV infection in Section 8.9) are reported and schedule a CMV Illness Assessment Visit as 
applicable. 
With Sponsor approval, a safety telephone call or telemedicine visit may also be conducted with 
the participant in place of the study visit in the event that the participant is not able to comply 
with a study visit. The safety call or telemedicine visit should encompass all scheduled visit 
assessments that can be completed remotely, such as assessment for AEs and concomitant 
medications (eg, as defined in scheduled safety calls). 
All safety information described by the participant must be written down in a designated location 
within the source documents and not written on the script used for the telephone call. 
8.13.4. 
Blood Sampling Volumes  
The maximum planned volume of blood samples per participant is no more than 500 mL for the 
complete study. 
8.13.5. 
Participant-Reported Health Status and Health-Related Productivity due to 
Symptomatic Primary CMV Infection  
To evaluate the impact of symptomatic primary CMV infection on participant-reported health 
and health-related productivity in CMV-seronegative participants, participants reporting 
symptoms meeting criteria for possible primary CMV infection by protocol-defined criteria 
(Section 8.9) may receive electronic questionnaires (otherwise referred to as ePRO 
questionnaires) to collect information on health state and health-related productivity as reported 
by the participant. The ePRO questionnaires may include the EQ-5D-5L and/or the HRPQ 
version 2. 
The EQ-5D-5L is a preference-based measure of generic health status that is widely used in 
clinical studies and is recommended by several health technology assessment bodies as a key 
component of cost-utility analysis (EuroQol Research Foundation 2019). The EQ-5D-5L 
instrument comprises a short descriptive system questionnaire and a visual analog scale that are 
cognitively undemanding, taking only a few minutes to complete. The questionnaire provides a 
simple descriptive profile of a respondent’s health state. 


--- Page 80 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 80 
The HRPQ evaluates the impact of disease on absenteeism and presenteeism for household 
chores and classes/homework in addition to employment (Tundia et al 2015). 
Participants may receive the ePRO questionnaires based on potential symptomatic primary CMV 
illness symptoms. 
8.14. 
Safety Definitions  
8.14.1. 
Adverse Event  
An AE is defined as any untoward medical occurrence in a clinical study participant 
administered a medicinal drug product and which does not necessarily have a causal relationship 
with this treatment. An AE can be any unfavorable or unintended sign, symptom, or disease 
associated with the use of a medicinal product, whether or not considered related to the 
medicinal product. 
Adverse events will be reported by the participant (or, when appropriate, by a caregiver, 
surrogate, or the participant’s legally authorized representative). 
A TEAE is defined as any event that was not present before exposure to study injection or any 
event already present that worsens in intensity or frequency after exposure. 
Events Meeting the AE Definition 
• 
Exacerbation of a chronic or intermittent preexisting condition including either an 
increase in frequency and/or intensity of the condition. 
• 
New conditions detected or diagnosed after the first dose of the study injection even 
though they may have been present before the start of the study. 
Events NOT Meeting the AE Definition 
• 
Medical or surgical procedure (eg, endoscopy, appendectomy): the condition that 
leads to the procedure should be the AE. 
• 
Situations in which an untoward medical occurrence did not occur (social and/or 
convenience admission to a hospital). 
An AR is any AE for which there is a reasonable possibility that the study vaccination caused the 
AE (Section 8.14.3). For the purposes of investigational new drug safety reporting, “reasonable 
possibility” means that there is evidence to suggest a causal relationship between the study 
injection and the AE. 
An unsolicited AE is any AE reported by the participant that is one of the following: 
• 
Not specified as a solicited AR in the protocol 
• 
Is specified as a solicited AR in the protocol but starts outside the protocol-defined 
period for reporting solicited ARs (ie, after 7 days of each injection). 
8.14.2. 
Serious Adverse Events  
An AE (including an AR) is considered an SAE if, in the view of either the Investigator or 
Sponsor, it results in any of the following outcomes: 


--- Page 81 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 81 
• 
Death 
− A death that occurs during the study or that comes to the attention of the 
Investigator during the protocol-defined Follow-up Period must be reported to the 
Sponsor, whether or not it is considered related to study injection. 
• 
Life-threatening 
− An AE is considered life-threatening if, in the view of either the Investigator or 
the Sponsor, its occurrence places the participant at immediate risk of death. It 
does not include an AE that, had it occurred in a more severe form, might have 
caused death. 
• 
Inpatient hospitalization or prolongation of existing hospitalization 
− In general, inpatient hospitalization indicates the participant was admitted to the 
hospital or emergency ward for at least 1 overnight stay for observation and/or 
treatment that would not have been appropriate in the physician’s office or 
outpatient setting. The hospital or emergency ward admission should be 
considered an SAE regardless of whether opinions differ as to the necessity of the 
admission. Complications that occur during inpatient hospitalization will be 
recorded as an AE; however, if a complication/AE prolongs hospitalization or 
otherwise fulfills SAE criteria, the complication/AE will be recorded as a separate 
SAE. 
• 
Persistent or significant incapacity or substantial disruption of the ability to 
conduct normal life functions 
− This definition is not intended to include experiences of relatively minor medical 
significance such as uncomplicated headache, nausea/vomiting, diarrhea, 
influenza, and accidental trauma (eg, sprained ankle) which may interfere with or 
prevent everyday life functions but do not constitute a substantial disruption. 
• 
Congenital anomaly or birth defect 
• 
Medically important event 
− Medical judgement should be exercised in deciding whether SAE reporting is 
appropriate in other situations, such as important medical events that may not be 
immediately life-threatening or result in death or hospitalization but may 
jeopardize the participant or require medical or surgical intervention to prevent 
one of the other outcomes listed in the above definition. These events should 
usually be considered serious. Examples of such medical events include allergic 
bronchospasm requiring intensive treatment in an emergency room or at home, 
blood dyscrasias or convulsions that do not result in inpatient hospitalization, or 
the development of drug dependency or drug abuse. 
8.14.3. 
Solicited Adverse Reactions and Reactogenicity Events  
The term “reactogenicity” refers to the occurrence and intensity of selected signs and symptoms 
also known as solicited ARs occurring after study injection. The eDiary will solicit daily 


--- Page 82 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 82 
participant reporting of ARs. Participants will record such occurrences in the eDiary on the day 
of each study injection and for the 6 days after the day of dosing. 
At each injection visit, participants will be instructed (Day 1) or reminded (Day 57 and Day 169) 
on thermometer usage to measure body temperature, ruler usage to measure injection site 
erythema and swelling/induration (hardness), and self-assessment for localized axillary swelling 
or tenderness ipsilateral to the injection arm. Participants will record body temperature, any 
solicited local (injection site) and systemic ARs, and whether any medications were taken to 
prevent or treat pain or fever starting on the day of each injection visit, at approximately 
30 minutes post injection under supervision of the study site staff to ensure successful entry of 
assessments. The study site staff will perform any re-training as necessary. Thereafter, the 
participant will be instructed to complete the eDiary later that day, preferably in the evening, and 
at the same time each day on the 6 subsequent days post injection. If assessments are not 
recorded for a given day, the participant will have a limited window on the following day to 
complete assessments for the previous day. 
Severity grading of solicited ARs will occur based on participant entry into the eDiary according 
to the grading scales presented in Table 3 modified from the Toxicity Grading Scale for Healthy 
Adult and Adolescent Volunteers Enrolled in Preventive Vaccine Clinical Trials (DHHS 2007). 
All solicited ARs (local and systemic) will be considered causally related to dosing. 
If a solicited local or systemic AR continues beyond 7 days after dosing, the participant will be 
prompted daily to capture solicited local or systemic ARs in the eDiary until no longer reported, 
but not to exceed 28 days after each injection. Investigators or designee will be required to 
review the solicited ARs recorded in the eDiary as part of the ongoing safety review. The 
Investigator or designee will review the eDiary 7 days after each study injection. Solicited ARs 
recorded in eDiaries lasting beyond 7 days post injection and any medications taken to prevent or 
treat pain or fever recorded in eDiaries will be reviewed either via scheduled telephone call or at 
the following study visit. 
Any solicited AR that meets any of the following criteria must be entered into the participant’s 
source document and recorded as a reactogenicity event in the eCRF: 
•
Solicited local or systemic ARs that were not recorded in the eDiary but reported to
the study site/Investigator and is Grade 1 or greater.
•
Solicited local or systemic AR that results in a visit to an HCP, including unscheduled
visits at the study site.
•
Solicited local or systemic AR that otherwise meets the definition of an SAE*.
•
Solicited local or systemic AR lasting beyond 7 days post injection*.
•
Solicited local or systemic AR leading to the participant withdrawing from the study
or the participant being withdrawn from the study by the Investigator (AE leading to
withdrawal).
•
Solicited local or systemic AR that leads to participant discontinuation from study
injection.
−
*Solicited ARs will meet definition of an AE if serious or lasts beyond 7 days
post injection.

8.14.4. 
Medically Attended Adverse Events  
An MAAE is an AE that leads to a visit to an HCP. This would include visits to a study site for 
assessments of the event (eg, illness, COVID-19) and visits to HCPs external to the study site 
(eg, urgent care, primary care physician). Adverse events reported during scheduled study visits 
that require medical attention should also be considered MAAEs. Investigators will review 
unsolicited AEs for the occurrence of any MAAEs. All MAAEs from Day 1 through 6 months 
after the last injection must be fully reported on the AE page in the eCRF. 
8.14.5. 
Adverse Events of Special Interest  
An AESI is an AE (serious or nonserious) of scientific medical concern specific to the Sponsor’s 
product or program, for which ongoing monitoring and immediate notification by the 
Investigator to the Sponsor is required. Such events may require further investigation to 
characterize and understand them. Refer to Section 11.4 for a list of AESIs pertinent to this 
study. All AESIs are collected through the entire Study Period and must be reported to the 


--- Page 85 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 85 
Sponsor or designee immediately and in all circumstances within 24 hours of becoming aware of 
the event via the EDC system. The Investigator will submit any updated information on AESIs to 
the Sponsor within 24 hours of it being available. If a site receives a report of a new AESI from a 
study participant or receives updated data on a previously reported AESI, and the eCRF has been 
taken offline, then the site can report this information on a paper AESI form using the SAE 
Mailbox (Section 8.14.11). 
8.14.5.1. Anaphylaxis  
All suspected cases of anaphylaxis should be recorded as MAAEs and AESIs and reported as 
SAEs, based on criteria for a medically important event (Section 8.14.2), unless the event meets 
other serious criteria. For reporting purposes, a participant who displays signs/symptoms 
consistent with anaphylaxis as shown below should be reported as a potential case of 
anaphylaxis. This is provided as a general guidance for Investigators and is based on the 
Brighton Collaboration case definition (Rüggeberg et al 2007). 
Anaphylaxis is an acute hypersensitivity reaction with multi-organ-system involvement that can 
present as, or rapidly progress to, a severe life-threatening reaction. It may occur following 
exposure to allergens from a variety of sources. Anaphylaxis is a clinical syndrome characterized 
by: 
• 
Sudden onset AND 
• 
Rapid progression of signs and symptoms AND 
• 
Involving 2 or more organ systems, as follows: 
− Skin/mucosal: urticaria (hives), generalized erythema, angioedema, generalized 
pruritus with skin rash, generalized prickle sensation, red and itchy eyes 
− Cardiovascular: measured hypotension, clinical diagnosis of uncompensated 
shock, loss of consciousness or decreased level of consciousness, evidence of 
reduced peripheral circulation 
− Respiratory: bilateral wheeze (bronchospasm), difficulty breathing, stridor, 
upper airway swelling (lip, tongue, throat, uvula, or larynx), respiratory distress, 
persistent dry cough, hoarse voice, sensation of throat closure, sneezing, 
rhinorrhea 
− Gastrointestinal: diarrhea, abdominal pain, nausea, vomiting 
8.14.5.2. Myocarditis and Pericarditis  
Any case of suspected, probable, or confirmed myocarditis, pericarditis, or myopericarditis 
should be reported as an AESI, even if it does not meet criteria per the CDC case definition. The 
event should also be reported as an SAE if it meets seriousness criteria (Section 8.14.2). The 
CDC case definition is provided in Section 11.7 as guidance. 
The Investigator’s medical judgment must be applied when assessing participants reporting 
symptoms for myocarditis, pericarditis, and/or myopericarditis contained within the CDC case 
definition. Diagnostic evaluation (eg, ECG, echocardiogram) and laboratory testing (eg, 
troponin) included in the CDC definition (Section 11.7) should promptly be obtained if 


--- Page 86 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 86 
considered clinically indicated in any participant with concerning signs/symptoms. Referral to a 
cardiologist should be obtained in those with positive test results or clinically significant 
symptoms without other identifiable causes. Additional testing and evaluation may be indicated. 
The Investigator will submit any updated myocarditis, pericarditis and/or myopericarditis case 
data to the Sponsor within 24 hours of it being available. Cases of myocarditis, pericarditis, 
and/or myopericarditis will be followed until resolution of symptoms and abnormal test findings. 
Participants with events of myocarditis, pericarditis, and/or myopericarditis will be discontinued 
from further study injection but should continue to be followed in the study for safety as per the 
protocol. 
An independent CEAC will review all suspected cases of myocarditis, pericarditis, and 
myopericarditis, which are reported in ongoing interventional clinical studies per the CEAC 
charter, to determine if they meet CDC criteria for “probable” or “confirmed” events 
(Section 11.7). 
In the case of any SAE or AESI, the participant must be followed up until clinical recovery is 
complete or until the outcome has been stabilized. 
8.14.6. 
Recording and Follow-up of Pregnancy  
Female participants who have a positive urine pregnancy test at Screening should not be 
enrolled. Participants who have a positive urine pregnancy test any time during the study should 
receive no further dosing with the study treatment/placebo and will be followed per-protocol for 
safety including pregnancy and pregnancy outcome data collection, seroconversion due to 
primary CMV infection or CMV shedding (as applicable according to CMV serostatus), and 
immunogenicity. Any CMV-seropositive participants who become pregnant will continue to 
have urine collections for CMV shedding Per-Protocol schedule. Any CMV-seronegative 
pregnant participants will continue scheduled blood testing for CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] to assess for 
seroconversion due to primary CMV infection and in addition will be offered blood testing for 
CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] on a monthly basis. If a previously CMV-seronegative participant becomes pregnant 
during the study and also meets the endpoint of seroconversion due to primary CMV infection 
during pregnancy, the study site Investigator inform the participant’s physician as soon as 
possible after receipt of a positive [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] result and every effort will be made to assure that the 
participant receives appropriate evaluation, counseling, and obstetric follow-up. The study site 
Investigator will provide the result of the Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test to the participant’s physician 
when received. 
Pregnancies occurring after the start of study treatment and until Month 30 (Day 887, EoS) or 
withdrawal from the study will be followed for outcome. Pregnancy and pregnancy outcome data 
may be collected beyond EoS (ie, for pregnancies continuing beyond EoS Visit). Pregnancy 
testing for female participants of childbearing potential is scheduled to occur as specified in 
Table 8 and Table 9. 
• 
If a pregnancy is reported, the Investigator should inform the Sponsor within 24 hours 
of learning of the pregnancy and should follow the procedures outlined in this section. 
• 
Abnormal pregnancy outcomes (eg, spontaneous abortion, fetal death, stillbirth, 
congenital anomalies, ectopic pregnancy) are considered SAEs.

If the participant agrees to submit this information, the pregnancy must be followed to determine 
the outcome, including spontaneous or voluntary termination, details of the birth, and the 
presence or absence of any birth defects, congenital abnormalities, or maternal and/or newborn 
complications. This follow-up should occur even if intended duration of the safety follow-up for 
the study has ended. Pregnancy report forms will be distributed to the study site to be used for 
this purpose. The Investigator must immediately (within 24 hours of awareness) report to the 
Sponsor any pregnancy resulting in an abnormal outcome according to the procedures described 
for SAEs. 
Pregnancy complications that occur more than 6 months after the last study injection 
administration will only be captured in the pharmacovigilance database, unless the event 
otherwise meets criteria to be reported as an SAE. 
8.14.6.1. Pregnancy and Infant Outcome Substudy  
Participants who become pregnant and are planning to carry the pregnancy to term will also be 
offered participation in an Infant Outcome Substudy under separate consent (see Section 11.6). 
8.14.7. 
Time Period, Recording, and Follow-up of an AE and/or SAE  
Medical occurrences that begin before the start of [AMENDMENT_A101] but after obtaining informed 
consent will be recorded in the medical history/current medical conditions section in the eCRF 
and not in the AE section; however, if the condition worsens at any time during the study, it will 
be recorded and reported as an AE. 
The Investigator is responsible for ensuring that all AEs and SAEs are recorded in the eCRF and 
reported to the Sponsor. 
Adverse events may be collected as follows: 
• 
Observing the participant. 
• 
Receiving an unsolicited complaint from the participant. 
• 
Questioning the participant in an unbiased and nonleading manner. 
Solicited ARs will be collected from the day of each injection through 7 days after each 
injection. Other (unsolicited) AEs will be collected from the day of injection through 28 days 
after each injection, including if participants used any new medications, changed concomitant 
medication regimens (both prescription and over-the-counter medications), or had any nonstudy 
injections. 
An abnormal value or result from a clinical or laboratory evaluation can also indicate an AE if it 
is determined by the Investigator to be clinically significant (eg, leads to Study Intervention 
discontinuation, or meets any serious criteria). If this is the case, it must be recorded in the 
source document and as an AE on the appropriate AE form(s). The evaluation that produced the 
value or result should be repeated until that value or result returns to normal or is stabilized and 
the participant’s safety is not at risk. 
All SAEs will be recorded and reported to the Sponsor or designee immediately and under no 
circumstance should this exceed 24 hours, as indicated in Section 8.14.2. The Investigator will 
submit any updated SAE data to the Sponsor within 24 hours of it being available. 


--- Page 88 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 88 
After the initial AE/SAE report, the Investigator is required to proactively follow each 
participant at subsequent visits/contacts. All AEs and SAEs (as defined in Section 8.14.1 and 
Section 8.14.2) will be treated as medically appropriate and followed until resolution, 
stabilization, the event is otherwise explained, or the participant is LTFU (as defined in 
Section 7.4), including ongoing SAEs after study completion. 
In addition to participant observations, physical examination findings, or other documents 
relevant to participant safety that is classified as an AE will be documented in the eCRF. 
Investigators are not obligated to actively seek AEs or SAEs after conclusion of the study 
participation (Day 887). However, if an Investigator learns of any SAE, including a death, at any 
time after a participant has been discharged from the study and considers the event to be 
reasonably related to the study injection or study participation, the Investigator must promptly 
notify the Sponsor. 
8.14.8. 
Assessment of Intensity  
An event is defined as “serious” when it meets at least one of the predefined outcomes as 
described in the definition of an SAE (Section 8.14.2), NOT when it is rated as severe. 
The severity (or intensity) of an AR or AE refers to the extent to which it affects the participant’s 
daily activities. The modified Toxicity Grading Scale for Healthy Adult and Adolescent 
Volunteers Enrolled in Preventive Vaccine Clinical Trials (DHHS 2007) will be used to 
categorize local and systemic solicited ARs (see Table 3), clinical laboratory test results, and 
vital sign measurements observed during this study. Specific criteria for local and systemic 
reactogenicity events are presented in Section 8.14.4. Specific criteria for clinical and laboratory 
abnormalities are presented in Section 11.4 and will be graded if outside of the reference range 
for the laboratory utilized. 
The determination of severity for all unsolicited AEs should be made by the Investigator based 
upon medical judgment and the definitions of severity as follows: 
• 
Mild: These events do not interfere with the participant’s daily activities. 
• 
Moderate: These events cause some interference with the participant’s daily activities 
and require limited or no medical intervention. 
• 
Severe: These events prevent the participant’s daily activity and require intensive 
therapeutic intervention. 
Study site staff should elicit from the participant the impact of AEs on the participant’s activities 
of daily living to assess severity and document appropriately in the participant’s source 
documentation. Changes in the severity of an AE should be documented in the participant’s 
source documentation to allow an assessment of the duration of the event at each level of 
intensity to be performed. An AE characterized as intermittent requires documentation of onset 
and duration of each episode. An AE that fluctuates in severity during the course of the event is 
reported once in the eCRF at the highest severity observed. 


--- Page 89 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 89 
8.14.9. 
Assessment of Causality  
The Investigator’s assessment of an AE’s relationship to the study treatments ([AMENDMENT_A101] or 
placebo) is part of the documentation process but is not a factor in determining what is or is not 
reported in the study. 
The Investigator will assess causality (ie, whether there is a reasonable possibility that the study 
treatment caused the event) for all AEs and SAEs. The relationship will be characterized using 
the following classification: 
• 
Not related: There is not a reasonable possibility of a relationship to the study 
treatment. Participant did not receive the study treatment OR temporal sequence of 
the AE onset relative to administration of the study treatment is not reasonable OR 
the AE is more likely explained by another cause than the study treatment. 
• 
Related: There is a reasonable possibility of a relationship to the study treatment. 
There is evidence of exposure to the study treatment. The temporal sequence of the 
AE onset relative to the administration of the study treatment is reasonable. The AE is 
more likely explained by the study treatment than by another cause. 
8.14.10. 
Reporting Adverse Events  
The Investigator is responsible for reporting all AEs that are observed or reported during the 
study, regardless of their relationship to the study treatment or their clinical significance. If there 
is any doubt as to whether a clinical observation is an AE, the event should be reported. 
All unsolicited AEs reported or observed during the protocol-defined AE reporting period (as 
per-protocol Section 4.1, Section 8.13, and Section 8.14.7) will be recorded in the eCRF. 
Information to be collected includes type of event, time of onset, Investigator-specified 
assessment of severity (impact on activities of daily living) and relationship to the study 
injection, time of resolution of the event, seriousness, any required treatment or evaluations, and 
outcome. The unsolicited AEs resulting from concurrent illnesses, reactions to concurrent 
illnesses, reactions to concurrent medications, or progression of disease states during the 
reporting period must also be reported. All AEs will be followed until they are resolved or stable 
or judged by the Investigator to be not clinically significant. The Medical Dictionary for 
Regulatory Activities (MedDRA) will be used to code all unsolicited AEs. 
Any medical condition that is present at the time that the participant is screened but does not 
deteriorate should not be reported as an unsolicited AE. However, if it deteriorates at any time 
during the study, it should be recorded as an unsolicited AE. 
8.14.11. 
Reporting SAEs  
Prompt notification by the Investigator to the Sponsor of a SAE is essential so that legal 
obligations and ethical responsibilities toward the safety of participants and the safety of a Study 
Intervention under clinical investigation are met. 
The Sponsor has a legal responsibility to notify both the local regulatory authority and other 
regulatory agencies about the safety of a Study Intervention under clinical investigation. The 
Sponsor will comply with country-specific regulatory requirements relating to safety reporting to 
the regulatory authority, IRBs, IECs, and Investigators. 


--- Page 90 ---

Investigator safety reports must be prepared for suspected unexpected serious ARs according to 
local regulatory requirements and Sponsor policy and forwarded to Investigators as necessary. 
An Investigator who receives an Investigator safety report describing a SAE or other specific 
safety information (eg, summary or listing of SAEs) from the Sponsor will review and then file it 
along with the IB and will notify the IRB/IEC, if appropriate according to local requirements. 
Any AE considered serious by the Investigator or that meets SAE criteria (Section 8.14.2) must 
be reported to the Sponsor immediately (within 24 hours of becoming aware of the SAE); these 
include anaphylaxis. The Investigator will assess whether there is a reasonable possibility that 
the study injection caused the SAE. The Sponsor will be responsible for notifying the relevant 
regulatory authorities of any SAE. The Investigator is responsible for notifying the IRB/IEC 
directly. 
If the eCRF is unavailable at the time of the SAE, the contact information to be used for SAE

recording events that meet the definition of an AE, including SAEs, and remain responsible for 
following up AEs that are serious, considered related to [AMENDMENT_A101] or study procedures, or that 
caused the participant to discontinue the study. 
8.14.12. 
Method of Detecting AEs and SAEs  
The method of recording, evaluating, and assessing causality of AE and SAE and the procedures 
for completing and transmitting SAE reports are provided in Section 8.14. 
Electronic diaries have specifically been designed for this study by the Sponsor. At the time of 
consent, the participants or participant’s parent(s)/legal guardian(s) must confirm they will be 
willing to complete the eDiary via an application downloaded to their smartphone or via a device 
that is provided at the time of enrollment. Prior to enrollment on Day 1, the participant will be 
instructed to download the eDiary application or will be provided an eDiary device to record 
solicited ARs on Day 1 (see Section 8.14.3). 
The Investigator is responsible for the documentation of AEs regardless of treatment group or 
suspected causal relationship to the study injection. For all AEs, the Investigator must pursue and 
obtain information adequate to determine the outcome of the AE and to assess whether the AE 
meets the criteria for classification as an SAE requiring immediate notification to the Sponsor or 
its designated representative. 
Care will be taken not to introduce bias when detecting AEs and/or SAEs. Open-ended and 
nonleading verbal questioning of the participant or the participant’s parent(s)/legal guardian(s) is 
the preferred method to inquire about AE occurrences.

9. 
STATISTICAL CONSIDERATIONS  
The details of statistical analysis will be provided in the SAP, which will be finalized before the 
clinical database lock for the study and treatment unblinding. If, after the study has begun, but 
prior to any unblinding, changes are made to primary and/or key secondary 
objectives/hypotheses, or the statistical methods related to those hypotheses, then the protocol 
will be amended (consistent with ICH Guideline E9). Changes to other secondary or exploratory 
analyses made after the protocol has been finalized, along with an explanation as to when and 
why they occurred, will be listed in the SAP or CSR for the study. Ad hoc exploratory analyses, 
if any, will be clearly identified in the CSR. 
9.1. 
Blinding and Responsibility for Analyses  
Blinding during the study will be conducted as described in Section 6.2.2. The Sponsor 
Biostatistics department or designee will generate the randomized allocation schedule(s) for 
study treatment assignment. Randomization will be implemented via an IRT. 
Planned analyses are described in Section 9.6. 
In addition to the routine study monitoring outlined in this protocol, an external DSMB will 
review interim data to safeguard the interests of clinical study participants and to enhance the 
integrity of the study. The DSMB will review treatment-level results, provided by the 
independent unblinded statistician. Participant level unblinding will be restricted to an 
independent unblinded statistician and, as needed, a statistical programmer performing the 
planned interim data analyses, who will have no other responsibilities associated with the study. 
Limited additional Sponsor personnel may be unblinded to the treatment-level results, if 
required, in order to act on the recommendations of the DSMB. The extent to which individuals 
are unblinded with respect to results will be documented. Participants and Investigators will 
remain blinded. 
9.2. 
Statistical Hypotheses  
For the primary efficacy objective, the null hypothesis (H0) and alternative hypothesis (H1) are as 
follows: 
H0efficacy: VE ≤25% versus H1efficacy: VE >25% 
VE is defined as the percent reduction in the hazard of the primary endpoint (mRNA‑1647 vs. 
placebo). The VE will be estimated using 1 minus the HR ([AMENDMENT_A101] vs. placebo). 
Equivalently, the null hypothesis is: H0efficacy: HR ≥0.75. 
The study will be considered to meet the primary efficacy objective if the corresponding CI of 
VE rules out 25% at either planned inferential analysis of efficacy (see Section 9.6). The overall 
Type I error rate for this test is strictly controlled at 2.5% (one-sided) with 0.5% allocated to the 
Primary Analysis and 2.0% allocated to the Final Analysis. 
 


--- Page 93 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 93 
9.3. 
Sample Size Determination  
The study originally planned to enroll approximately 6,900 female participants outside Japan 
(5,500 CMV-seronegative and 1,400 CMV-seropositive). In Protocol Amendment 2, 
approximately 400 female participants (320 CMV-seronegative and 80 CMV-seropositive) were 
added in Japan, resulting in a total sample size of approximately 7,300 female participants 
(5,820 CMV-seronegative and 1,480 CMV-seropositive). As this sample size update occurred 
prior to the first planned analysis without unblinding the study, no adjustment to the alpha levels 
of the planned analyses (Section 9.6) is needed. 
At the time of preparing Protocol Amendment 2, it was anticipated that, by the time enrollment 
in Japan started, enrollment outside Japan would have been completed. Therefore, approximately 
400 participants in Japan were added beyond the originally planned total sample size to ensure 
an adequate number of participants would be enrolled in Japan. Since Protocol Amendment 2 
became effective, enrollment in Japan started earlier than anticipated and overall enrollment 
outside Japan was slower than anticipated. As a result, in Protocol Amendment 3, the sample size 
was reduced back to the originally planned total of approximately 6,900 female participants 
(5,500 CMV-seronegative and 1,400 CMV-seropositive), with at least 400 participants in Japan 
now a part of this planned total. As in Protocol Amendment 2, given this sample size update 
occurred prior to the first planned analysis without unblinding the study, no adjustment to the 
alpha levels of the planned analyses (Section 9.6) is needed. In addition, this is a case-driven 
study in which the statistical power to address the primary efficacy objective in 
CMV-seronegative female participants depends directly on the number of primary infection 
cases observed at the time of the planned inferential analyses; as detailed below, this sample size 
will still provide at least 90% power at either planned inferential analysis. 
9.3.1. 
Power and Sample Size for the Cytomegalovirus-Seronegative Cohort  
The primary efficacy objective is to demonstrate VE in CMV-seronegative female participants. 
The sample size of the CMV-seronegative female cohort is driven by the total number of cases 
meeting the primary efficacy endpoint of primary CMV infection to demonstrate [AMENDMENT_A101] 
VE versus placebo in female participants who are CMV-seronegative at baseline. The study will 
randomly assign approximately 5,500 CMV-seronegative female participants in 1:1 ratio to 
[AMENDMENT_A101] and placebo in the CMV-seronegative female cohort. The sample size calculation 
focuses on having 90% power demonstrating VE of [AMENDMENT_A101] versus placebo by rejecting the 
null hypothesis H0: VE ≤25% at the Primary Analysis at one-sided 0.5% alpha and is based on 
the following assumptions: 
1. The underlying VE is 70%, 
2. The 12-months incidence rate on placebo is 1.5%, 
3. An enrollment period of 26 months, 
4. The primary analysis population for efficacy is PP Set, and a yearly loss of evaluable 
participants of 10% (to be excluded from the PP analysis), and 
5. Participants are at risk for primary CMV infection starting 1 month after the third 
injection. 


--- Page 94 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 94 
There are 2 planned inferential analyses of efficacy in this study: the Primary Analysis and the 
Final Analysis. The overall Type I error rate for this study is strictly controlled at 2.5% 
(one-sided) with 0.5% allocated to the Primary Analysis and 2.0% allocated to the Final Analysis 
for testing the null hypothesis for the primary efficacy endpoint (H0). 
The Primary Analysis will be carried out when: 
1. A total of 81 cases of the primary efficacy endpoint (ie, primary CMV infection) have 
been observed across the 2 groups in the PP Set in the CMV-seronegative female 
participants, and 
2. The median follow-up time of CMV-seronegative female participants is at least 
12 months after the third injection. 
A total of 81 primary infection cases at the Primary Analysis will provide 90% power to detect a 
VE of 70% (70% reduction in the hazard rate), rejecting the null hypothesis of H0: VE ≤25%, at 
a (one-sided) Type I error rate of 0.5%. 
If VE is demonstrated at the Primary Analysis (ie, one-sided p-value for testing the null 
hypothesis of H0: VE ≤25% is less than 0.005), there will be no further Type I error-controlled 
inferential analysis of the primary efficacy endpoint. All further/subsequent analyses of the 
primary efficacy endpoint will be considered descriptive or supportive in nature. In the situation 
that VE is demonstrated at the Primary Analysis, a Final Analysis after at least 112 primary 
efficacy endpoint cases have been observed across the 2 groups in the PP Set for Efficacy may 
be performed as a supportive analysis of the primary efficacy endpoint with longer follow-up 
time. 
In the event that VE is not demonstrated at the Primary Analysis (ie, one-sided p-value for 
testing the null hypothesis of H0: VE ≤25% is at or above 0.005), the Final Analysis will be 
carried out as an inferential analysis of efficacy when at least a total of 112 cases of the primary 
efficacy endpoint (ie, primary CMV infection) have been observed across the 2 groups in the PP 
Set for Efficacy. A total of 112 primary infection cases at the Final Analysis will provide >90% 
and approximately 90% power to detect a VE of 70% and 60%, respectively, rejecting the null 
hypothesis of H0: VE ≤25%, at a (one-sided) Type I error rate of 2.0%. 
The calculation is carried out using R package gsDesign. The total number of cases pertains to 
the PP Set with case accrual beginning at Month 7 when serum sample for 
efficacy/immunogenicity assessment is planned 1 month after the third injection. 
9.3.2. 
Power and Sample Size for the Cytomegalovirus-Seropositive Participants  
The sample size of the CMV-seropositive cohort is driven by safety. Approximately 
1,400 CMV-seropositive female participants will be randomly assigned in a 1:1 ratio to 
[AMENDMENT_A101] and placebo. With 700 CMV-seropositive participants exposed to mRNA‑1647, the 
study has at least 90% probability to observe at least 1 CMV-seropositive participant with an AE 
at a true 0.35% AE rate. 
9.4. 
Analyses Populations  
Analysis populations for statistical analyses are Randomization Set, FAS, mITT Set, PP Set, 
Immunogenicity Subset, Solicited Safety Set, and Safety Set, as shown in Table 4.

9.5. 
Statistical Analyses  
This section is a summary of the planned statistical analyses of the primary and secondary 
endpoints. 


--- Page 96 ---

Confidential 
Page 96 
The overall Type I error rate for this study is strictly controlled at 2.5% (one-sided) with 0.5% 
allocated to the Primary Analysis and 2.0% allocated to the Final Analysis for testing the null 
hypothesis for the primary efficacy endpoint (H0) (see Section 9.6 for details). Statistical 
significance of the primary efficacy endpoint can be achieved either at the Primary Analysis or at 
the Final Analysis. 
No formal multiple comparison adjustments will be employed for multiple safety endpoints or 
multiple efficacy endpoints. 
9.5.1. 
Summary of Baseline Characteristics and Demographics  
Demographic variables and baseline characteristics will be summarized by treatment group by 
descriptive statistics (mean, standard deviation for continuous variable, number and percentage 
for categorical variables). 
9.5.2. 
Efficacy Analyses  
9.5.2.1. 
Vaccine Efficacy in the Cytomegalovirus-Seronegative Cohort  
9.5.2.1.1. Analysis of Primary Efficacy Endpoint  
The primary efficacy endpoint is primary CMV infection. A primary efficacy endpoint (ie, 
primary CMV infection) case is defined as seroconversion from a negative to a positive result for 
serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] as measured by a platform-based automated immunoassay based on at least 1 of the 
4 recombinant CMV antigens not encoded by [AMENDMENT_A101] (pp150, pp28, pp52, pp38) and 
confirmed by a repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion. The primary 
analysis will be conducted in the PP Set with cases counted starting 28 days after the third 
injection. 
VE is defined as the percent reduction in the hazard of the primary endpoint (mRNA‑1647 vs. 
placebo). The VE will be estimated using 1 minus the HR ([AMENDMENT_A101] vs. placebo) estimand. 
A stratified Cox proportional hazard model will be used to assess the magnitude of the treatment 
group difference (ie, HR) between [AMENDMENT_A101] versus placebo. The HR and its alpha-adjusted 
CI from the stratified Cox model with Efron’s method of tie handling and with injection group as 
covariate will be reported. The stratification factor under serostatus used for randomization (ie, 
age group) will be applied to the stratified Cox model. For the primary efficacy analyses, cases 
will be counted starting at 1 month (28 days) after the third injection. The starting timepoint for 
deriving time to event (ie, primary CMV infection) or censoring will be the date of 
randomization. The event time will be defined as the sample collection date of the first of the 
2 positive [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] results, which represents the earliest time of a confirmed primary efficacy 
endpoint case. 
The PP Set will be the primary analysis population for all efficacy endpoints unless otherwise 
specified. Supportive analyses of efficacy using the mITT Set will also be carried out. Sensitivity 
analyses will be performed to assess VE in participants who have not received all 3-dose 
injections per schedule. 
For the primary efficacy endpoints, participants without documented primary CMV infection 
will be censored at the last study assessment date at which serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] is measured. 


--- Page 97 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 97 
In the estimand of the primary analysis on the primary endpoint, a hypothetical policy strategy 
will be used for death unrelated to primary CMV infection, where the time to primary CMV 
infection will be censored at the time of death; a hypothetical policy strategy will also be used 
for early primary CMV infection, where the time to primary CMV infection will be censored at 
the time of early infection. The details of intercurrent event description and estimand strategies 
are presented in Section 11.5.1. 
Supportive analyses of efficacy using the mITT Set will also be carried out. Sensitivity analyses 
will be performed with cases counted starting from the third injection, from 1 month (28 days) 
after the second injection, from the second injection, from the first injection, and after 
randomization, separately. An additional sensitivity analysis may be performed to assess VE in 
participants who have not received all 3-dose injection per schedule. 
In addition, VE will also be estimated based on the incidence rate of primary CMV infection in 
each group, defined as (1 – relative risk), where relative risk is the ratio of incidence rate of the 
primary CMV infection in participants in the [AMENDMENT_A101] arm relative to that of the placebo arm 
([AMENDMENT_A101]/placebo). The 2-sided 95% CI of VE will be provided using the exact method 
conditional upon the total number of cases. 
Table 5 summarizes the analysis approach for primary efficacy endpoint. 
Further details will be described in the SAP.

9.5.2.1.2. Analysis of Secondary Efficacy Endpoint of Systemic Viral Dissemination 
A secondary efficacy endpoint (ie, systemic viral dissemination) case is defined as: 
• seroconversion from a negative to a positive result for serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] as measured by a 
platform-based automated immunoassay based on at least 1 of the 4 recombinant CMV 
antigens not encoded by [AMENDMENT_A101] (pp150, pp28, pp52, pp38) and confirmed by a 
repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion, AND  
• positive CMV PCR results in both blood and urine (on the same date or on different 
dates) or in urine (on ≥2 different dates) on or after the date of seroconversion. 
This secondary efficacy endpoint will be analyzed using methods similar to those for the primary 
efficacy endpoint as described in Section 9.5.2.1.1. VE and the corresponding nominal 2-sided 
95% CI will be provided. 
Further details will be described in the SAP. 
9.5.2.2. 
Secondary Efficacy Analyses in Cytomegalovirus-Seronegative Participants 
Meeting the Endpoint of Seroconversion Due to Primary CMV Infection 
To evaluate the efficacy of [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine to reduce the frequency of urinary viral 
shedding after seroconversion, among all CMV-seronegative participants in the PP Set for 
Efficacy meeting the endpoint of seroconversion due to primary CMV infection, the number and 
percentage of participants with positive urine CMV PCR results will be summarized at each 
post-seroconversion timepoint with respect to the date of seroconversion and during the entire 
post-seroconversion time period. The 2-sided 95% Clopper-Pearson CI for the percentage will 
also be provided. The efficacy will be estimated by the difference in percentages ([AMENDMENT_A101] 
vs. placebo) and its 2-sided 95% CI, calculated using the method of Miettinen and Nurminen, at 
each post-seroconversion timepoint and during the entire post-seroconversion time period. 
Further details will be described in the SAP. 
9.5.3. 
Immunogenicity Analyses  
Immunogenicity endpoints include nAb against epithelial cell infection, nAb against fibroblast 
infection, pentamer-specific binding antibody, and gB-specific binding antibody. 
Immunogenicity endpoints will be analyzed by serostatus (CMV-seronegative, 
CMV-seropositive) and treatment group using the Immunogenicity PP Subset, unless otherwise 
specified. The SAP will describe the complete set of immunogenicity analyses, including the 
approach to sample individuals into an Immunogenicity Subset for characterizing 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-induced immunogenicity. 
Neutralizing antibody and binding antibody data will be summarized for each cohort and 
treatment group using GMT or GMC with corresponding 95% CI at each timepoint for which an 
assessment is performed, and GMFR with corresponding 95% CI at each postbaseline timepoint 


--- Page 99 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 99 
over preinjection baseline at Day 1 will be provided by study arm. Descriptive summary 
statistics including median, minimum, and maximum will also be provided. 
The number and percentage of participants with fold rise ≥2, ≥3, and ≥4 of vaccine-induced 
antibody titers and CMV-seronegative cohort participants with seroconversion to vaccine 
antigens from baseline will be provided with 2-sided 95% CI using the Clopper-Pearson method 
at each postbaseline timepoint for all assays. At a participant level, seroconversion to vaccine 
antigens from baseline is defined as a change in antigen-specific nAb or binding antibody titer 
from below the LLOQ to equal to or above the LLOQ. 
A restricted maximum likelihood-based MMRM will be used to estimate the treatment effect 
between [AMENDMENT_A101] versus placebo. The model will include all available log-transformed 
antibody titers at each postbaseline visit as the dependent variable, treatment groups, visit (as a 
class variable), and interaction of treatment group and visit as fixed effects, and participant as a 
random effect. An unstructured covariance structure will be used to model the within-participant 
errors. If the model fails to converge, a compound symmetry covariance structure will be 
considered. The degrees of freedom of the denominator will be approximated by the Kenward-
Roger method. The GLSM and corresponding 2-sided 95% CI for the antibody titers for each 
treatment group will be provided for each scheduled visit. The GLSM and corresponding 95% CI 
results in log-transformed scale estimated from the model will be back-transformed to obtain 
these estimates in the original scale. 
In addition, GMR, estimated by the ratio of GLSM and the corresponding 2-sided 95% CI, will 
be provided to assess the treatment difference between [AMENDMENT_A101] group versus placebo group 
at each visit. The analysis may adjust for the stratification factor, ie, the stratification factor may 
be included in the MMRM as a fixed effect. 
Table 6 summarizes the analysis approach for immunogenicity endpoints. 
Further details will be described in the SAP.

9.5.4. 
Safety Analyses in All Participants  
Safety analysis will be performed for the overall study population as well as separately for the 
CMV-seronegative and the CMV-seropositive participants. 
Safety endpoints include solicited local and systemic ARs collected through 7 days following 
each injection, unsolicited AEs collected through 28 days following each injection, MAAEs 
collected from Day 1 through 6 months after the last injection, AESIs collected from Day 1

through EoS, SAEs collected from time of consent through EoS. Pregnancy and pregnancy

participants for all safety endpoints. 
Number and percentage of participants with unsolicited AEs, SAEs, MAAEs, Grade 3 or higher

participation in the study, deaths, pregnancy, and pregnancy outcome data will be summarized. 
Number of events of solicited ARs, unsolicited AEs/SAEs, and MAAEs will be reported in 
summarization tables accordingly. 
For all other safety parameters, descriptive summary statistics will be provided. Further details 
will be described in the SAP.

9.5.5. 
Exploratory Analyses  
9.5.5.1. 
Cytomegalovirus Infection Kinetics in the Cytomegalovirus-Seronegative Cohort  
In participants with seroconversion due to primary CMV infection, viral kinetics will be assessed 
by the presence and quantitative viral load of CMV in blood, urine, and saliva at the 
Seroconversion Visit and subsequent scheduled visits. For participants with primary CMV 
infection, number and proportions of participants with detectable or positive CMV in blood, 
urine, or saliva; descriptive statistics of CMV quantitative viral loads within each compartment, 
as applicable, at each visit and over the sampling period, will be provided by treatment group. 
9.5.5.2. 
Cytomegalovirus Shedding in the Cytomegalovirus-Seropositive Cohort  
Cytomegalovirus shedding will be assessed within participants by determining the presence and 
quantitative viral load of CMV shedding in urine at each study visit. Data will be presented as 
proportions of participants with detectable or positive CMV in urine and corresponding 
descriptive statistics of CMV quantitative viral loads in the urine at each study visit and over the 
course of the study and reported according to treatment group. 
Further details will be described in the SAP. 
All other analyses of the exploratory endpoints will be described in the SAP before database 
lock. 
9.5.6. 
Subgroup Analyses for Cytomegalovirus-Seronegative Cohort  
To determine whether the VE is consistent across various subgroups, the VE and its 95% CI may 
be estimated using the similar model of primary endpoint analysis within each category of the 
following classification variables. 
• 
Age groups (≥16 to <18 years, ≥18 to <20 years, or ≥20 to ≤40 years) 
• 
Region (US, ex-US) 
9.5.7. 
Subgroup Analyses in Participants in Japan  
Subgroup analyses of selected key efficacy, safety, and immunogenicity endpoints will be 
carried out in participants in Japan at the End-of-Study Analysis step (Section 9.6). Such 
analyses will be descriptive in nature without any formal hypothesis testing. Details of these 
analyses will be provided in the main SAP or in a separate analysis plan.

Confidential 
Page 102 
9.6. 
Planned Analyses  
There are 2 planned inferential analyses of efficacy in this study: the Primary Analysis and the 
Final Analysis. The study will be considered to achieve its primary efficacy objective if VE for 
the primary efficacy endpoint is demonstrated at either planned inferential analysis. 
The overall Type I error rate for this study is strictly controlled at 2.5% (one-sided) with 0.5% 
allocated to the Primary Analysis and 2.0% allocated to the Final Analysis for testing the null 
hypothesis for the primary efficacy endpoint (H0). 
The Primary Analysis will be carried out when: 
1. A total of 81 cases of the primary efficacy endpoint (ie, primary CMV infection) have 
been observed across the 2 groups in the PP Set of the CMV-seronegative female cohort, 
and 
2. The median follow-up time of CMV-seronegative female participants are at least 
12 months after the third injection. 
A total of 81 primary infection cases at the Primary Analysis will provide 90% power to detect a 
VE of 70% (70% reduction in the hazard rate), rejecting the null hypothesis of H0: VE ≤25%, at 
a (one-sided) Type I error rate of 0.5%. 
If VE is demonstrated at the Primary Analysis (ie, one-sided p-value for testing the null 
hypothesis of H0: VE ≤25% is less than 0.005), there will be no further Type I error-controlled 
inferential analysis of the primary efficacy endpoint. All further/subsequent analyses of the 
primary efficacy endpoint will be considered descriptive or supportive in nature. In the situation 
that VE is demonstrated at the Primary Analysis, a Final Analysis after at least 112 primary 
efficacy endpoint cases have been observed across the 2 groups in the PP Set for Efficacy may 
be performed as a supportive analysis of the primary efficacy endpoint with longer follow-up 
time. 
In the event that VE is not demonstrated at the Primary Analysis (ie, one-sided p-value for 
testing the null hypothesis of H0: VE ≤25% is at or above 0.005), the Final Analysis will be 
carried out as an inferential analysis of efficacy when at least a total of 112 cases of the primary 
efficacy endpoint (ie, primary CMV infection) have been observed across the 2 groups in the PP 
Set for Efficacy. A total of 112 primary infection cases at the Final Analysis will provide >90% 
and approximately 90% power to detect a VE of 70% and 60%, respectively, rejecting the null 
hypothesis of H0: VE ≤25%, at a (one-sided) Type I error rate of 2.0%. 
There is no intention to stop the study early if the study achieves its primary efficacy objective 
either at the Primary Analysis or at the Final Analysis. In this case, any subsequent efficacy 
analyses performed for the primary efficacy endpoint will be considered descriptive/supportive 
in nature instead of inferential. For such descriptive/supportive analyses, VE and 95% CI will be 
provided. An End-of-Study Analysis will be carried out as a supportive analysis when all 
participants have completed 24 months of follow-up after the third injection or have discontinued 
the study. Results from this analysis will be included in a final CSR for the main study. 


--- Page 103 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc.

Confidential

9.7. 
Multiplicity  
The overall Type I error rate for this study is strictly controlled at 2.5% (one-sided) with 0.5% 
allocated to the Primary Analysis and 2.0% allocated to the Final Analysis for testing the null 
hypothesis for the primary efficacy endpoint (H0). 
No formal multiple comparison adjustments will be employed for multiple safety endpoints or 
multiple efficacy endpoints.

Abbreviations: AE = adverse event; AR = adverse reaction; CMV = cytomegalovirus; D = day; EBV = Epstein-Barr virus; eDiary = electronic diary; 
ePRO = electronic patient-reported outcomes; EQ-5D-5L = EuroQol-5 Dimension 5 Level; HIV = human immunodeficiency virus; ICF = informed consent 
form; HRPQ = Health-Related Productivity Questionnaire; [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] = Immunoglobulin G; IgM = Immunoglobulin M; M = month; MAAE = medically attended 
adverse event; min = minute; PCR = polymerase chain reaction; SAE = serious adverse event; S = study site visit; SC = safety (telephone) call. 
Note: In accordance with regulatory authority guidance, Investigators may convert some study site visits to telemedicine visits with the approval of the Sponsor.   
a. 
Safety Call Visits 3a and 7a are not required if participants are not dosed at the Visits #3 and #7, respectively. 
b. 
A full physical examination including height and weight (body mass index will be calculated) will be performed at Screening. Symptom-directed physical 
examinations will be performed at all study site visits following Screening, if warranted; on each dosing day before injection, the arm receiving the injection 
must be examined and the associated lymph nodes must be evaluated. Any clinically significant findings identified during a study visit should be reported as 
an MAAE, as appropriate. 
c. 
On days of study injection, vital signs should be collected preinjection and 30 to 45 minutes post injection. Vital sign measurements include the assessment 
of body temperature, systolic, and diastolic blood pressures, heart rate, and respiratory rate. When applicable, vital sign measurements should be performed 
before blood collection. Participants who are febrile (body temperature ≥38.0°C/100.4°F) before injection (Day 1, Day 57 [Month 2], and Day 169 


--- Page 112 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 112 
[Month 6]) must be rescheduled within the relevant window period to receive the injection. Afebrile participants with minor illnesses can be enrolled at the 
discretion of the Investigator. 
d. 
Female participants who have a positive pregnancy urine test any time during the study will not receive additional study injections but will be followed for 
safety, pregnancy outcome, and seroconversion in CMV-seronegative cohort, or CMV shedding (in the CMV-seropositive cohort and CMV-seronegative 
participants meeting the endpoint of seroconversion) (Section 8.14.6),and female participants in the CMV-seronegative and CMV-seropositive cohorts will 
be offered participation in the Infant Outcome Substudy (Section 11.6). Participants who are confirmed pregnant during the study do not need their urine 
pregnancy test performed during study visits after confirmation of and during the course of the pregnancy. Urine pregnancy test must be resumed in site 
visits after the pregnancy is complete. Cytomegalovirus-seronegative cohort participants becoming pregnant during the study will also be offered blood 
testing on a monthly basis for seroconversion due to primary CMV infection. 
e. 
On dosing days, blood sampling should be completed prior to study injection but after measurement of the pre-dose vital signs. Serum samples for 
immunogenicity may be used to test CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]. 
f. 
CMV-seronegative cohort only: Serum for CMV primary infection ([INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]) will be collected at each study visit. A CMV-seronegative cohort participant 
meets the criteria for seroconversion (Section 4.1) once confirmed by a repeat positive [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion 
(Section 8.10). If seroconversion is confirmed, serum collection for CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] does not need to be completed at subsequent visits and the participant will 
begin following the seropositive cohort procedures. On dosing days, blood sampling should be completed prior to study injection but after measurement of 
the pre-dose vital signs. An indeterminate result will be repeated per the study protocol ≥2 weeks after the date of the indeterminate result. If an 
indeterminate result represents an evolving antibody response to a primary CMV infection, the repeat test should be positive. See procedures for 
Seroconversion Visit (Section 8.10). 
g. 
CMV-seropositive participants only: Urine for CMV shedding will be collected at each study visit for participants in the CMV-seropositive cohort, or 
participants who have seroconverted from CMV-seronegative to CMV-seropositive due to primary CMV infection. On dosing days, urine sampling should 
be completed prior to study injection. 
h. 
Participants who are randomized to treatment but do not receive the first study injection on the same day will be permitted to return for the first study 
injection on Day 1 if within the 28-day Screening window. 
i. 
The participant will record entries in the eDiary approximately 30 minutes after dosing while at the study site, with instruction provided by study site staff. 
Participants will continue to record in the eDiary each day after they leave the study site, preferably in the evening, on the day of dosing and for 6 days 
following. Any solicited AR that is ongoing beyond Day 7 will be recorded until no longer reported, not exceeding 28 days. Participants will be given 
thermometers to record their temperatures and rulers to measure any injection site reactions (Section 8.14.3). 
j. 
Solicited ARs recorded in eDiaries lasting beyond 7 days post injection and any medication take to prevent or treat pain or fever recorded in eDiaries will be 
reviewed either via scheduled telephone calls or at the following study visit (Section 8.14.3). 
k. 
Trained study personnel will call all participants to collect information relating to any unsolicited AEs through 28 days post injection, MAAEs, AESIs, AEs 
leading to withdrawal, SAEs, information on concomitant medications associated with those events, and any nonstudy injections. 
l. 
All unsolicited AEs will be recorded starting the day of each injection and through 28 days following each injection. 
m. 
All concomitant medications and nonstudy injections will be recorded through 28 days after each injection; all concomitant medications relevant to or for the 
treatment of an MAAE will be recorded through 6 months after the last injection, all concomitant medications relevant to or for the treatment of an AESI 
will be recorded from Day 1 through the final study visit, and all concomitant medications relevant to or for the treatment of a SAE will be recorded from 
Screening through the final study visit. Any COVID-19 vaccine(s) taken during the period starting 28 days before the first injection and through the last 
study visit. 
n. 
CMV-seronegative cohort only: The occurrence of symptoms meeting criteria for primary CMV infection (Section 8.9) at Month 3 or later timepoint will 
also be reported. Participants reporting symptoms meeting criteria for possible primary CMV infection will have a CMV Illness Assessment Visit 
(unscheduled visit) (Section 8.9). The CMV Illness Assessment Visit will include physical examination (including vital signs); collection of blood samples 


--- Page 113 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 113 
for hematology, chemistry, seroconversion due to primary CMV infection, and EBV panel; and a urine sample for CMV PCR. At the discretion of the 
Investigator, testing for HIV antibodies, HIV viral load, and SARS-CoV-2 may be performed. In addition, participants reporting symptoms for possible 
symptomatic primary CMV infection by protocol-defined criteria may also receive ePRO questionnaires to collect information on health state and health-
related productivity as reported by the participant. The questionnaires include the EQ-5D-5L and the HRPQ, which is tr[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]ered based on potential 
symptomatic primary CMV illness symptoms. 
o. 
CMV-seronegative cohort only: Participants with seroconversion due to primary CMV infection at Month 3 or later timepoint will be asked to be seen for a 
Seroconversion Visit (unscheduled visit) (Section 8.10) for clinical assessment and blood, urine, and saliva sampling for CMV PCR, after which they will 
return to their usual visit schedule. At each scheduled visit after a positive confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test, urine will be collected for CMV PCR, serum will be 
collected for immunogenicity, and serum will no longer be collected for CMV serology (see Section 8.11). Participants who seroconvert prior to Month 3 
will not require a Seroconversion Visit, will no longer be required to have serum collected for CMV serology at subsequent planned visits, with the 
exception of Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing (see Section 8.11), and will have urine collected for CMV PCR at subsequent visits. 
p. 
For participants who seroconvert: Confirmation of seroconversion by a repeat test performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion (Section 8.11).
