X 
Abbreviations: AE = adverse event; CMV = cytomegalovirus; D = day; EBV = Epstein-Barr virus; eD = electronic diary; EoS = end-of-study; ePRO = electronic 
patient-reported outcomes; EQ-5D-5L = EuroQol-5 Dimension 5 Level; HIV = human immunodeficiency virus; HRPQ = Health-Related Productivity 
Questionnaire; M = month; MAAE = medically attended adverse event; SAE = serious adverse event; S* = study site visit or home visit. 
Note: In accordance with regulatory authority guidance, Investigators may convert some study site visits to telemedicine visits with the approval of the Sponsor.  
a. 
Symptom-directed physical examinations will be performed at all study site visits following Screening, if warranted. When the physical examination is 
performed, vital signs must be performed as well. When applicable, vital sign measurements should be performed before blood collection. 
b. 
Participants who have a positive pregnancy urine test any time during the study will not receive additional study injections but will be followed for safety, 
pregnancy outcome, and seroconversion in CMV-seronegative cohort, or CMV shedding (in the CMV-seropositive cohort and CMV-seronegative 
participants meeting the endpoint of seroconversion) (Section 8.14.6), and female participants in the CMV-seronegative and CMV-seropositive cohorts will 
be offered participation in the Infant Outcome Substudy (Section 11.6). Participants who are confirmed pregnant during the study do not need their urine 
pregnancy test performed during study visits after confirmation of and during the course of the pregnancy. Urine pregnancy test must be resumed in site 
visits after the pregnancy is complete. Cytomegalovirus-seronegative cohort participants becoming pregnant during the study will also be offered 
blood- testing on a monthly basis for seroconversion due to primary CMV infection. 
c. 
Blood sampling should be completed after measurement of vital signs. 
d. 
CMV-seronegative cohort only: Serum for CMV primary infection ([INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]) will be collected at each study visit. A CMV-seronegative cohort participant 
meets the criteria for seroconversion (Section 4.1) once confirmed by a repeat positive [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion 
(Section 8.10).If seroconversion is confirmed, serum collection for CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] does not need to be completed at subsequent visits and the participant will 


--- Page 117 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 117 
begin following the seropositive cohort procedures. Blood sampling should be completed after measurement of vital signs. An indeterminate CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] will 
be repeated per the study protocol ≥2 weeks after the date of the indeterminate result. If an indeterminate result represents an evolving antibody response to a 
primary CMV infection, the repeat test should be positive. See procedures for Seroconversion Visit (Section 8.10). 
e. 
CMV-seropositive participants only: Urine for CMV shedding will be collected at each study visit for participants in the CMV-seropositive cohort, or 
participants who have seroconverted from CMV-seronegative to CMV-seropositive due to primary CMV infection. 
f. 
Safety eDiary will prompt the participant to report occurrence of relevant safety events. If eDiary prompt results in identification of a relevant safety event, 
trained study site personnel will call the participant within 1 business day, or within 2 business days after the window for eDiary completion has closed if the 
participant did not complete the eDiary, to collect information relating to MAAEs (up to 6 months after last injection), AESIs, AEs leading to withdrawal, 
SAEs, and information on concomitant medications associated with those events. For CMV-seronegative cohort only, safety eDiary will also prompt the 
participant to report symptoms that may be consistent with symptomatic primary CMV infection. Study personnel will call the participant if symptoms 
consistent with possible primary CMV infection (see symptom criteria for possible primary CMV infection in Section 8.9) are reported, and schedule a CMV 
Illness Assessment Visit as applicable (Section 8.13). In addition, participants reporting symptoms for possible symptomatic primary CMV infection by 
protocol-defined criteria may also receive ePRO questionnaires to collect information on health state and health-related productivity as reported by the 
participant. The questionnaires include the EQ-5D-5L and the HRPQ, which is tr[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]ered based on potential symptomatic primary CMV illness symptoms. 
g. 
CMV-seronegative cohort only: The occurrence of symptoms meeting criteria for primary CMV infection (see symptom criteria for possible primary CMV 
infection in Section 8.9) at Month 3 or later timepoint will also be reported. Participants reporting symptoms meeting criteria for possible primary CMV 
infection will have a CMV Illness Assessment Visit (unscheduled visit) (Section 8.9). The CMV Illness Assessment Visit will include physical examination 
(including vital signs); collection of blood samples for hematology, chemistry, seroconversion due to primary CMV infection, and EBV panel; and a urine 
sample for CMV PCR. At the discretion of the Investigator, testing for HIV antibodies, HIV viral load, and SARS-CoV-2 may be performed. In addition, 
participants reporting symptoms for possible symptomatic primary CMV infection by protocol-defined criteria may also receive ePRO questionnaires to 
collect information on health state and health-related productivity as reported by the participant. The questionnaires include the EQ-5D-5L and the HRPQ, 
which is tr[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]ered based on the CMV illness symptoms. 
h. 
CMV-seronegative cohort only: Participants with seroconversion due to primary CMV infection at Month 3 or later timepoint will be asked to be seen for a 
Seroconversion Visit (unscheduled visit) (Section 8.10) for clinical assessment and blood, urine, and saliva sampling for CMV PCR, after which they will 
return to their usual visit schedule. At each scheduled visit after a positive confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test, urine will be collected for CMV PCR, serum will be 
collected for immunogenicity, and serum will no longer be collected for CMV serology (see Section 8.11). Participants who seroconvert prior to Month 3 
will not require a Seroconversion Visit, will no longer be required to have serum collected for CMV serology at subsequent planned visits, with the 
exception of Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing (see Section 8.11), and will have urine collected for CMV PCR at subsequent visits. Participants who seroconvert at 
the EoS Visit (Visit 31) will be asked to return to the clinic as soon as possible for a Seroconversion Visit (unscheduled visit) and will be asked to return ≥28 
days from the date of seroconversion (unscheduled visit) for confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing and urine collection. 
i. 
For participants who seroconvert: Confirmation of seroconversion by a repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion.

11.2. 
APPENDIX 2: Study Governance Considerations  
11.2.1. 
Regulatory and Ethical Considerations  
This study will be conducted in accordance with the protocol and with the following: 
• 
Consensus ethical principles derived from international guidelines including the 
Declaration of Helsinki and Council for International Organizations of Medical 
Sciences International Ethical Guidelines. 
• 
Applicable ICH GCP Guidelines. 
• 
Applicable laws and regulatory requirements. 
• 
The protocol, protocol amendments, ICFs, IBs, and other relevant documents (eg, 
advertisements) must be submitted to an IRB/IEC by the Investigator and reviewed 
and approved by the IRB/IEC before the study is initiated. 
• 
Any amendments to the protocol will require IRB/IEC approval before 
implementation of changes made to the study design, except for changes necessary to 
eliminate an immediate hazard to study participants. 
• 
The Investigator will be responsible for the following: 
− Providing written summaries of the status of the study to the IRB/IEC annually or 
more frequently in accordance with the requirements, policies, and procedures 
established by the IRB/IEC. 
− Notifying the IRB/IEC of SAEs or other significant safety findings as required by 
IRB/IEC procedures. 
− Providing oversight of the conduct of the study at the site and adherence to 
requirements of 21 CFR, ICH guidelines, the IRB/IEC, European regulation 
536/2014 for clinical studies (if applicable), and all other applicable local 
regulations. 
11.2.2. 
Study Monitoring  
Before an investigational study site can enter a participant into the study, a representative of 
[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. or its representatives will visit the investigational study site to: 
• 
Determine the adequacy of the facilities. 
• 
Discuss with the Investigator(s) and other personnel their responsibilities with regard 
to protocol adherence, and the responsibilities of [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. or its 
representatives. This will be documented in a Clinical Study Agreement between 
[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc., designated CRO, and the Investigator. 
According to ICH GCP guideline, the Sponsor of the study is responsible for ensuring the proper 
conduct of the study with regard to protocol adherence and validity of data recorded in the 
eCRFs. The study monitor’s duties are to aid the Investigator and [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. in the 
maintenance of complete, accurate, legible, well-organized, and easily retrievable data. The 
study monitor will advise the Investigator of the regulatory necessity for study-related 


--- Page 119 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 119 
monitoring, audits, IRB/IEC review, and inspection by providing direct access to the source 
data/documents. In addition, the study monitor will explain to and interpret for the Investigator 
all regulations applicable to the clinical evaluation of an IP as documented in ICH guidelines. 
It is the study monitor’s responsibility to inspect the eCRFs and source documentation 
throughout the study to protect the rights of the participants; to verify adherence to the protocol; 
to verify completeness, accuracy, and consistency of the data; and to confirm adherence of study 
conduct to any local regulations. Details will be outlined in the Clinical Monitoring Plan. During 
the study, a monitor from [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. or a representative will have regular contacts with 
the investigational site, for the following: 
• 
Provide information and support to the Investigator(s). 
• 
Confirm that facilities remain acceptable. 
• 
Confirm that the investigational team is adhering to the protocol, that the data are 
being accurately recorded in the eCRFs, and that IP accountability checks are being 
performed. 
• 
Perform source data verification. This includes a comparison of the data in the eCRFs 
with the participant’s medical records at the hospital or practice, and other records 
relevant to the study. This will require direct access to all original records for each 
participant (eg, clinical charts or electronic medical record system). 
• 
Record and report any protocol deviations not previously sent. 
• 
Confirm AEs and SAEs have been properly documented in eCRFs and those SAEs 
that met criteria for reporting have been forwarded to the IRB/IEC. 
The monitor will be available between visits if the Investigator(s) or other study site staff needs 
information or advice. 
11.2.3. 
Audits and Inspections  
[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc., their designee(s), the IRB/IEC, or regulatory authorities will be allowed to 
conduct site visits to the investigational facilities for the purpose of monitoring or inspecting any 
aspect of the study. The Investigator agrees to allow [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc., their designee(s), the 
IRB/IEC, or regulatory authorities to inspect the IP storage area, IP stocks, IP records, participant 
charts and study source documents, and other records relative to study conduct. 
Authorized representatives of [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc., a regulatory authority, and any IRB/IEC may 
visit the site to perform audits or inspections, including source data verification. The purpose of a 
Sponsor audit or inspection is to systematically and independently examine all study-related 
activities and documents to determine whether these activities were conducted, and data were 
recorded, analyzed, and accurately reported according to the protocol, ICH GCP (R2), and any 
applicable regulatory requirements. The Investigator should contact [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
immediately if contacted by a regulatory agency about an inspection. 
The Principal Investigator must obtain IRB/IEC approval for the investigation. Initial IRB/IEC 
approval, and all materials approved by the IRB/IEC for this study including the participant 
consent form and recruitment materials must be maintained by the Investigator and made 
available for inspection. 


--- Page 120 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 120 
11.2.4. 
Financial Disclosure  
The Investigator is required to provide financial disclosure information to allow the Sponsor to 
submit the complete and accurate certification or disclosure statements required under 21 CFR 54. 
In addition, the Investigator must provide the Sponsor with a commitment to promptly update 
this information if any relevant changes occur during the course of the investigation and for 
1 year following the completion of the study. 
The Sponsor, the CRO, and the study site are not financially responsible for further testing or 
treatment of any medical condition that may be detected during the Screening process. In 
addition, in the absence of specific arrangements, the Sponsor, the CRO, and the study site are 
not financially responsible for further treatment of the disease under study. 
11.2.5. 
Recruitment Procedures  
Advertisements to be used for the recruitment of study participants, and any other written 
information regarding this study to be provided to the participant should be submitted to the 
Sponsor for approval. All documents must be approved by the IRB/IEC. 
11.2.6. 
Informed Consent/Assent Process  
The informed consent document(s) must meet the requirements of 21 CFR 50, local regulations, 
ICH guidelines, Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act requirements, where 
applicable, and the IRB/IEC or study site. All consent documents will be approved by the 
appropriate IRB/IEC. For minors, depending on local legal and regulatory requirements, a 
separate assent form signed by the participant may be required in addition to, not in place of, an 
ICF that is signed by the parent/guardian/legally acceptable representative (and by an 
independent witness if required). The actual ICF used at each center may differ, depending on 
local regulations and IRB/IEC requirements. However, all versions must contain the standard 
information found in the sample ICF provided by the Sponsor. Any change to the content of the 
ICF must be approved by the Sponsor and the IRB/IEC prior to the form being used. 
If new information becomes available that may be relevant to the participant’s or participant's 
parent, guardian or legally acceptable representative’s willingness to continue participation in the 
study, this will be communicated in a timely manner. Such information will be provided via a 
revised ICF or an addendum to the original ICF. 
The Investigator or his/her representative will explain the nature of the study to the participant or 
participant’s parent, guardian, or legally authorized representative and answer all questions 
regarding the study. 
The Investigator is responsible for ensuring that the participant or the participant’s parent, 
guardian, or legally authorized representative fully understands the nature and purpose of the 
study. Information should be given in both oral and written form whenever possible. 
No participant should be obligated to participate in the study. The participant or participant’s 
parent, guardian, or legally authorized representative must be informed that participation is 
voluntary. Participants, their relatives, guardians, or (if applicable) legal representatives must be 
given ample opportunity to inquire about details of the study. The information must make clear 
that refusal to participate in the study or withdrawal from the study at any stage is without any 
prejudice to the participant’s subsequent care. 


--- Page 121 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 121 
The participant or participant’s parent, guardian, or legally authorized representative must be 
allowed sufficient time to decide whether they wish to participate. Minor participants will 
provide assent, while their parent(s) and/or legal guardian(s) will provide consent after they have 
read the informed consent/assent form and the Investigator or designee has answered any 
questions they may have about the study. 
The participant must be made aware of and give consent or assent to direct access to her source 
medical records by study monitors, auditors, the IRB/IEC, and regulatory authorities. The 
participant or participant’s parent, guardian, or legally authorized representative should be 
informed that such access will not violate participant confidentiality or any applicable 
regulations. The participant or participant’s parent, guardian, or legally authorized representative 
should also be informed that he/she is authorizing such access by signing or giving assent to the 
ICF. 
Participants under the age of majority (ie, under legal age) at the time of enrollment must provide 
written informed consent at the next study visit once turning the age of majority. 
A copy of the ICF(s) must be provided to the participant or participant’s parent, guardian, or 
legally authorized representative. 
A participant who is rescreened is not required to sign another ICF if the visit occurs within 
28 days from the previous ICF signature date. If performed >28 days from the previous ICF 
signature date, participants who are rescreened are required to sign a new ICF. 
Where permitted, and approved by the IRB/IEC, the ICF may be signed electronically via an 
electronic platform. 
11.2.7. 
Protocol Amendments  
No change or amendment to this protocol may be made by the Investigator or the Sponsor after 
the protocol has been agreed to and signed by all parties unless such change(s) or amendment(s) 
has (have) been agreed upon by the Investigator or the Sponsor. Any change agreed upon will be 
recorded in writing, and the written amendment will be signed by the Investigator and the 
Sponsor. Approval from each IRB/IEC is required prior to the implementation of an amendment, 
unless overriding safety reasons warrant immediate action, in which case the IRBs/IECs will be 
promptly notified. 
Any modifications to the protocol or the ICF, which may impact the conduct of the study, 
potential benefit of the study, or may affect participant safety, including changes of study 
objectives, study design, participant population, sample sizes, study procedures, or significant 
administrative aspects will require a formal amendment to the protocol. Such amendment will be 
released by the Sponsor, agreed by the Investigators, and approved by the relevant IRBs/IECs 
prior to implementation. A signed and dated statement that the protocol, any subsequent relevant 
amended documents and the ICF have been approved by relevant IRBs/IECs must be provided to 
the Sponsor before the study is initiated. 
Administrative changes of the protocol are minor corrections and/or clarifications that have no 
effect on the way the study is to be conducted. These administrative changes will be released by 
the Sponsor, agreed by the Investigators, and notified to the IRBs/IECs. 


--- Page 122 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 122 
11.2.8. 
Protocol Deviations  
A protocol deviation is any noncompliance either on the part of the participant, the Investigator, 
or the study site staff. As a result of deviations, corrective actions are to be developed by the site 
and implemented promptly. 
It is the responsibility of the site Investigator to use continuous vigilance to identify and report 
deviations within 10 working days of the scheduled protocol-required activity. All deviations 
must be addressed in study source documents and reported to the CRA. Protocol deviations must 
be sent to the reviewing IRB/IEC and regulatory authority per their policies. The site Investigator 
is responsible for knowing and adhering to the reviewing IRB/IEC and regulatory authority 
requirements. 
11.2.9. 
Data Protection  
Participants will be assigned a unique identifier by the Sponsor. Any participant records or 
datasets that are transferred to the Sponsor will contain the identifier only; participant names or 
any information which would make the participant identifiable will not be transferred. 
The participant must be informed that her personal study-related data will be used by the 
Sponsor in accordance with local data protection law. The level of disclosure must also be 
explained to the participant. 
The participant must be informed that her medical records may be examined by Clinical Quality 
Assurance auditors or other authorized personnel appointed by the Sponsor, by appropriate 
IRB/IEC members, and by inspectors from regulatory authorities. 
Individual participant medical information obtained as a result of this study is considered 
confidential, and disclosure to third parties is prohibited. Information will be accessible to 
authorized parties or personnel only. Medical information may be given to the participant’s 
physician or to other appropriate medical personnel responsible for the participant’s well-being. 
Each participant will be asked to complete a form allowing the Investigator to notify the 
participant’s primary health care provider of his/her participation in this study. 
All laboratory specimens, evaluation forms, reports, and other records will be identified in a 
manner designed to maintain participant confidentiality. All records will be kept in a secure 
storage area with limited access. Clinical information will not be released without the written 
permission of the participant or participant’s parent, guardian, or legally authorized 
representative, except as necessary for monitoring and auditing by the Sponsor, its designee, 
relevant regulatory authority, or the IRB/IEC. 
The Investigator and all employees and coworkers involved with this study may not disclose or 
use for any purpose other than performance of the study, any data, record, or other unpublished, 
confidential information disclosed to those individuals for the purpose of the study. Prior written 
agreement from the Sponsor or its designee must be obtained for the disclosure of any 
confidential information to other parties. 
11.2.10. 
Sample Retention and Future Biomedical Research  
Samples may be used for purposes related to this research at the direction of the Sponsor. The 
samples may be stored until the study team has determined that specimens are no longer needed 


--- Page 123 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 123 
and the decision has been made that there are no samples to be re-assayed, or up to 20 years. In 
addition, identifiable (by code) samples can be destroyed at any time at the request of the 
participant or participant’s parent, guardian, or legally authorized representative. 
11.2.11. 
Dissemination of Clinical Study Data  
[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. shares information about clinical studies and results on publicly accessible 
websites, based on international and local legal and regulatory requirements, and other clinical 
study disclosure commitments established by pharmaceutical industry associations. These 
websites include clinicaltrials.gov, European Union clinical trial register (eu.ctr), etc, as well as 
some national registries. 
In addition, results from clinical studies are required to be submitted to peer-reviewed journals 
following internal company review for accuracy, fair balance, and intellectual property. For 
those journals that request sharing of the analyzable data sets that are reported in the publication, 
interested researchers are directed to submit their request to clinicalstudydatarequest.com. 
Individual participant data and supporting clinical documents are available for request at 
clinicalstudydatarequest.com. While making information available the privacy of participants in 
clinical studies sponsored by [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. is assured. Details on data sharing criteria and 
process for requesting access can be found at this web address: clinicalstudydatarequest.com. 
11.2.12. 
Data Quality Assurance and Quality Control  
Data collection is the responsibility of the study site staff at the site under the supervision of the 
site Investigator. The Investigator is responsible for ensuring the accuracy, completeness, 
legibility, and timeliness of the data reported. 
• All participant data relating to the study will be recorded in the eCRF unless 
transmitted to the Sponsor or designee electronically (eg, laboratory data). The 
Investigator is responsible for verifying that data entries are accurate and correct by 
physically or electronically signing the eCRF. 
• The Investigator must maintain accurate documentation (source data) that supports 
the information entered in the eCRF. 
• The Investigator must permit study-related monitoring, audits, IRB/IEC review, 
regulatory agency inspections, and provide direct access to source data documents. 
• Monitoring details describing strategy (eg, risk-based initiatives in operations and 
quality such as Risk Management and Mitigation Strategies and Analytical Risk-
Based Monitoring), methods, responsibilities and requirements, including handling of 
noncompliance issues and monitoring techniques (central, remote, or on-site 
monitoring) are provided in the Monitoring Plan. 
• The Sponsor or designee is responsible for the data management of this study 
including quality checking of the data. 
• The Sponsor assumes accountability for actions delegated to other individuals (eg, 
CROs). 


--- Page 124 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 124 
• Study monitors will perform ongoing source data verification to confirm that data 
entered into the eCRF by authorized study site personnel are accurate, complete, and 
verifiable from source documents; that the safety and rights of participants are being 
protected; and that the study is being conducted in accordance with the currently 
approved protocol and any other study agreements, ICH GCP, and all applicable 
regulatory requirements. 
• Records and documents, including signed ICFs, pertaining to the conduct of this 
study must be retained by the Investigator for 2 years after study completion unless 
local regulations or institutional policies require a longer retention period. No records 
may be destroyed during the retention period without the written approval of the 
Sponsor. No records may be transferred to another location or party without written 
notification to the Sponsor. 
Quality assurance includes all the planned and systematic actions that are established to ensure 
that the clinical study is performed and the data are generated, documented (recorded), and 
reported according to ICH GCP and local/regional regulatory standards. 
A quality assurance representative from Sponsor or qualified designee, who is independent of 
and separated from routine monitoring, may periodically arrange inspections/audits of the 
clinical study by reviewing the data obtained and procedural aspects. These inspections may 
include on-site inspections/audits and source data checks. Direct access to source documents is 
required for the purpose of these periodic inspections/audits. 
11.2.13. 
Data Collection and Management  
This study will be conducted in compliance with ICH CGP guidelines. This study will also be 
conducted in accordance with the most recent version of the Declaration of Helsinki. 
This study will use electronic data collection to collect data directly from the investigational site 
using eCRFs. The Investigator is responsible for ensuring that all sections of each eCRF are 
completed promptly and correctly and that entries can be verified against any source data. 
Study monitors will perform source document verification to identify inconsistencies between 
the eCRFs and source documents. Discrepancies will be resolved in accordance with the 
principles of GCP. Detailed study monitoring procedures are provided in the Clinical Monitoring 
Plan. 
Adverse events will be coded with MedDRA. Concomitant medications will be coded using 
World Health Organization – Drug Reference List. 
11.2.14.

Source documents are original documents or certified copies, and include, but are not limited to, 
diary cards, medical and hospital records, Screening logs, informed consent/assent forms, 
telephone contact logs, and worksheets. Source documents provide evidence for the existence of 
the participant and substantiate the integrity of the data collected. Source documents are filed at 
the Investigator’s site. 
Data reported in the eCRF or entered in the eCRF that are transcribed from source documents 
must be consistent with the source documents or the discrepancies must be explained. The

11.2.15.

The Principal Investigator must maintain all documentation relating to the study for a period of 
at least 2 years after the last marketing application approval or, if not approved, 2 years 
following the discontinuance of the IP for investigation. If this requirement differs from any 
local regulations, the local regulations will take precedence unless the local retention policy is 
less than 2 years. 
If it becomes necessary for [SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. or the regulatory authority to review any 
documentation relating to the study, the Investigator must permit access to such records. No 
records will be destroyed without the written consent of the Sponsor, if applicable. It is the 
responsibility of the Sponsor to inform the Investigator when these documents no longer need to 
be retained. 
11.2.16.

If the study is prematurely terminated or suspended, the Sponsor shall promptly inform the 
Investigators, the IECs/IRBs, the regulatory authorities, and any CROs used in the study of the 
reason for termination or suspension, as specified by the applicable regulatory requirements. The 
Investigator shall promptly inform the participant and should assure appropriate participant 
therapy and/or follow-up. 
The Sponsor or designee reserves the right to close the study site or terminate the study at any 
time for any reason at the sole discretion of the Sponsor. 
The Investigator may initiate study site closure at any time, provided there is reasonable cause 
and sufficient notice is given in advance of the intended termination. 
Reasons for the early closure of a study site by the Sponsor or Investigator may include but are 
not limited to: 
• Continuation of the study represents a significant medical risk to participants. 
• Failure of the Investigator to comply with the protocol, the requirements of the 
IRB/IEC or local health authorities, the Sponsor’s procedures, or GCP guidelines. 
• Inadequate recruitment of participants by the Investigator.

11.4.1. 
Myocarditis and/or Pericarditis  
A case of suspected probable or confirmed myocarditis, pericarditis, or myopericarditis should 
be reported as an AESI even if it does not meet criteria per the CDC case definition. The event 
should also be reported as an SAE if it meets seriousness criteria. The CDC case definition is 
provided in Section 11.7 as guidance. 
An independent CEAC will review all suspected cases of myocarditis, pericarditis, and 
myopericarditis, which are reported in ongoing interventional clinical studies per the CEAC 
charter, to determine if they meet CDC criteria for “probable” or “confirmed” events 
(Section 11.7).

11.6.1. 
Introduction 
11.6.1.1. Study Rationale 
The aim of the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301a substudy is to assess CMV-related outcomes in live births of 
female participants who become pregnant during the course of the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main 
study. All objectives and endpoints in this substudy are exploratory. 
The [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study is enrolling a female population at risk for CMV infection 
and reinfection due to the enrollment requirement of close exposure to young children. Since the 
ultimate goal of developing the [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine is to prevent cCMV infection by 
establishing or enhancing preconceptional immunity against CMV in prospective mothers, this 
substudy provides a unique opportunity to collect information on infant outcomes in a maternal 
population at increased risk for CMV infection or reinfection. The objectives of the 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301a substudy are to assess all enrolled newborns for CMV shedding, assess for 
diagnoses of cCMV based on clinical records, and assess placental transfer of vaccine-induced 
antibodies in paired maternal/infant blood samples. 
Given an estimated enrollment of 6,900 (5,500 CMV-seronegative and 1,400 CMV-seropositive) 
females in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study, and based on published estimates of annual 
pregnancy incidence, live births, primary CMV infection rates in CMV-seronegative pregnant 
women, and cCMV infection rates in CMV-seronegative and CMV-seropositive pregnant 
women, it is estimated that a maximum of approximately 1,200 live births may occur during the 
course of participation in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study and the number of newborns with 
cCMV infection is expected to be very low (Figure 2). 
11.6.1.2. Background and Overview 
Cytomegalovirus is the most common infectious cause of birth defects worldwide, with an 
annual birth prevalence of cCMV infection ranging from 0.6% - 0.7% in developed countries to 
as high as 6% in the developing world (Kenneson and Cannon 2007; Lanzieri et al 2014). 
Though initial (primary) CMV infections in children and adults are rarely symptomatic, a 
pregnant mother with an active CMV infection can transmit the virus to the fetus, resulting in 
cCMV infection that can cause significant infant morbidity and lifelong disability. At highest 
risk are infants born to CMV-seronegative mothers who acquire a primary CMV infection in the 
weeks prior to or during pregnancy, with cCMV infection occurring in approximately 1/3 of 
these newborns (Fowler et al 1992; Kenneson and Cannon 2007). In comparison, the risk of 
cCMV infection in infants born to CMV-seropositive mothers is observed to be 70% to 80% 
lower due to maternal primary CMV infection and establishment of partially protective immunity 
prior to the pregnancy. Reinfection with CMV strain variants or reactivation of latent CMV 
during pregnancy are thought to account for the incomplete protection against cCMV infection 
observed in CMV-seropositive mothers (Fowler et al 1992; Adler et al 1995; Fowler et al 2003; 
Boppana et al 2001; Yamamoto et al 2010). The major source of CMV infection and reinfection 
in pregnant women is hypothesized to be contact young children, especially toddlers, whose 
saliva and urine contain high levels of CMV (Staras 2006, Cannon et al 2011). 
Congenital CMV infection in newborns can result in significant lifelong disability due to its 
effect on the developing nervous system of the fetus. Up to 15% of infants with cCMV infection 
due to maternal primary infection during pregnancy manifest symptoms at birth that include 


--- Page 135 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 135 
jaundice, hepatosplenomegaly, hematologic abnormalities, microcephaly, sensorineural hearing 
loss, chorioretinitis, or seizures. Additionally, up to 15% of newborns with cCMV infection but 
without symptoms at birth carry an increased risk for diagnoses CMV-related sequelae later in 
infancy and childhood, mainly sensorineural hearing loss (Goderis et al 2014; Fowler et al 1999; 
Fowler and Boppana 2006). In comparison, the risk of symptomatic cCMV infection due to 
maternal non-primary infection is as low as 1% and the risk of developing late sequelae is 
approximately 8% (Coppola et al 2019). Congenital CMV infection is the most common 
nongenetic cause of pediatric sensorineural hearing loss and is more common than hearing loss 
from congenital rubella infection prior to the advent of rubella vaccination 
(Kenneson and Cannon 2007; Pass and Arav-Boger 2018). 
There are limited options for women of childbearing age to prevent cCMV infection or reduce its 
complications. Administration of CMV-specific hyperimmune globulin to pregnant women with 
primary CMV infection has not proven effective (Revello et al 2014), and use of anti-CMV 
antivirals showed benefit in 1 study; however, treatment was limited to pregnant women with 
primary CMV infection in the first trimester (Shahar-Nissan et al 2020). A notable disadvantage 
of maternal interventional therapies to prevent cCMV is that they rely on active surveillance for 
CMV infection during pregnancy, which is not endorsed practice in obstetric care due to 
feasibility. Antiviral treatment of neonates with cCMV infection is reserved for severely 
symptomatic infants due to drug-induced toxicity and is not endorsed for asymptomatic infants, 
premature infants, or infants over 1 month old, which account for the majority of children at risk 
for development of late-onset hearing loss (Chiopris et al 2020). Lastly, it is important to note 
that the extent and severity of cCMV infection sequelae in children who are asymptomatic at 
birth is likely underestimated due to lack of universal newborn CMV Screening 
(Kadambari et al 2020; Fowler and Boppana 2018). 
There is no approved modality to prevent CMV infections in women of childbearing age, and in 
2000, the US Institute of Medicine recognized this important medical need by designating the 
development of a vaccine for the prevention of CMV infection as one of the highest (Level 1) 
public health priorities (Institute of Medicine 2000). 
This study will be conducted in compliance with the protocol, GCP, and all applicable regulatory 
requirements. 
11.6.2. 
Objectives and Endpoints  
The objectives that will be evaluated in this substudy are exploratory and endpoints associated 
with each objective are provided in Table 17. All female participants who become pregnant 
during the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study will be offered enrollment in this substudy.

transfer of vaccine-induced pentamer-specific 
and gB-specific [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] in live births of participants 
who were CMV-seronegative at enrollment. 
Newborn: maternal ratio of pentamer-specific 
and gB-specific binding antibody titers and nAb 
titers in paired samples of maternal blood 
obtained ≤72 hours of delivery and newborn 
cord blood or venous blood obtained ≤72 hours 
of delivery.

11.6.3. 
Substudy Design  
This substudy of [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 aims to assess occurrence and severity of clinically 
diagnosed cCMV, CMV shedding, and [AMENDMENT_A101] immunogenicity dynamics in participants 
becoming pregnant during the course of participation in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 and their newborns. 
The parent study is [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301: A Phase 3, randomized, observer-blind, 
placebo-controlled study to evaluate the efficacy, safety, and immunogenicity of [AMENDMENT_A101] 
CMV vaccine against primary CMV infection in healthy participants 16 to 40 years of age. The 
primary objectives of [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 are to demonstrate the efficacy of [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine 
against primary CMV infection in CMV-seronegative female participants, and to evaluate the 
safety and reactogenicity of [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine when administered on a 3-dose injection 
schedule in all participants. 
This substudy may enroll all participants who have received at least 1 study injection in the 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study and become pregnant at any point during study participation with 
plans to carry the pregnancy to term. Pregnancy is defined as a positive urine pregnancy test 
obtained during the course of participation in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study. All participants 
who become pregnant during participation in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study will not receive 
any further study injections but will continue to be followed per the main protocol for safety, 
pregnancy outcome, immunogenicity, seroconversion due to primary CMV infection 
(CMV-seronegative participants), CMV shedding (CMV-seropositive participants and 
CMV-seronegative participants meeting the endpoint of seroconversion), and will be offered in 
the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301a substudy. In addition, as part of the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study, 
pregnant CMV-seronegative participants will have the option of returning to the study site more 
frequently (on a monthly basis) to have blood testing for seroconversion due to primary CMV 
infection. If a CMV-seronegative pregnant participant has a seroconversion due to primary CMV 
infection, as determined by a positive [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] result for serum for CMV primary infection, the 
participant will no longer have monthly serum collected CMV serology ([INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]) at study visits, 
with the exception of Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing (Section 8.11). 
There are no randomization procedures in this substudy. All study site staff, the CRO blinded 
team, and the Sponsor will remain blinded to individual treatment assignments. 
The duration of participation may begin from the time the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 participant meets 
the definition of pregnancy and provides consent and is determined to be eligible for 
participation in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301a substudy, through 6 weeks after delivery. Participation 
in this substudy may extend beyond the EoS Visit on [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 (parent study) if the 
delivery date is less than 6 weeks from the EoS Visit or occurs after the EoS Visit. 
Up to approximately 1,200 participants and their infants are anticipated to be eligible for 
participation in this substudy. Participants will provide individual consent to each of the substudy 
procedures for themselves and their infant. 
Substudy procedures may include the following: 
1. Newborn sampling of urine and saliva on 1 occasion within 3 weeks after delivery. 
2. Request for and review of participant and/or infant medical records. 
3. If within the operational capacity of the participant’s study site, collection of 1 set of 
paired samples* of maternal venous blood obtained ≤72 hours of delivery and newborn 


--- Page 138 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 138 
cord blood or newborn venous blood (if cord blood is not collected) obtained ≤72 hours 
of delivery. If collection of cord blood and/or newborn venous blood is within the 
operational capacity of the study site, regardless of whether a participant refuses or 
accepts these tests, participation is allowed in the Infant Outcome Substudy. 
*Maternal sample and newborn sample do not need to be collected at the same time as 
long as both are taken ≤72 hours of delivery. 
This substudy will be conducted in compliance with the protocol, GCP, and all applicable 
regulatory requirements. 
11.6.4. 
Study Population  
Approximately 1,200 participants who become pregnant during the course of participation in the 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study and their infants will be enrolled. 
Prospective approval of protocol deviations to recruitment and enrollment criteria, also known as 
protocol waivers or exemptions, are not permitted. 
11.6.4.1. Inclusion Criteria  
Participants are eligible to be included in the substudy if all the following criteria apply: 
I1. [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study participant who has received at least 1 study injection with 
positive urine or serum pregnancy test who is either CMV-seronegative or 
CMV-seropositive. 
I2. Participant plans to carry the pregnancy to term. 
I3. Provision of written informed consent. 
I4. Agrees to provide contact information for obstetrician, and pediatrician for infant as soon 
as available, and release of medical records, as applicable. 
11.6.4.2. Exclusion Criteria  
There are no exclusion criteria for the substudy. 
11.6.5. 
Study Intervention  
No Study Intervention will be administered in the substudy. 
11.6.5.1. Discontinuation of Study Intervention and Participant 
Discontinuation/Withdrawal  
Not applicable. 
11.6.6. 
Study Assessments and Procedures  
The following study assessments and procedures may be completed for participants in the 
substudy: 
1. Urine pregnancy test (if a positive urine pregnancy test is not documented within the 
main [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study or other medical records). 


--- Page 139 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 139 
2. Newborn sampling of urine and saliva for CMV PCR using a research-use only assay 
on 1 occasion within 3 weeks after delivery. These samples may be collected either at 
the birth facility or in the study clinic, as appropriate (see Figure 3). Newborn urine 
samples will be collected using a urine bag if performed at the study clinic. Saliva 
samples will be collected at least 90 minutes after the last breastfeeding using an oral 
swab. The Principal Investigator will immediately refer the participant and her infant 
to the participant’s pediatrician and inform the participant’s obstetrician if any infant 
urine sample returns a positive CMV PCR result. Any such positive CMV PCR 
results from the newborn urine should be confirmed outside of the study by their 
clinician with a CMV PCR assay which has been approved by a local regulatory body 
during their clinical evaluation. 
A clinical diagnosis of cCMV infection and disease will be based on clinical 
assessment and diagnosis documented in infant ± participant medical records. 
3. Request for and review of participant and/or infant medical records if any of the 
following occur or are reported: 
a. infants with positive urine CMV PCR results from samples taken within 3 weeks after 
delivery (as above); 
b. congenital anomaly or infant abnormalities reported on the Pregnancy Report Form 
completed as part of the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study; 
c. infants born to CMV-seronegative participants who meet the endpoint of 
seroconversion due to primary CMV infection prior to or during pregnancy. 
Medical records will be reviewed for criteria supporting the diagnosis of cCMV 
infection and disease. 
4. If within the operational capability of the participant’s study site, collection of 1 set of 
paired samples of maternal blood obtained ≤72 hours of delivery and newborn cord 
blood or newborn venous blood obtained ≤72 hours of delivery. Immunogenicity 
assessments of these samples may include: 
a. Serum binding antibody levels to the pentamer and gB vaccine antigens as measured 
by ELISA. 
b. Serum functional antibody levels to the pentamer and gB vaccine antigens as 
measured by nAb titer against epithelial cell infection and nAb titer against fibroblast 
infection. 
11.6.6.1. Safety Oversight  
Safety data collected on pregnancies and birth outcomes will be included in the periodic reviews 
of safety by the DSMB in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main protocol. 
If any CMV-seronegative participant becomes pregnant and also has seroconversion due to 
primary CMV infection in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study, the study site Investigator will 
inform the participant’s obstetrician and/or physician as soon as possible and every effort will be 
made to assure that the participant receives appropriate evaluation, counseling, and obstetric 
follow-up regardless of whether they participate in this substudy.

11.6.6.2. Efficacy and Immunogenicity Assessments  
No assessment of clinical efficacy will be performed in this study. All objectives in this substudy 
are exploratory. 
11.6.6.3. Safety Assessments  
Safety will be assessed as described in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main protocol. 
11.6.6.4. Pharmacokinetics  
Pharmacokinetic parameters are not evaluated in this study. 
11.6.6.5. Pharmacodynamics  
Pharmacodynamic parameters are not evaluated in this study.

Biomarkers are not evaluated in this study. 
11.6.7. 
Statistical Considerations  
11.6.7.1. Statistical Hypotheses  
No hypotheses will be tested. All analyses will be descriptive. 
11.6.7.2. Sample Size Determination  
The sample size of this substudy is not driven by statistical assumptions for formal hypothesis 
testing. 
11.6.7.3. Populations for Analyses  
The exploratory analyses will be based on the FAS as described in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main 
protocol. 
11.6.7.4. Statistical Analyses  
11.6.7.4.1. Exploratory Analyses  
The exploratory analyses will be based on the FAS as described in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main 
protocol (Section 9.4) and reported by treatment group assignment. Data in the neonate(s) will be 
reported by treatment group assignment of the (participant) mother. 
The endpoint of positive CMV PCR of newborn saliva and urine will be assessed by 
documentation of positive results as measured by CMV oral swab (saliva) and CMV viral load 
(urine). 


--- Page 141 ---

[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 141 
The endpoint of presence or absence of clinically diagnosed cCMV infection will be determined 
by review of infant ± participant medical records based on the following criteria 
(Lazzarotto 2020): 
• 
Neonatal CMV PCR in saliva or urine collected in the first 3 weeks of life 
-- or -- 
• 
In cases of CMV-seronegative participant seroconversion due to primary CMV infection during 
pregnancy, a positive CMV PCR in amniotic fluid after 20 weeks and more than 8 weeks after 
presumed onset of maternal primary infection 
The endpoint of presence or absence of cCMV disease will be based on review of 
infant ± participant medical records for documentation of the following signs and symptoms 
(Luck 2017): 
Clinically detectable symptoms/signs 
Physical Examination 
• 
Small for gestational age (birth weight <-2 SD for gestational age) 
• 
Microcephaly (head circumference <-2 SD for gestational age) 
• 
Petechiae or purpura (usually found within hours of birth and persist for several weeks) 
• 
Blueberry muffin rash (intra-dermal hematopoiesis) 
• 
Jaundice* 
• 
Hepatomegaly 
• 
Splenomegaly 
Neurologic physical examination 
• 
Microcephaly (head circumference <-2 SD for gestational age) 
• 
Neurologic signs (lethargy, hypotonia, seizures, poor sucking reflex) 
Abnormalities detected incidentally or through subsequent investigation/specialist examination 
Laboratory results 
• 
Anemia 
• 
Thrombocytopenia (occurs in the first week but platelets often increase spontaneously after the second 
week) 
• 
Leukopenia, isolated neutropenia 
• 
Elevated liver enzymes (ALT/AST) 
• 
Conjugated hyperbilirubinemia 
Cerebrospinal fluid 
• 
Abnormal cerebral fluid indices, positive CMV DNA 
Neuroimaging 
• 
Calcifications, peri ventricular cysts, ventricular dilatation, subependymal pseudocysts, germinolytic 
cysts, white matter abnormalities, cortical atrophy, migration disorders, cerebellar hypoplasia, 
lenticulostriatal vasculopathy 
Hearing test 
• 
Sensorineural hearing loss uni- or bilaterally 
Visual examination 
• 
Chorioretinitis, retinal hemorrhage, optic atrophy, strabismus, cataracts 
Abbreviations: ALT = alanine aminotransferase; AST = aspartate aminotransferase; CMV = cytomegalovirus; 
SD = standard deviations. 
*CMV-associated jaundice can be present at the first day after birth and usually persists longer than physiologic 
jaundice. 


--- Page 142 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 142 
The endpoint of cCMV disease severity will be determined by review of infant ± participant 
medical records based on the following criteria (Rawlinson et al 2017): 
Moderately to severely symptomatic cCMV disease  
• 
Multiple manifestations attributable to cCMV infection: thrombocytopenia, petechiae, hepatomegaly, 
splenomegaly, intrauterine growth restriction, hepatitis (raised transaminases or bilirubin), or  
• 
Central nervous system involvement such as microcephaly, radiographic abnormalities consistent with 
cytomegalovirus central nervous system disease (ventriculomegaly, intracerebral calcifications, 
periventricular echogenicity, cortical or cerebellar malformations), abnormal cerebrospinal fluid indices 
for age, chorioretinitis, sensorineural hearing loss, or the detection of cytomegalovirus DNA in 
cerebrospinal fluid  
Mildly symptomatic cCMV disease  
• 
Might occur with one or 2 isolated manifestations of cCMV infection that are mild and transient (eg, mild 
hepatomegaly, or a single measurement of low platelet count, or raised levels of alanine aminotransferase). 
These might overlap with more severe manifestations. However, the difference is that they occur in 
isolation  
Asymptomatic cCMV infection with isolated sensorineural hearing loss  
• 
No apparent abnormalities to suggest cCMV disease, but sensorineural hearing loss (≥21 decibels)  
Asymptomatic cCMV infection  
• 
No apparent abnormalities to suggest cCMV disease, and normal hearing 
The endpoint of newborn-to-maternal antibody titer ratios will be calculated for each set of 
paired samples of cord serum:maternal serum or newborn serum:maternal serum. The antibody 
titer ratios may include pentamer-specific binding antibody, gB-specific binding antibody, nAb 
against epithelial cell infection, or nAb against fibroblast infection. 
Further details will be described in the SAP of the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main protocol. 
11.6.7.4.2. Safety Analyses  
No additional safety analysis is planned in this substudy. Safety data related to pregnancy will be 
collected as a part of safety monitoring and evaluation in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main protocol. 
11.6.7.5. Interim Analyses  
There is no planned IA for this substudy. Findings from this substudy will be included in an 
addendum to the CSR.

11.8. 
APPENDIX 8: Contraceptive Guidance  
The following definitions of WOCBP and birth control methods are based on the 
Recommendations Related to Contraception and Pregnancy Testing in Clinical Trials 
Version 1.1 (CTFG 2020) established by the CTFG. 
11.8.1. 
Definition of Women of Childbearing Potential and Fertile Men  
A woman is a WOCBP, ie, fertile, following menarche and until becoming postmenopausal, 
unless permanently sterile. Permanent sterilization methods include hysterectomy, bilateral 
salpingectomy, and bilateral oophorectomy. 
A postmenopausal state is defined as no menses for 12 months without an alternative medical 
cause. A high FSH level in the postmenopausal range may be used to confirm a postmenopausal 
state in women not using hormonal contraception or hormonal replacement therapy; however, in 
the absence of 12 months amenorrhea, a single FSH measurement is insufficient. 
A man in considered fertile after puberty unless permanently sterile by bilateral orchidectomy. 
11.8.2. 
Birth Control Methods  
11.8.2.1. Birth Control Methods that may be Considered as Highly Effective  
Methods that can achieve a failure rate of less than 1% per year when used consistently and 
corrected are considered as highly effective birth control methods. Such methods include: 
• 
Combined (estrogen and progestogen containing) hormonal contraception associated 
with inhibition of ovulation: 
− Oral 
− Intravaginal 
− Transdermal 
• 
Progestogen-only hormonal contraception associated with inhibition of ovulation: 
− Oral 
− Injectable 
− Implantable 
• 
Intrauterine device 
• 
Intrauterine hormone-releasing system 
• 
Bilateral tubal occlusion 
• 
Vasectomized partner (vasectomized partner is a highly effective birth control method 
provided that partner is the sole sexual partner of the WOCBP study participant and 
that the vasectomized partner has received medical assessment of the surgical 
success) 
• 
Sexual abstinence (sexual abstinence is considered a highly effective birth control 
method only if defined as refraining from heterosexual intercourse during the entire 


--- Page 149 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 149 
period of risk associated with the study treatments. The reliability of sexual 
abstinence needs to be evaluated in relation to the duration of the clinical study and 
the preferred and usual lifestyle of the participant. 
11.8.2.2. Acceptable Birth Control Methods that may not be Considered as Highly 
Effective  
Acceptable birth control methods that result in a failure rate of more than 1% per year include: 
• 
Progestogen-only oral hormonal contraception, where inhibition of ovulation is not 
the primary mode of action 
• 
Male or female condom with or without spermicide 
• 
Cap, diaphragm, or sponge with spermicide 
A combination of a male condom with either a cap, diaphragm, or sponge with spermicide 
(double barrier methods) are also considered acceptable, but not highly effective, birth control 
methods. 
11.8.2.3. Birth Control Methods that are Considered Unacceptable  
Periodic abstinence (calendar, symptothermal, or postovulation methods), withdrawal (coitus 
interruptus), spermicides only, and lactational amenorrhea method are not acceptable methods of 
contraception. A female and male condom should not be used together. 
See Section 11.10.1.1 for country-specific requirements regarding contraception requirements for 
participants in Japan.

11.9.1. 
Introduction  
11.9.1.1. Study Rationale  
The purpose of this Phase 3 Extension Substudy is to assess the longer-term immunogenicity, 
efficacy, and safety of the 100µg dose level of [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccine against primary CMV 
infection in healthy females 16 to 40 years of age who were CMV-seronegative at Baseline of 
the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study (including participants who remain CMV-seronegative upon 
entry into the Extension Substudy AND participants who seroconverted during the main study). 
This Extension Substudy will also evaluate the immune persistence and safety of [AMENDMENT_A101] in 
a subset (approximately 360) of female participants who were CMV-seropositive at Baseline of 
the main study. 
All participants who enter the Extension Substudy must have completed the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 
main study including the follow-up period up to Month 30. Therefore, the main study plus the 
Extension Substudy will provide a total of approximately 4 years of immunogenicity data post 
final injection in the P301 study. 
11.9.1.2. Background and Overview  
Refer to Section 2.2.

11.9.3. 
Extension Substudy Design  
This is a Phase 3, long-term extension substudy in participants who completed 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study. All consenting participants in the CMV-seronegative group at 
Baseline who completed the final study visit in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study are potentially 
eligible to enroll. A subset of the CMV-seropositive group (approximately 360 participants) from 
the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study who complete the final study visit and received all 3 study 
injections within window per-protocol in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study will also be 
potentially eligible to enroll. 
The following eligible participants from [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study will be enrolled in the 
Extension Substudy: 


--- Page 153 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 153 
• 
Females who were seronegative at Baseline and did not seroconvert during 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study, received at least one study injection during the main 
study, and did not withdraw study consent. 
• 
Females who were seronegative at Baseline and seroconverted during the 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study, received at least one study injection during the main 
study, and did not withdraw study consent. 
• 
A subset of approximately 360 females who were seropositive at Baseline and 
received all 3 study injections in a 0-, 2-, and 6-month schedule and within window 
per-protocol, and did not withdraw study consent. 
This Extension Substudy will start to enroll eligible participants while the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 
main study is ongoing. To maintain the integrity of [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study, study blind 
will be maintained until after [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study is fully unblinded. Refer to 
Section 11.9.5.1 and Section 11.9.5.2 for details. CMV serostatus for the CMV-seronegative 
cohort will be determined at the EoS Visit of [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study by a negative result 
for serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] as measured by a platform-based automated immunoassay based on at least 1 of 
the 4 recombinant CMV antigens not encoded by [AMENDMENT_A101] (pp150, pp28, pp52, pp38). 
Extension Substudy Assessments: 
CMV-seronegative cohort:  
• Serum will be collected to assess for seroconversion every 6 months for 2 years after the 
final study visit in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study from the signing of ICF for P301-EXT 
through EoES. 
• CMV-seronegative participants with seroconversion during the Extension Substudy due 
to primary CMV infection will no longer be required to have serum collected for CMV 
serology ([INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]) at subsequent planned visits through EoES, with the exception of 
Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing and immunogenicity testing. 
• At the time of seroconversion, participants will return for a seroconversion visit with 
blood and urine collection for CMV PCR and then follow the schedule of assessments for 
the CMV-seroconverter cohort (Table 24). 
CMV-seroconverter cohort:  
• CMV-seroconverters from the main study will have urine collected every 3 months for 
CMV PCR from signing ICF for P301-EXT through EoES. 
• Participants who seroconvert during P301-EXT will begin urine PCR collection at the 
next scheduled study visit following seroconversion and will continue at all subsequent 
scheduled visits every 3 months. 
All participants will also be assessed for safety, including all deaths, AEs leading to study 
discontinuation, and all SAEs throughout the Substudy P301-EXT from signing of ICF through 
EoES. Serum will be collected in all participants to measure immune persistence of antigen-
specific neutralizing antibody and binding antibody titers or concentrations in all or a subset of 
participants every 6 months for 2 years after the final study visit in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main

study from signing informed consent for P301-EXT through EoES. The selection of the subset 
will be detailed in the SAP and/or a separate immunogenicity sampling plan. 
A detailed overview of procedures and visits for the Extension Substudy can be found in the SoA

11.9.4. 
Substudy Population  
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study is projected to enroll a total of approximately 6,900 participants 
(5,500 CMV-seronegative and 1,400 CMV-seropositive). However, it is anticipated that only a 
subset of these participants will be eligible for the Extension Substudy. Assuming either 20% or 
25% of the participants in each CMV serostatus group in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study are 
ineligible for Substudy P301-EXT (either did not complete the final study visit in 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study, did not receive all 3 study injections [CMV-seropositive 
participants], or did not otherwise meet the eligibility criteria for Substudy P301-EXT), the 
expected number of participants eligible for the Extension Substudy can be found in 
Section 11.9.8.5. All consenting participants in the CMV-seronegative group at Baseline who 
completed the final study visit in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study are potentially eligible to enroll. 
The exact sample size of CMV-seronegative participants in Substudy P301-EXT will depend on 
how many are eligible and, among them, how many consent to participate. Approximately 360 
eligible and consenting participants who were CMV-seropositive at Baseline of the main study 
will be enrolled in Substudy P301-EXT; this sample size is considered sufficient to provide a 
descriptive summary of the longer-term immunogenicity and safety of [AMENDMENT_A101] in CMV-
seropositive participants. 
11.9.4.1. Inclusion Criteria  
Note: The numbering of the inclusion criteria is continued from [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main 
study. 
Participants are eligible to be included in the Extension Substudy if all the following criteria 
apply: 
10. All consenting participants who were CMV-seronegative at Baseline in the mRNA-
1647-P301 main study (including those who did seroconvert and did not seroconvert 
during the main study), received at least one study injection in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 
main study but did not withdraw study consent, and completed the final study visit in 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study. 
11. Consenting participants in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study who were CMV-
seropositive at Baseline, received all 3 study injections in a 0-, 2-, and 6-month 
schedule and within window per-protocol, did not withdraw study consent, and 
completed the final study visit in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study. 
12. According to the assessment of the Investigator, is capable of complying with study 
procedures. 
13. Willingness to comply with study procedures and provide written informed consent.
