11.9.4.2. Exclusion Criteria  
Note: The numbering of the exclusion criteria is continued from [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main 
study. 
Participants are excluded from the study if any of the following criteria apply: 
11. Receipt of any CMV vaccine other than [AMENDMENT_A101]. 
12. Diagnosis or condition that, in the judgment of the Investigator, may affect participant 
safety, assessment of safety endpoints, assessment of immune response, or adherence 
to study procedures, including any medical, psychiatric, or occupational condition 
that, in the opinion of the Investigator, might pose additional risk due to participation 
in the study or could interfere with the interpretation of study results. 
11.9.5. 
Substudy Intervention  
No interventional vaccine is administered in this extension study. Refer to main Study 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301, Section 6.1 for any study intervention details. The [AMENDMENT_A101] injection 
administered in that study utilized an mRNA platform for IM delivery of mRNA, encoding target 
antigens in a lipid nanoparticle formulation, composed of SM-102, cholesterol, DSPC, and 
PEG2000-DMG. 
11.9.5.1. Assignment to Study Intervention  
While no intervention will be administered in this Extension Substudy, the randomization 
assignments from [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study will be maintained and blinding preserved. This 
Extension Substudy will start to enroll eligible participants while the Phase 3 pivotal 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study is ongoing. To maintain the integrity of the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 
main study, the Investigators, study site staff, site monitors, participants, Sponsor, and CRO 
personnel will remain blinded (with respect to the treatment assignments of participants in 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study) until after [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study is fully unblinded, with 
the exception of prespecified CRO and Sponsor team members, who will be unblinded to the 
interim results from the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study and/or Substudy P301-EXT (if 
applicable). 
11.9.5.2. Unblinding Procedures  
In case of an emergency, the Investigator has the responsibility for determining whether 
unblinding of a participant’s intervention assignment (in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study) is 
warranted. Participant safety must always be the first consideration in making such a 
determination. If the Investigator decides that unblinding is warranted, they should contact the 
Sponsor to discuss the situation prior to unblinding a participant’s intervention assignment, 
unless this could delay the participant’s emergency treatment. If a participant’s intervention 
assignment is unblinded, the Sponsor must be notified within 24 hours of this occurrence. 
The Investigator will be responsible for documenting the time, date, reason for unblinding, and 
the names of the personnel involved. The Investigator (or designee) will have access to unblind 
participants within IRT. All unblinding events will be tracked via an audit trail in the IRT and 
documented in the final study report. 


--- Page 156 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 156 
If unblinding should occur (by either accidental unblinding or emergency unblinding) before 
completion of the study, the Investigator must contact the Sponsor within 24 hours and document 
the circumstances on the appropriate forms. 
11.9.5.3. Participant Discontinuation/Withdrawal from Study  
Participants who are withdrawn from the study will not be replaced. 
From an analysis perspective, a “withdrawal” from the study refers to a situation wherein a 
participant does not return for the final visit foreseen in the protocol. 
All data collected until the date of withdrawal or last contact of the participant will be used for 
the analysis. 
A participant is considered a “withdrawal” from the study when no study procedure has 
occurred, no follow-up has been performed, and no further information has been collected for 
that participant from the date of withdrawal or last contact. 
Investigators will attempt (eg, 3 telephone calls) to contact those participants who do not return 
for scheduled visits or follow-up. 
Information relative to the withdrawal will be documented in the eCRF. The Investigator will 
document whether the decision to withdraw a participant from the study was made by the 
participant or by the Investigator as well as which of the following was the primary reason for 
withdrawal: 
• 
AE (including SAE) 
• 
Death 
• 
LTFU (Section 11.9.5.4) 
• 
Physician decision (specify) 
• 
Pregnancy (Section 11.9.6.9) 
• 
Protocol deviation (specify) 
• 
Study terminated by Sponsor 
• 
Withdrawal of consent by participant (specify) 
• 
Other (specify) 
Participants who are withdrawn from the study because of SAEs/AEs must be clearly 
distinguished from participants who are withdrawn for other reasons. Investigators will follow-
up with participants who are withdrawn from the study as result of an SAE or AE until resolution 
of the event. 
If a participant withdraws from the study, she may request destruction of any samples taken and 
not tested, and the Investigator must document this in the site study records. 
If the participant withdraws consent for disclosure of future information, the Sponsor may retain 
and continue to use any data collected before such a withdrawal of consent. 
The Sponsor will continue to retain and use all research results that have already been collected 
for the study evaluation. All biological samples that have already been collected may be retained 


--- Page 157 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 157 
and analyzed at a later date (or as permitted by local regulations) unless the participant has 
requested for them to be destroyed. 
11.9.5.4. Lost to Follow-up  
A participant will be considered LTFU if she repeatedly fails to return for scheduled visits 
without stating an intention to withdraw consent and is unable to be contacted by the study site. 
The following actions must be taken if a participant fails to return to the clinic for a required 
study visit: 
• 
The study site must attempt to contact the participant and reschedule the missed visit 
as soon as possible, counsel the participant on the importance of maintaining the 
assigned visit schedule and ascertain whether the participant wishes to and/or should 
continue in the study. 
• 
Before a participant is deemed LTFU, the Investigator or designee must make every 
effort to regain contact with the participant (where possible, 3 telephone calls and, if 
necessary, a certified letter to the participant’s last known mailing address or local 
equivalent methods). These contact attempts (eg, dates of telephone calls and 
registered letters) should be documented in the participants’ study record. 
• 
Should the participant continue to be unreachable, she will be considered to have 
withdrawn from the study for reason of LTFU. 
• 
A participant should not be considered LTFU until due diligence has been completed. 
Date of withdrawal/LTFU should be the date of last contact with the participant 
where safety status of the participant was assessed (eg, study visit, telephone call). 
11.9.6. 
Substudy Assessments and Procedures  
11.9.6.1. Screening Visit  
Screening for the P301-EXT study may be conducted any time after the informed consent is 
signed. For the CMV-seronegative cohort and CMV-seropositive subset, screening may occur 
between M30 (End-of-Study visit in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study) and M36 (Visit 1 of 
P301-EXT). For the CMV-seroconverter cohort, screening may occur between M30 and M33 
(Visit 1a of P301-EXT). 
Screening procedures will be performed as outlined in the SoA-Extension Substudy (Table 23). 
All inclusion and exclusion criteria described in Section 11.9.4.1 and Section 11.9.4.2 
respectively, must be met before participants are considered enrolled.  
Demographic data will be captured from [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study data. 
Medical history will be updated to include any history or AE not previously recorded for 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study up until Extension Substudy ICF signature. 
Symptom-directed physical examination and vital signs will be performed as needed. 


--- Page 158 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 158 
11.9.6.2. Enrollment  
Enrollment will occur after eligibility is determined. 
11.9.6.3. Scheduled Follow-up Visits  
Scheduled visits will occur every 3 or 6 months. Concomitant medications and nonstudy 
vaccinations will be reviewed as outlined in Section 11.9.7, a symptom-directed physical exam 
and vital signs may be performed if indicated, AEs will be reviewed as outlined in 
Section 11.9.6.8, and serum will be collected for seroconversion (seronegative cohort only) and 
immunogenicity every 6 months (Table 23).  
CMV-seronegative participants with seroconversion due to primary CMV infection, as 
determined by a positive [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] result, will no longer be required to have serum collected for CMV 
serology ([INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]) at subsequent planned visits through EoES, with the exception of Confirmatory 
[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing (see Section 11.9.6.4). CMV-seronegative participants with an indeterminate [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] 
result for primary CMV infection will require repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing (Section 11.9.6.4 and 
Section 11.9.6.12). Participants in the CMV-seronegative cohort will be informed if antibody 
testing demonstrates seroconversion due to primary CMV infection. 
Participants who seroconverted during the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study will begin urine PCR 
collection at the start of the Extension Substudy and will continue to have urine PCR collected at 
every scheduled Extension Substudy visit (ie, Month 33, 36, 39, 42, 45, 48, 51, and 54). 
Participants who seroconvert during the Extension Substudy will begin urine PCR collection at 
the next scheduled study visit following seroconversion and will continue at all subsequent 
scheduled visits. Urine PCR collection is aligned with the predefined Extension Study visit 
schedule and is not based on a rolling 3-month interval from the date of seroconversion 
(Table 24). 
Starting at screening and reinforced at each subsequent visit, participants will be reminded of the 
symptoms for possible primary CMV infection and counseled to call the study site should they 
have any symptoms meeting criteria. At each study visit, participants will be asked if they have 
had any symptoms of possible primary CMV infection since their last visit and their symptoms 
will be recorded. 
Possible symptoms meeting clinical criteria for possible primary CMV infection is defined as an 
illness reported by the participant consisting of at least 2 of the following symptoms: fever 
≥ 38°C/100.4°F, myalgia, moderate to severe fatigue, sore throat/pharyngitis, or cervical 
lymphadenopathy in the absence of respiratory symptoms, (eg, nasal congestion, runny nose, 
cough). 
Starting at screening and continuing at each subsequent visit, participants will also be asked if 
they have had a positive pregnancy test or become pregnant since their last visit. All reported 
positive pregnancy tests or confirmed pregnancies will be recorded and participants will continue 
to be followed as per SoA-Extension Substudy (Table 23). All pregnancies will be followed for 
outcome, including spontaneous or voluntary termination, details of the birth, and the presence or 
absence of any birth defects, congenital abnormalities, or maternal and/or newborn 
complications. Pregnancy and infant outcome data may be collected beyond EoES (ie, for 
pregnancies continuing beyond EoES visit). Sites will be trained to obtain any records to confirm 
the reported outcomes, where records are available. 


--- Page 159 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 159 
11.9.6.4. Seroconversion Visit (Unscheduled Visit) in Seronegative Cohort  
Participants in the CMV-seronegative cohort with seroconversion due to primary CMV infection, 
as determined by a positive [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] result for serum for CMV primary infection collected at a 
scheduled or unscheduled study visit during the extension substudy, will be asked to return to the 
clinic as soon as possible for a Seroconversion Visit (unscheduled visit). This visit will include 
clinical assessments, blood, and urine sampling for CMV PCR, after which they will return to 
their usual visit schedule, with the exception of confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing and immunogenicity 
samples. At each scheduled visit after the Seroconversion Visit through the EoES, urine will be 
collected for CMV PCR and serum will no longer be collected for CMV serology, with the 
exception of Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing (see Section 11.9.6.5). 
11.9.6.5. Confirmatory CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] Testing  
Participants who seroconvert will have a repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed as soon as practicable, but no 
sooner than 28 days from the date of seroconversion, to confirm the diagnosis of primary CMV 
infection. The Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test may be conducted in one of the following ways: 
• 
At an unscheduled visit occurring ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion.  
• 
At the next planned study visit occurring ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion. 
The management of confirmatory testing for participants who seroconverted prior to the 
implementation of Protocol Amendment 5 will be as follows:  
• 
Where feasible, a suitable stored sample that was collected ≥28 days from the date of 
seroconversion will be utilized for the confirmatory test.  
• 
If no suitable stored sample exists, participants may be asked to give a new sample, 
either at an unscheduled visit or during their next scheduled study visit. 
Confirmatory CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test results starting with implementation of Protocol Amendment 5 will 
be managed as follows: 
• 
If the Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test is negative, the participant will revert to seronegative 
status and follow seronegative assessments. Specifically, the participant will resume 
the standard seronegative monitoring procedures, including serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing at 
scheduled study visits and the reporting of symptoms that meet criteria for possible 
primary CMV infection to the site.  
• 
If the Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test is positive, the participant will follow seropositive 
assessments. 
• 
If the Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test is indeterminate, a [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test will be repeated ≥2 weeks 
after the date of the indeterminate result. If the repeat Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test returns 
positive, the participant will be considered seroconverted and will follow seropositive 
assessments. If the repeat Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test returns negative, the participant will 
revert to seronegative status and follow seronegative assessments. An indeterminate 
repeat Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test will be handled on a case-by-case basis. 
Please refer to Table 23 for seropositive and seronegative assessments. 


--- Page 160 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 160 
11.9.6.6. Unscheduled Visits  
For CMV-seronegative participants who report symptoms meeting criteria for possible primary 
CMV infection between visits, their symptoms will be recorded, and they will be offered the 
opportunity to come in for an unscheduled visit to have serum drawn for seroconversion as well 
as symptom-directed physical exam and vital signs, as needed. CMV-seronegative participants 
who become pregnant will have the option to come in for CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing on a monthly basis 
during their pregnancy, if they choose. If a CMV-seronegative pregnant participant has a 
seroconversion due to primary CMV infection, as determined by a positive [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] result for serum 
for CMV primary infection, the participant will no longer have monthly serum collected for 
CMV serology ([INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]) at study visits, with the exception of Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing 
(Section 11.9.6.5), but will have urine collected for CMV PCR at subsequent visits every 3 
months. Pregnant CMV-seronegative participants will be informed if antibody testing 
demonstrates seroconversion due to primary CMV infection. In addition to informing the 
participant, the study site Investigator will inform the participant’s physician as soon as possible 
and every effort will be made to assure that the participant receives appropriate evaluation, 
counseling, and appropriate obstetric follow-up. 
For participants in the CMV-seroconverter cohort, urine will be collected for CMV PCR at an 
unscheduled visit. 
Either CMV-seropositive or CMV-seronegative participants may have an unscheduled visit for 
further assessment of safety events, as needed, such as an AE leading to discontinuation. 
CMV-seronegative participants who seroconvert may have an unscheduled visit for 
Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing as outlined in Section 11.9.6.5. 
11.9.6.7. Estimated Substudy Duration  
Each participant shall be enrolled for approximately 24 months in the Extension Substudy. 
11.9.6.8. Safety Assessments  
Planned timepoints for all safety assessments are provided in the SoA. All deaths, all AEs 
leading to study discontinuation, and all SAEs will be collected and reviewed from P301-EXT 
ICF signature through EoES. 
11.9.6.9. Pregnancy Outcome Assessments  
Participant-reported details of all pregnancies in female participants will be collected from 
P301-EXT ICF signature through EoES. Participant (maternal) records will be obtained where 
able to confirm all participant-reported outcomes. 
Pregnancy and pregnancy outcome data may be collected beyond EoES (ie, for pregnancies 
continuing beyond EoES visit). 
• 
If a pregnancy is reported, the Investigator should inform the Sponsor within 24 hours 
of learning of the pregnancy. 
• 
Abnormal pregnancy outcomes (eg, spontaneous abortion, fetal death, stillbirth, 
congenital anomalies, ectopic pregnancy) are considered SAEs. 


--- Page 161 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 161 
If the participant agrees to submit this information, the pregnancy must be followed to determine 
the outcome, including spontaneous or voluntary termination, details of the birth, and the 
presence or absence of any birth defects, congenital abnormalities, or maternal and/or newborn 
complications. This follow-up should occur even if intended duration of the safety follow-up for 
the study has ended. The Investigator must immediately (within 24 hours of awareness) report to 
the Sponsor any pregnancy resulting in an abnormal outcome according to the procedures 
described for SAEs. 
11.9.6.10. Infant Outcome Assessments  
Participant-reported details of outcomes among all infants born to participants in P301-EXT will 
be collected from signing of Substudy P301-EXT ICF through EoES. Infant records will be 
obtained where able to confirm all outcomes reported by the infant’s mother and to collect 
additional information up to 6 weeks post delivery. 
11.9.6.11. Immunogenicity Assessments  
Planned timepoints for all immunogenicity assessments are provided in the SoA. 
Serum for humoral immunogenicity will be collected for all participants and analyzed for all or a 
subset of participants as outlined in the SAP and/or a separate immunogenicity sampling plan. 
11.9.6.12. Efficacy Assessments  
Planned timepoints for all efficacy assessments are provided in the SoA. Serum for primary 
CMV infection ([INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]) is analyzed for the CMV-seronegative cohort only. Urine for CMV PCR is 
analyzed for the CMV-seroconverter cohort only (Section 11.9.6.3). 
If a blood sample for assessment of primary CMV infection returns a positive CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] result, 
Confirmatory CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing is required (Section 11.9.6.5). 
If a blood sample for assessment of primary CMV infection returns an indeterminate CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] 
result, a CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test will be repeated ≥2 weeks after the date of the indeterminate result to 
assess for an evolving antibody response to a primary CMV infection. If the repeat CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] 
test returns positive, Confirmatory [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] testing is required (Section 11.9.6.5). If the repeat CMV 
[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test returns negative, the participant will revert to seronegative status and follow 
seronegative assessments as outlined in Table 23. An indeterminate repeat CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test will be 
handled on a case-by-case basis. 
11.9.6.13. Safety Oversight  
Safety monitoring will be conducted by the Sponsor Medical Lead, Sponsor Pharmacovigilance 
Lead, and Contract Research Organization Medical Monitor. All deaths, all AEs leading to study 
discontinuation, and all SAEs will be reviewed on an ad hoc basis as the Sponsor is notified of 
the above outcomes. 
11.9.7. 
Concomitant Therapy  
At each study visit, the study site personnel should question the participant or participant’s 
parent(s)/legal guardian(s)/legally authorized representative regarding any medications taken and 
vaccinations received. 


--- Page 162 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc.

[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 162 
11.9.7.1. Recording of Concomitant Medications and Concomitant Vaccinations  
The following concomitant medication(s) and vaccine(s) must be recorded in the eCRF: 
• 
Any COVID-19 vaccine(s). 
• 
Any concomitant medications and vaccines listed in Section 11.9.7.2. 
• 
Any concomitant medications and vaccines relevant to an SAE or administered from 
the signing of the ICF through the EoES/the last study visit for the treatment of a 
SAE. 
11.9.7.2. Concomitant Medications and Vaccines that May Lead to the Elimination of a 
Participant from Per-protocol Analyses  
The use of the following concomitant medications and/or vaccines may determine a participant’s 
evaluability in the PP analysis. Analysis sets are described in Section 11.9.8.2 and Table 21. 
• 
Any investigational or nonregistered product (drug or vaccine) other than the study 
injection used during the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Study Period. 
• 
Immunosuppressants or other immune-modifying drugs administered chronically 
(ie, more than 14 days in total) during the Study Period. For corticosteroids, this 
includes prednisone >5 mg/day or the equivalent. Inhaled, nasal, and topical steroids 
are allowed. Stable immunomodulator regimens used for managing environmental 
allergies are allowed. 
• 
Long-acting immune-modifying drugs administered at any time during the Study 
Period (eg, infliximab). 
• 
Immunoglobulins and/or any blood products administered during the Study Period. 
• 
Antiviral with activity against CMV (ganciclovir, valganciclovir, foscarnet, cidofovir, 
letermovir, acyclovir, valacyclovir) administered during the course of the study. 
11.9.8. 
Statistical Considerations  
11.9.8.1. Statistical Hypotheses  
There is no formal statistical hypothesis testing in this study. Descriptive analyses of the 
immunogenicity, efficacy, and safety data will be performed. 
11.9.8.2. Analyses Sets  
This study is an Extension Substudy of [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study. In general, an analysis set 
in Study P301-EXT will be defined as participants who are enrolled in Substudy P301-EXT and 
are in the respective analysis set in the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study. Detailed definitions of the 
analysis sets are provided in Table 21.

11.9.8.3. Interim Analyses  
No interim analyses are currently planned. 
11.9.8.4. Final Analyses  
A final analysis of all data collected throughout Substudy P301-EXT from ICF signature through 
EoES will be conducted after the full database is cleaned and locked. Results of this analysis will 
be presented in a final Clinical Study Report, including individual listings. 
11.9.8.5. Power and Sample Size Determination  
This study is an Extension Substudy for [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study. Approximately 
6,900 total participants (5,500 CMV-seronegative and 1,400 CMV-seropositive) are planned to 
be enrolled in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study. Table 22 shows the expected number of 
participants eligible to be enrolled in the Extension Substudy, assuming either 20% or 25% of the 
participants in each CMV serostatus group in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study are ineligible for 
Substudy P301-EXT (did not complete the final study visit in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study, did 
not receive all 3 study injections within window per-protocol [CMV-seropositive participants], 
or did not otherwise meet the eligibility criteria for Substudy P301-EXT). All eligible and 
consenting CMV-seronegative participants can enroll in the Extension Substudy. The exact 
sample size of CMV-seronegative participants for Substudy P301-EXT will depend on both the 
number of participants eligible and among those the number of participants who consent to 
participate in this Extension Substudy. Approximately 360 eligible and consenting 
CMV-seropositive participants will be enrolled in Substudy P301-EXT; this sample size is 
considered sufficient to provide a descriptive summary of the longer-term immunogenicity and 
safety of [AMENDMENT_A101] in CMV-seropositive participants.

11.9.8.6. Immunogenicity Analyses  
Antibody-mediated immunogenicity endpoints include nAb against epithelial cell infection, nAb 
against fibroblast infection, gB-specific bAb, and pentamer-specific bAb. 
Immunogenicity analyses will be based on the PP Set for Immunogenicity and will be presented 
by CMV serostatus (CMV-seronegative and CMV-seropositive) and treatment group in 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study, unless otherwise specified. Supportive analyses of 
immunogenicity data may be conducted using the Immunogenicity Subset. 
Geometric mean of specific antibody titers or concentrations with corresponding 2-sided 95% CI 
at each timepoint assessed and GMFR of specific antibody titers or concentrations with 
corresponding 2-sided 95% CI at each postbaseline timepoint assessed over preinjection baseline 
at Day 1 in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study will be provided by CMV serostatus and treatment 
group. The 95% CIs will be calculated based on the t-distribution of the log-transformed values 
and then back-transformed to the original scale. Descriptive summary statistics including the 
number of participants (n), median, minimum, and maximum will also be provided at each 
timepoint assessed. 
The number and percentage of participants with ≥2-fold, ≥3-fold, and ≥4-fold increases in each 
of the nAb and bAb titers or concentrations from preinjection baseline at Day 1 in the 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study will be provided with 2-sided 95% CI using the Clopper-Pearson 
method at each postbaseline timepoint assessed. 
11.9.8.7. Efficacy Analyses  
11.9.8.7.1. Analyses of Long-Term Vaccine Efficacy  
The 2 Extension Substudy primary efficacy endpoints for assessing VE are CMV seroconversion 
and systemic viral dissemination in participants who meet the endpoint of CMV seroconversion.  
For the primary efficacy endpoint of CMV seroconversion, an endpoint case is defined as 
seroconversion from a negative to a positive result for serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] against at least one of the 
4 recombinant CMV antigens not encoded by [AMENDMENT_A101] (pp150, pp28, pp52, and pp38) as 
measured by a platform-based automated immunoassay and confirmed by a repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test 
performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion, assessed throughout Substudy P301-EXT 
from ICF signature through EoES. 
For the primary efficacy endpoint of systemic viral dissemination in participants who meet the 
endpoint of CMV seroconversion, an endpoint case is defined as: 
• seroconversion from a negative to a positive result for serum [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] as measured by a 
platform-based automated immunoassay based on at least 1 of the 4 recombinant CMV 
antigens not encoded by [AMENDMENT_A101] (pp150, pp28, pp52, pp38) and confirmed by a 
repeat [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] test performed ≥28 days from the date of seroconversion, AND  
• positive CMV PCR results in both blood and urine (on the same date or on different 
dates) or in urine (on ≥2 different dates) on or after the date of seroconversion, 
assessed throughout Substudy P301-EXT from ICF signature through EoES. 


--- Page 166 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 166 
For both primary efficacy endpoints, analyses of VE will be based on the PP Set for Efficacy. 
Supportive analyses based on the mITT Set will also be performed. 
The number of subjects with an endpoint case (ie, first occurrence of CMV seroconversion), 
person-time, incidence rate, and 2-sided 95% CI for incidence rate will be provided for each 
treatment group in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study and by time period in Substudy P301-EXT. 
Incidence rate will be calculated as the number of subjects with the case divided by the number 
of subjects at risk adjusted by person-time (years). Person-time will be calculated as the duration 
from ICF signature to the first occurrence of CMV seroconversion, the end of the time period, 
study completion, discontinuation from the study, death, or data cutoff date in Substudy 
P301-EXT, whichever is the earliest. The 2-sided 95% CI will be calculated using the exact 
method (Poisson distribution) and adjusted by person-time. Time periods of interest are from ICF 
signature to Month 36, Month 42, Month 48, and Month 54 in Substudy P301-EXT. 
VE is defined as the percent reduction in the incidence of the endpoint ([AMENDMENT_A101] vs. placebo, 
as defined by the treatment groups in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study). VE will be estimated by 
one minus the ratio of incidence rate of CMV seroconversion ([AMENDMENT_A101] vs. placebo) 
adjusting for person-time, and the 2-sided 95% CI of VE will be calculated using the exact 
method conditional upon the total number of cases, adjusting for person-time. VE estimate will 
be provided by time period in Substudy [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301-EXT. 
11.9.8.7.2. Secondary Efficacy Analyses in Cytomegalovirus-Seronegative Participants 
Meeting the Endpoint of Seroconversion Due to Primary CMV Infection  
The secondary efficacy analyses to evaluate the efficacy of [AMENDMENT_A101] to reduce the frequency 
of urinary CMV shedding in CMV-seronegative participants meeting the endpoint of 
seroconversion will be performed using methods similar to those for this secondary efficacy 
endpoint in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study as described in Section 9.5.5.2. CMV-seronegative 
participants who seroconverted in both [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study and the Extension 
Substudy are eligible for these analyses, and all available post-seroconversion urine CMV PCR 
data will be included. 
Further details will be described in the SAP. 
11.9.8.8. Safety Analyses  
All safety analyses will be based on the Safety Set and will be provided by CMV serostatus 
(CMV-seronegative and CMV-seropositive) and treatment group in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main 
study, unless otherwise specified. Participants will be included in the treatment group 
corresponding to the actual treatment received in [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 main study. 
Safety will be assessed by clinical review of all relevant parameters, including deaths, AEs 
leading to discontinuation from study participation, SAEs, vital signs, and physical examination 
findings throughout Substudy [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301-EXT from ICF signature through EoES. 
The number and percentage of participants with deaths, AEs leading to discontinuation from 
study participation, and SAEs will be summarized. AEs will be coded according to the MedDRA 
and presented by MedDRA system organ class and preferred term. 
For all other safety parameters, descriptive summary statistics will be provided.

11.10. 
APPENDIX 10: Country-specific Requirements  
11.10.1. 
Country-specific Requirements for Japan  
11.10.1.1. Section 11.8. Appendix 8: Contraceptive Guidance  
Based on Section 11.8 and on the approval status of contraception measures in Japan, the 
following contraceptive methods are acceptable and available for use in participants treated in 
this study in Japan:  
• 
Barrier contraceptives (male condoms only) 
• 
Hormonal contraceptives 
• 
Intrauterine device 
• 
Intrauterine hormone-releasing system 
• 
Vasectomy, Bilateral tubal ligation 
11.10.1.2. Section 11.2.14. Source Documents  
Additional explanation of source documents that should be provided to the CMV Adjudication 
Committee as mentioned in Section 11.2.14 were clarified (Administrative Change Letter to 
Protocol Amendment 3 for Japan) per the bullets below to address the specific requirements 
identified at sites involved in this study in Japan: 
• 
Discharge summary and/or Emergency Department Notes where applicable 
• 
Admission history and physical where applicable 
• 
Other relevant source documents or clinical information as applicable (eg, clinic notes 
for participant who are not admitted, analgesics, antibiotics or antivirals prescribed, 
etc.) 
• 
Virological Panel/Assays (including urine CMV PCR, serological EBV testing, HIV 
testing) 
• 
COVID-19 PCR testing if performed at discretion of site Investigator 
• 
Laboratory reports (complete blood count with differential and comprehensive 
metabolic panel with liver function tests) with units and reference ranges 
11.11. 
APPENDIX 11: Changes Related to Mitigation of Study Disruptions 
Due to Cases of Civil Crisis, Natural Disaster, or Public Health Crisis  
Note: These changes should only be implemented if allowable by local/regional guidelines and 
following written agreement from or notification by the Sponsor. Changes below should be 
implemented only during study disruptions due to any of or a combination of civil crisis, natural 
disaster, or public health crisis (eg, during quarantines and resulting site closures, or regional 
travel restrictions) during which participants may not wish to or may be unable to visit the study 
site for study visits. 


--- Page 173 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 173 
Reconsent of Study Participants During Study Interruptions  
During study interruptions, it may not be possible for the participants to complete study visits 
and assessments on site and alternative means for carrying out the visits and assessments may be 
necessary (eg, remote/decentralized visits). Reconsent should be obtained for the alternative 
means of carrying out visits and assessments and should be obtained prior to performing the 
procedures described in Section 11.1, Section 11.6.6, and Section 11.9.10. Local and regional 
regulations and/or guidelines regarding reconsent of study participants should be checked and 
followed. Reconsent may be verbal if allowed by local/regional guidelines (Note: in the case of 
verbal reconsent, the ICF should be signed at the participant’s next contact with the study site). 
Visiting the study sites for the sole purpose of obtaining reconsent should be avoided.  
Rescreening of Participants to Reconfirm Study Eligibility  
Additional rescreening for screen failure due to study disruption can be performed in previously 
screened participants. The Investigator should confirm this with the designated study clinical 
lead. 
In addition, during study disruption there may be a delay between confirming eligibility of a 
participant and either enrolment/randomization into the study or commencing of dosing with 
study intervention. If this delay is outside the screening window specified in Section 11.1 and 
Section 11.9.10, the participant will need to be rescreened to reconfirm eligibility before 
commencing study procedures. This will provide another opportunity to rescreen a participant in 
addition to that detailed in Section 5.3. The procedures detailed in Section 11.1 and 
Section 11.9.10 must be undertaken to confirm eligibility using the same randomization number 
as for the participant. 
Telemedicine Visit to Replace On-site Visit (Where Applicable) 
In this appendix the term “telemedicine visit” refers to remote contact with the participants using 
telecommunications technology including phone calls, virtual or video visits, and mobile health 
devices. 
During a civil crisis, natural disaster, or public health crisis, on-site visits may be replaced by a 
telemedicine visit if allowed by local/regional guidelines. Having a telemedicine visit with the 
participants will allow AEs, concomitant medication(s), and other applicable study data to be 
reported and documented. 
Data Capture During Telemedicine Visits 
Data collected during telemedicine visits will be captured by the qualified health care 
professional from the study site in the source documents, or by the participant themselves. 


--- Page 174 ---

[SPONSOR_A]TX, Inc. 
[AMENDMENT_A101] 
[AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 Protocol Amendment 7 
Confidential 
Page 174 
11.12. 
APPENDIX 12: Protocol Amendment History  
11.12.1. 
Amendment 1, 23 Aug 2021  
Main Rationale for the Amendment: 
The purpose of this amendment is to restrict enrollment to female participants, revise eligibility 
and concomitant medication criteria to re-define the interval between coronavirus disease 2019 
(COVID-19) vaccination and study injections, and describe the observation of myocarditis and 
pericarditis following COVID-19 vaccines. 
The summary of changes table provided here describes the changes made in Amendment 1 
relative to the original protocol, including the sections modified and the corresponding 
rationales. The synopsis of Amendment 1 has been modified to correspond to changes in the 
body of the protocol. Minor editorial and grammatical corrections were also made which are not 
included in the SOC.

11.12.1.1. Amendment 1/BEL 1 (Belgium Country-Specific Requirements), 04 Feb 2022  
Country-specific requirements for Belgium are as follows. 
CMV-seropositive participants will be enrolled in Belgium after the planned DSMB review of 
the first 600 participants enrolled in the overall study and the DSMB has recommended 
continuation of the study (See Section 4.1, Section 5, and Section 5.1). 
In addition to the re-screening procedures provided in Section 5.3, if re-screening is required for 
a CMV-seropositive participant (participant who has had result of CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-positive and CMV 
IgM-negative, or CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]-positive and CMV IgM-positive in laboratory samples obtained 
during the initial study Screening Visit), the CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] and IgM testing is not required to be 
repeated. If re-screening is required for a previously CMV-seronegative participant, the CMV 
[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] and IgM testing is required. 
To address the omission in the SoA – Follow-up Phase, the assessment “Recording of AESIs” 
row was added with collection at every visit, to incorporate the previous administrative change 
letter to Protocol Amendment 1 (See Table 9).

11.12.3. 
Amendment 3, 15 Jun 2023  
Main Rationale for the Amendment: 
At the time of preparing Protocol Amendment 2, it was anticipated that by the time enrollment in 
Japan started, enrollment outside Japan would have been completed. Therefore, approximately 
400 participants in Japan were added beyond the originally planned total sample size to ensure 
an adequate number of participants would be enrolled in Japan. Since Protocol Amendment 2 
became effective, enrollment in Japan started earlier than anticipated and overall enrollment 
outside Japan was slower than anticipated. As a result, in Protocol Amendment 3, the sample size 
is reduced back to the originally planned total of approximately 6,900 female participants 
(5,500 CMV-seronegative participants and 1,400 CMV-seropositive participants), including at 
least 400 participants in Japan. The sample size update occurred prior to the first planned 
analysis without unblinding the study; therefore, no adjustment to the alpha levels of the planned 
analyses is needed. Minor editorial and grammatical corrections were also made. 
Summary of Major Changes from Protocol Amendment 2 to Protocol Amendment 3:

Section 2.3.2 Risks from Study 
Participation and Their 
Mitigation 
Updated: 
There have been very rare (<1 in 
10,000 recipients) reports of 
myocarditis and pericarditis 
occurring after vaccination with 
coronavirus disease 2019 
(COVID-19) mRNA vaccines. The 
majority of the cases have been 
reported in young males, within 7 
to 14 days shortly after the second 
dose of the vaccine. These are 
typically mild cases and 
individuals tend to recover within 
a short time following standard 
treatment (including rest, 
NSAIDs, and/or colchicine). and 
rest Healthcare professionals and 
study participants should be 
alert to the signs and symptoms 
of myocarditis and pericarditis 
(Gargano et al 2021). It is not 
known whether the risk of 
myocarditis or pericarditis is 
increased following additional 
doses of other non-COVID 
mRNA vaccines (Gargano et al 
2021). Investigators and 
participants should be alert to the 
signs and symptoms of 
myocarditis and pericarditis. 
To align with [SPONSOR_A] 
position on clinical 
management and CEAC 
review of myocarditis, 
pericarditis, and/or 
myopericarditis.

Committee

To align with [SPONSOR_A] 
position on clinical 
management and CEAC 
review of myocarditis, 
pericarditis, and/or 
myopericarditis.

Section 11.6.6 Study 
Assessments and Procedures 
(Infant Outcome Substudy) 
Added: 
Newborn sampling of urine and 
saliva for CMV PCR using a 
research-use only assay on 
1 occasion within 3 weeks after 
delivery. These samples may be 
collected either at the birth facility 
or in the study clinic, as 
appropriate (see Figure 3). Saliva 
samples testing positive for CMV 
by PCR will have follow-up urine 
sampling for CMV PCR testing. 
Newborn urine samples will be 
collected using a urine bag if 
performed at the study clinic. 
Saliva samples will be collected at 
least 90 minutes after the last 
breastfeeding using an oral swab. 
The Principal Investigator will 
immediately refer the participant 
and her infant to the participant’s 
pediatrician and inform the 
participant’s obstetrician of any 
infant urine or saliva sample 
returns a positive CMV PCR 
result. Any such positive CMV 
PCR results from the newborn 
urine or saliva should be 
confirmed outside of the study 
by their clinician with a CMV 
PCR assay which has been 
approved by a local regulatory 
body during their clinical 
evaluation. 
Added language to clarify 
that the urine and saliva 
CMV PCR assays are for 
research-use-only assay and 
therefore all positive tests 
should be confirmed with a 
clinical PCR test approved 
by the local regulatory body.

11.12.4. 
Amendment 4, 28 Nov 2023  
Main Rationale for the Amendment: 
This amendment is substantial. The main rationale for the amendment is to add an Extension 
Substudy to extend the observation period of the study. The purpose of the Extension Substudy is 
to assess the longer-term immunogenicity, safety, and VE against primary CMV infection in 
healthy CMV-seronegative participants from the conclusion (Month 30) of the [AMENDMENT_A101]-
P301 main study for an additional 2 years for females 16 to 40 years of age and to evaluate the 
immune persistence and safety of [AMENDMENT_A101] vaccination at the 100-µg dose level in a subset 
of (approximately 360) CMV-seropositive females who complete the [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301 study. 
This will provide a total of approximately 4 years of immunogenicity, efficacy, and safety data 
postfinal injection in the P301 study.

11.12.5. 
Amendment 5, 29 Apr 2024  
Main Rationale for the Amendment: 
This amendment is substantial. The main rationale for the amendment is to implement 
confirmatory CMV [INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A] antibody testing to verify the diagnosis of seroconversion due to primary 
CMV infection. The summary of changes table outlines the revisions made in Amendment 5 
relative to Amendment 4, including the modified sections and the corresponding rationales for 
each description. Minor editorial or formatting changes are not included in the summary of 
changes table.

11.12.5.1. [AMENDMENT_A101]-P301-Protocol Amendment 5-JPN-1, 14 Aug 2024  
Main Rationale for the Amendment: 
The main rationale for the amendment is to include country-specific contraception method 
requirements for participants in Japan. Additionally, a summary of the source documents that 
should be provided to the CMV Adjudication Committee that were previously conveyed in an 
administrative change letter to Protocol Amendment 3 for Japan were included directly in the 
Japan country-specific appendix for clarity. The summary of changes table outlines the revisions 
made in Amendment 5-JPN-1 relative to Amendment 5, including the modified sections and the 
corresponding rationales for each description. Minor editorial or formatting changes are not 
included in the summary of changes table.

11.12.6. 
Amendment 6, 11 Dec 2024  
This amendment is substantial. The following are the main rationales for the amendment: 
• 
Change the timing of the second inferential analysis of efficacy (Final Analysis). 
Specifically, to de-couple it from the completion of the main study. In the situation 
where vaccine efficacy is not demonstrated at the Primary Analysis, the null 
hypothesis of vaccine efficacy for the primary efficacy endpoint will be tested at the 
Final Analysis when at least 112 cases of the primary efficacy endpoint (ie, primary 
CMV infection) have been observed across the 2 groups ([AMENDMENT_A101] or placebo) in 
the PP Set for Efficacy. 
• 
Change the End-of-Study Analysis from an inferential analysis of efficacy to a 
supportive analysis.

Add country-specific requirements for Japan that were written into a Japan-specific 
version of Amendment 5.

Section # and Name 
Description of Change 
Brief Rationale 
Section 9.2. Statistical 
Hypotheses; Section 9.3.1. 
Power and Sample Size for 
the Cytomegalovirus-
seronegative Cohort; Section 
9.5. Statistical Analyses; 
Section 9.6. Planned 
Analyses 
The second inferential analysis of 
efficacy was changed from the 
End-of-Study Analysis to a Final 
Analysis that will be carried out 
when at least a total of 112 cases of 
the primary efficacy endpoint have 
been observed across the 2 groups 
in the PP Set for Efficacy, without 
separately requiring reaching the 
end of the main study. The 
End-of-Study Analysis was 
changed from an inferential 
analysis of efficacy to a supportive 
analysis.  
The enrollment of this study was 
slower than initially anticipated. 
In the event that VE is not 
demonstrated at the Primary 
Analysis, changing the timing of 
the second inferential analysis of 
efficacy to be tr[INVESTIGATIONAL_PRODUCT_A]ered by the 
accrual of a prespecified number 
of primary efficacy endpoint 
cases alone will enable the 
Sponsor to potentially have an 
earlier second inferential analysis 
of efficacy, without 
compromising statistical rigor. 
The overall Type I error rate for 
this study remains strictly 
controlled at 2.5% (one-sided) 
with 0.5% allocated to the 
Primary Analysis and 2.0% 
allocated to the Final Analysis.
